Superiority of Adhan vs. Imamah
Dispute among scholars on whether adhan or imamah is superior.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the virtue of adhan and imamah, cite the proofs for each, and explain why Ibn al-Humam chose imamah as superior.

Core Idea
Imamah is more virtuous because the Prophet and caliphs were imams, not mu'adhdhins.

This lesson examines a well-known inter-madhhab dispute: which is more virtuous, giving the call to prayer (adhan) or leading the prayer (imamah)? The passage from Bahr al-Raiq presents three views, with the Hanafi authority Ibn al-Humam preferring imamah. We will analyze the evidence and understand the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
The passage mentions three views: adhan is better, imamah is better, and they are equal. Note that Ibn al-Humam chose imamah.
2
Examine the proof for adhan
The verse (41:33) praising those who invite to Allah, interpreted by Aisha as referring to mu'adhdhins, and the hadith about long necks on the Day of Resurrection.
3
Examine the proof for imamah
The practice of the Prophet and the caliphs, who were imams and not mu'adhdhins, and they only choose the best of matters.
4
Understand the Hanafi tarjih
Ibn al-Humam's reliance on the practice of the Prophet indicates that imamah is superior; this is the preferred Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف هل الأذان أفضل أم الإمامة قيل بالأول للآية «ومن أحسن قولا ممن دعا إلى الله» فسرته عائشة بالمؤذنين، وللحديث «المؤذنون أطول أعناقاً يوم القيامة». واختلف في معناه على أقوال... وقيل الإمامة أفضل لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والخلفاء من بعده كانوا أئمة ولم يكونوا مؤذنين وهم لا يختارون من الأمور إلا أفضلها وقيل هما سواء. واختار المحقق ابن الهمام أنها أفضل لما ذكرناه
And they differed: is adhan better or imamah? It was said the former due to the verse 'And who is better in speech than one who invites to Allah' which Aisha interpreted as the mu'adhdhins, and due to the hadith 'The mu'adhdhins will have the longest necks on the Day of Resurrection'. And they differed in its meaning... And it was said imamah is better because the Prophet, peace be upon him, and the caliphs after him were imams and were not mu'adhdhins, and they only choose the best of matters. And it was said they are equal. And al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam chose that imamah is better based on what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage presents the scholarly dispute on whether adhan or imamah is more virtuous. Evidence for adhan includes the verse from Surah Fussilat (41:33) interpreted as referring to mu'adhdhins, and the hadith about long necks on the Day of Resurrection. Evidence for imamah includes the practice of the Prophet and the rightly-guided caliphs who served as imams but not as mu'adhdhins. The author, Ibn al-Humam (a Hanafi scholar), chose imamah as superior. This is a classic inter-madhhab discussion, but also relevant within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الأذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer
الإمامة (al-imamah): Leading the congregational prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-Humam, which is considered more virtuous?
A) Adhan
B) Imamah
C) Both are equal
D) Neither is virtuous

Key Takeaway
Imamah is more virtuous than adhan according to the chosen Hanafi view of Ibn al-Humam.

Legal Status of Adhan: Wajib or Sunnah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on legal weight of adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi ruling on adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah kifayah, not wajib, and identify the intra-Hanafi arguments and their resolution.

Core Idea
Adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib — even though some Hanafi imams spoke of fighting those who abandon it.

The adhan is a prominent symbol of Islam, but what is its legal weight? Hanafi scholars debated whether it is wajib (obligatory) or sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah). This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the relied-upon position, showing how the Hanafi school distinguishes between emphasis and obligation. By analyzing the arguments of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, you will understand the delicate balance between textual evidence and legal principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal classification debate
Recognize that the passage focuses on whether adhan is wajib or sunnah mu'akkadah. Note the author's phrase 'sun for the obligatory prayers' sets the baseline.
The debate is intra-Hanafi: all agree on the act's importance, but disagree on its legal binding.
2
Extract the positions of the Hanafi imams
Note Muhammad's view: if a town abandons adhan, they are fought. Abu Yusuf says they are imprisoned and beaten. Abu Hanifa (via Miraj al-Dirayah) says those who skip it have 'violated the sunnah and sinned'.
These severe consequences might suggest wajib, but the author argues they indicate emphasis only.
3
Analyze the author's rebuttal
The author distinguishes between continuous practice without exception and the absence of objection to those who omit it. He also notes that sin (ithm) is common to both wajib and sunnah mu'akkadah.
This is a classic usul argument: punishment alone does not prove wujub.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if adhan were wajib, missing it would require qada (make-up) or expiation; as sunnah mu'akkadah, it is strongly recommended but no qada, though leaving it is sinful.
This distinction affects fatwa and practice.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is sunnah mu'akkadah kifayah. This is supported by the majority of later scholars and is the basis for fatwa.
Even though some early imams used harsh language, the principle that 'continuous practice without objection indicates sunnah' prevails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (سن للفرائض) أي سن الأذان للصلوات الخمس والجمعة سنة مؤكدة قوية قريبة من الواجب حتى أطلق بعضهم عليه الوجوب، ولهذا قال محمد لو اجتمع أهل بلد على تكره قاتلناهم عليه وعند أبي يوسف يحبسون ويضربون وهو يدل على تأكده لا على وجوبه... واستشهد على ذلك بما في معراج الدراية عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف صلوا في الحضر الظهر أو العصر بلا أذان ولا إقامة أخطأوا السنة وأثموا .اهـ. والجواب أن المواظبة المقرونة بعدم الترك مرة لما اقترنت بعدم الإنكار على من لم يفعله كانت دليل السنية لا الوجوب... والاستشهاد بالإثم على تركه لا يدل على الوجوب عندنا لأنه مشترك بين الواجب والسنة المؤكدة
His saying 'Sunnah for the obligatory prayers' means the adhan for the five prayers and Jumu'ah is a strong confirmed sunnah close to wajib, such that some considered it obligatory. For this, Muhammad said: If the people of a town unanimously abandon it, we would fight them. According to Abu Yusuf, they are imprisoned and beaten. This indicates its emphasis, not its obligation... And he cited as evidence what is in Miraj al-Dirayah from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: If they prayed in the city Dhuhr or Asr without adhan and iqamah, they violated the sunnah and sinned. The response is that continuous practice without ever leaving it, since it is accompanied by not objecting to those who leave it, is evidence of sunnah, not obligation... And citing sin for leaving it does not prove obligation according to us, because sin is common between wajib and sunnah mu'akkadah.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage deals with the legal classification of adhan. The commentator explains that the author's phrase 'sunnah for the obligatory prayers' indicates that adhan is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) close to wajib, to the extent that some scholars called it wajib. Imam Muhammad said that if an entire town abandons it, the authorities should fight them, while Abu Yusuf said they should be imprisoned and beaten. However, the author argues that this shows emphasis, not obligation. The evidence from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that praying without adhan makes them sin is refuted by noting that sin applies to abandoning confirmed sunnahs as well. The correct view is that adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah kifayah. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute over the legal weight of adhan.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah, strongly recommended, but not obligatory

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, adhan is classified as:
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah kifayah
C) Fard 'ayn
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Adhan is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah kifayah) in the Hanafi school, not wajib, because continuous practice without objection indicates sunnah, not obligation, and sin is common to both categories.

The Legal Status of Adhan: Sunnah Mu'akkadah or Wajib?
Dispute over whether adhan is wajib or sunnah mu'akkadah, with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the legal status of adhan and explain why the evidence for sunnah mu'akkadah outweighs the argument for wajib.

Core Idea
Adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, because sin attaches to both, but the proof lacks decisive obligation.

The call to prayer (adhan) is one of the most visible symbols of Islam. While many assume it is obligatory to call, the Hanafi school classifies it as a strongly emphasized sunnah. This lesson examines the evidence that leads to this conclusion, including the views of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on collective abandonment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling in the Matn
The base text (matn) states adhan is sunnah for the obligatory prayers. Recognize that the author begins with the term 'sunnah', not 'wajib'.
The choice of wording is significant in Hanafi usul.
2
Locate the Proofs for Obligation
The proponent of obligation cites the statement from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: 'If they prayed without adhan and iqamah, they erred regarding the sunnah and sinned.' This proof is found in Mi'raj al-Diraya.
The phrase 'they sinned' is used to argue that abandonment is sinful, hence wajib.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response is that sin is not exclusive to wajib; it also applies to abandoning sunnah mu'akkadah. Thus, the occurrence of sin does not imply obligation.
This is a key methodological point: sin is a shared consequence.
4
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Imam Muhammad ruled that if a town collectively abandons adhan, they should be fought. Abu Yusuf said they should be imprisoned and beaten. This shows the extreme emphasis but not obligation, because such punishments are for refusal to uphold the symbol, not for missing a wajib act.
The punishment is for lowering the symbols of Islam, not for omitting a fard.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah on the individual level, but a communal obligation (fard kifayah) in the sense that the town must maintain it as a symbol.
This reconciles the harsh punishment with the absence of personal obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (سن للفرائض) أي سن الأذان للصلوات الخمس والجمعة سنة مؤكدة قوية قريبة من الواجب حتى أطلق بعضهم عليه الوجوب، ولهذا قال محمد لو اجتمع أهل بلد على تكره قاتلناهم عليه وعند أبي يوسف يحبسون ويضربون وهو يدل على تأكده لا على وجوبه الاجتماع على تركه من استخفافهم بالدين بخفض أعلامه لأن الأذان من أعلام الدين كذلك واختار في فتح القدير وجوبه لأن عدم الترك مرة دليل الوجوب ولا يظهر كونه على الكفاية وإلا لم يأثم أهل بلدة بالاجتماع على تركه إذا قام به غيرهم ولم يضربوا ولم يحبسوا، واستشهد على ذلك بما في معراج الدراية عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف صلوا في الحضر الظهر أو العصر بلا أذان ولا إقامة أخطأوا السنة وأثموا .اهـ. والجواب أن المواظبة المقرونة بعدم الترك مرة لما اقترنت بعدم الإنكار على من لم يفعله كانت دليل السنية لا الوجوب كما صرح به في فتح القدير في باب الاعتكاف والظاهر كونه على الكفاية بمعنى أنه إذا فعل في بلد سقطت المقاتلة عن أهلها لا بمعنى أنه إذا أذن واحد في بلد سقط عن سائر الناس من غير أهل تلك البلدة إذ لم يحصل به إظهار أعلام الدين، ولو لم يكن على الكفاية بهذا المعنى لكان سنة في حق كل أحد وليس كذلك إذا أذان الحي يكفينا كما سيأتي والاستشهاد بالإثم على تركه لا يدل على الوجوب عندنا لأنه مشترك بين الواجب والسنة المؤكدة، ولهذا كان الصحيح أنه يأثم إذا ترك سنن الصلوات المؤكدة كما سيأتي في باب الخلاف، ولا يخفى أن لا تنافي بين الكلامين بوجه فإن المقاتلة إنما تكون عند الامتناع وعدم القهر لهم والضرب والحبس إنما يكون عند قهرهم فجاز أن يقاتلوا إذا امتنعوا عن قبول الأمر بالأذان ولم يسلموا أنفسهم، فإذا قوتلوا فظهر عليهم ضربوا وحبسوا .اهـ. قوله (والجواب الخ) أقول : المفهوم من كلام الفتح السابق أنه واجب على أهل كل بلدة بحيث لو تركوه أثموا إلا أنه واجب على كل واحد منهم، وحينئذ فالجواب المذكور إنما يصح لو ثبت عدم الإنكار على أهل بلدة تركوه لا على واحد بعينه إذ لا يلزم من جواز تركه لواحد من أهل بلدة جواز تركه الجميع أهل البلدة تأمل . قوله : (وليس كذلك قال في النهر : ولم أو حكم البلدة الواحدة إذا اتسعت أطرافها كمصر، والظاهر أن أهل كل محلة سمعوا الأذان ولو من محلة أخرى يسقط عنهم لا إن لم يسمعوا قوله : (والاستشهاد بالإثم الخ) قال في النهر المذكور في الولوالجية عن محمد وكذلك في سائر السنن وبهذا يبطل الاستدلال على الوجوب . قوله : ( ولعل الإثم الخ) لم يجزم بذلك هنا لكن سيجزم به في سنن الصلاة النوافل إن شاء الله تعالى. ولعل الإثم مقول بالتشكيك بعضه أقوى من بعض ولهذا صرح في الرواية بالسنية حيث قال : أخطأوا السنة. وفي غاية البيان والمحيط: والقولان متقاربان لأن السنة المؤكدة في معنى الواجب في حق لحوق الإثم لتاركهما .اهـ.
His saying: (Sunnah for the obligatory prayers) meaning the adhan for the five prayers and Jumu'ah is a strongly emphasized sunnah close to obligatory, such that some have called it obligatory. Hence Muhammad said: 'If the people of a town agree to abandon it, we would fight them.' According to Abu Yusuf, they are imprisoned and beaten. This indicates its emphasis, not its obligation, because agreement on abandoning it is a sign of their disdain for religion by lowering its symbols, since adhan is among the symbols of religion. Al-Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir chose its obligation because the fact that it was never omitted once is evidence of obligation, and it does not appear to be a communal obligation because if it were, the people of a town would not sin by collectively abandoning it if someone else performed it, nor would they be beaten or imprisoned. He cited as evidence what is in Mi'raj al-Diraya from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: 'If they prayed Zuhr or 'Asr in the settled area without adhan and iqamah, they erred regarding the sunnah and sinned.' The answer is that consistency coupled with never missing it, since it is coupled with no disapproval of one who does not do it, is evidence of sunnah, not obligation, as stated in Fath al-Qadir in the chapter on i'tikaf. Apparently it is a communal obligation in the sense that if it is performed in a town, fighting is lifted from its people, not in the sense that if one person calls the adhan in a town, it is no longer required from others outside that town, because then the display of the symbols of religion is not achieved. If it were not a communal obligation in this sense, it would be sunnah for every individual, but that is not the case since the adhan of the neighborhood suffices us as will come. The citation of sin for abandoning it does not indicate obligation in our school because sin is common between obligatory and emphasized sunnah. Hence the correct view is that one sins if he abandons the emphasized sunnahs of the prayers as will come in the chapter on conflict. And it is not hidden that there is no contradiction between the two statements at all, because fighting only occurs when they refuse and are not overpowered, while beating and imprisonment occur when they are overpowered. So it is permissible to fight them if they refuse to accept the command of adhan and do not surrender. Then when they are fought and overcome, they are beaten and imprisoned. His saying: (And the answer etc.) I say: The understanding from Fath al-Qadir's previous words is that it is obligatory upon the people of every town such that if they abandon it they sin, but it is an obligation upon each one of them. Then the aforementioned answer is only valid if there is proven no disapproval upon the people of a town who abandon it, not upon a specific individual, because permissibility of its abandonment by one person from the people of the town does not necessitate permissibility of its abandonment by all the people of the town. Contemplate. His saying: (And it is not like that) He said in al-Nahr: I did not find the ruling of one town when its outskirts are extensive like a metropolis. Apparently the people of each quarter who hear the adhan from another quarter, it is dropped from them; if they do not hear, it is not. His saying: (And the citation of sin etc.) He said in al-Nahr from al-Walwaljiyya from Muhammad: And likewise in the other sunnahs. By this the inference for obligation is invalidated. His saying: (And perhaps the sin etc.) He did not assert that here, but he will assert it in the sunnahs of prayer, nawafil insha'Allah. And perhaps sin is said by gradation, some stronger than others. Hence he explicitly stated in the transmission that it is sunnah: 'They erred regarding the sunnah.' In Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Muhit: The two statements are close because the emphasized sunnah is in the meaning of obligatory with regard to sin attaching to its abandoner.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal status of the call to prayer (adhan). The commentator explains that the matn states it is sunnah, but there is a strong debate within the Hanafi school. Some, like the author of Fath al-Qadir, consider it wajib, while the relied-upon position is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah. The discussion includes the views of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding punishment for abandoning adhan collectively. Imam Muhammad said the people of a town should be fought if they agree to abandon it; Abu Yusuf said they should be imprisoned and beaten. The commentator argues that this indicates emphasis, not obligation, because fighting and beating are for those who refuse to comply after being commanded, not for those who simply omit it as individuals. The passage also clarifies that adhan is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) in the sense that if it is performed in a town, the obligation is lifted from others, but it is still sunnah for each individual to say it. The sin for abandoning it is shared between wajib and sunnah mu'akkadah in Hanafi jurisprudence, so citing sin does not prove obligation.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A strongly emphasized recommended act that is not obligatory but its abandonment incurs sin.
كفاية (kifāyah): A communal obligation; if some perform it, the obligation is lifted from the rest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence cited by those who argue adhan is wajib?
A) The hadith 'The adhan is part of prayer'
B) The statement from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that those who pray without adhan 'erred regarding the sunnah and sinned'
C) The fact that Imam Muhammad said to fight those who abandon it
D) The consensus of the Sahaba

Key Takeaway
Adhan is a strongly emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) in the Hanafi school, with evidence from practice and from the term 'sunnah' itself.

Tarji' and Lahn in the Adhan: Hanafi Rulings and Dispute
Definition and ruling of tarji' and lahn in adhan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tarji' and lahn in the adhan and explain the reasoning behind the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Tarji' in adhan is mubah, not sunnah; lahn is haram. The Prophet's order to Abu Mahdhura was specific, not general.

In this passage, the commentator defines two important terms related to the adhan: tarji' (the practice of lowering and raising the voice) and lahn (melodic singing). The Hanafi school holds tarji' as permissible but not recommended, while the Shafi'i school considers it sunnah. The passage explains the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof and emphasizes that lahn in both adhan and Quran is prohibited. Let's walk through the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms
Define tarji' and lahn as used in the adhan. Tarji' is lowering and then raising the voice in the two shahadahs. Lahn is melodic singing or humming that distorts the words.
The same term 'lahn' can also mean intelligence, but here it refers to melody.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each
For tarji': mubah (permissible) but khilaf al-awla (contrary to better practice). For lahn: haram (forbidden) in adhan and Quran.
Tarji' is not sunnah; lahn is prohibited because it distorts the message.
3
Analyze the proof for tarji'
Bilal (ra) did not do tarji'. Abu Mahdhura (ra) did tarji' by order of the Prophet, but that order was for a specific teaching purpose due to his shyness, not as a general sunnah.
The Hanafi proof relies on the normal practice of Bilal and the context of Abu Mahdhura's instruction.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i considers tarji' as sunnah based on the same hadith of Abu Mahdhura, but the Hanafi school responds that the order was not general.
The difference stems from the interpretation of the command's generality.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In the Hanafi school, the mu'adhdhin does not perform tarji'. In the Shafi'i school, it is recommended to do so.
This difference affects the actual practice of adhan in each school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (بلا ترجيع) أي ليس فيه ترجيع وهو أن يخفض بالشهادتين صوته ثم يرجع فيرفع بهما صوته لأن بلالاً كان لا يرجع ، وأبو محذورة رجع بأمره للتعليم كما كان عادته في تعليم أصحابه لا لأنه سنة، ولأن المقصود منه إلا علام ولا يحصل بالإخفاء فصار كسائر كلماته. والظاهر من عباراتهم أن الترجيع عندنا مباح فيه ليس بسنة ولا مكروه لكن ذكر الشارح وغيره أنه لا يحل الترجيع بقراءة القرآن ولا التطريب فيه. والظاهر أن الترجيع هنا ليس هو الترجيع في الأذان بل هو التغني. وفي غاية البيان معزياً إلى ابن سعد في الطبقات : كان لرسول الله له ثلاثة مؤذنين : بلال وأبو محذورة وعمرو ابن أم مكتوم، فإذا غاب بلال أذن أبو محذورة، وإذا غاب أبو محذورة أذن .عمر. وقال الترمذي: أبو محذورة اسمه سمرة بن معير. قوله (ولحن) أي ليس فيه لحن أي تلحين وهو كما في المغرب التطريب والترنم ، يقال لحن في قراءته تلحيناً طرب فيها وترنم . وأما اللحن فهو الفطنة والفهم لما لا مستنداً إلى شرح المنية . قوله : ( وأبو محذورة رجع بأمره الخ) جواب عما استدل به الشافعي رحمه الله كما في الهداية. وفي العناية ذكر في الأسرار أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أمره بذلك لحكمة رويت في قصته وهي أن أبا محذورة كان يبغض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قبل الإسلام بغضاً شديداً فلما أسلم أمره رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالأذان ، فلما بلغ كلمات الشهادة خفض صوته حياء من قومه فدعاه رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم وعرك أذنه فقال له : ارجع وامدد بها صوتك إما ليعلمه أنه لا حياء من الحق أو ليزيده محبة للرسول و بتكرير كلمات الشهادة. قوله : (والظاهر من عبارتهم الخ) قال في النهر : ويظهر أنه خلاف الأولى، أما الترجيع بمعنى التغني فلا
His saying: (without tarji') meaning there is no tarji' in it, which is to lower the voice in the two shahadahs then return and raise the voice with them. Because Bilal would not do tarji', and Abu Mahdhura did tarji' by order for teaching, as was his habit in teaching his companions, not because it is sunnah. And because the purpose of it (adhan) is announcement, and it is not achieved by concealment, so it becomes like its other words. The apparent from their statements is that tarji' in our school is permissible, neither sunnah nor disliked. But the sharh and others mentioned that tarji' in Quran recitation is not allowed, nor is melody in it. Apparently tarji' here is not the same as tarji' in the adhan, but rather it is singing. In Ghayat al-Bayan, citing Ibn Sa'd in al-Tabaqat: The Messenger of Allah had three mu'adhdhins: Bilal, Abu Mahdhura, and 'Amr ibn Umm Maktum. When Bilal was absent, Abu Mahdhura called the adhan, and when Abu Mahdhura was absent, 'Umar called. And al-Tirmidhi said: Abu Mahdhura's name is Samura ibn Mu'ayr. His saying: (and without lahn) meaning there is no lahn in it, i.e., talhin, which is, as in al-Maghrib, singing and humming. It is said: he sang in his recitation, i.e., he made it melodic. As for lahn (with a different vowel), it is intelligence and understanding of what is not... based on Sharh al-Munyah. His saying: (And Abu Mahdhura did tarji' by his order) is a response to what al-Shafi'i used as proof, as in al-Hidayah. In al-'Inayah, it is mentioned in al-Asrar that the Prophet ordered him for a wisdom related in his story: that Abu Mahdhura intensely hated the Messenger of Allah before Islam. When he became Muslim, the Messenger ordered him to call the adhan. When he reached the words of the shahadah, he lowered his voice out of shyness from his people. So the Messenger called him, rubbed his ear, and said: 'Return and elongate your voice with it' either to teach him that there is no shyness from truth or to increase his love for the Messenger by repeating the words of shahadah. His saying: (And the apparent from their statements etc.) He said in al-Nahr: And it appears that it is contrary to the better practice. As for tarji' in the sense of singing, then no.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage defines two terms related to the adhan: tarji' and lah'n. Tarji' refers to the practice of lowering the voice during the two shahadahs and then raising it again. The Hanafi position is that tarji' is permissible (mubah) in the adhan; it is neither sunnah nor disliked. However, doing it is considered contrary to the preferred practice (khilaf al-awla). The commentator supports this by pointing out that Bilal (ra) did not do tarji', and Abu Mahdhura (ra) only did it by a specific order from the Prophet for teaching purposes, not as a general sunnah. The passage also refutes the Shafi'i argument that tarji' is sunnah based on Abu Mahdhura's hadith. As for lah'n (melody), it is prohibited in the adhan and in Quran recitation. The commentator distinguishes between 'lahn' (melody) and 'lahn' (wit), noting the different meanings.

Key Terms
ترجيع (tarjī'): The practice of lowering the voice during the two shahadahs in adhan and then raising it again.
لحن (lahn): Melody or singing in the voice while reciting adhan or Quran; prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on tarji' in the adhan?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
B) It is mubah (permissible) but contrary to better practice.
C) It is makruh tahrimi.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Tarji' in adhan is mubah but khilaf al-awla; lahn is haram; the dispute with Shafi'i hinges on the generality of the Prophet's command to Abu Mahdhura.

Prayers Without Adhan in the Hanafi School
Listing non-obligatory prayers excluded from the sunnah of adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which prayers have adhan prescribed in the Hanafi school and state the reasoning behind the exclusion of non-obligatory prayers.

Core Idea
Adhan is only for the five obligatory prayers and Jumu'ah; all other prayers are excluded.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a common misconception: not every prayer receives the call to prayer. The Hanafi school restricts the sunnah of adhan to the five daily prayers and Friday prayer. Other prayers like witr, 'Eid, and janazah are excluded because they are considered subsidiary or are performed within the time of an obligatory prayer. The commentary also notes Shafi'i practices where adhan is used for non-prayer occasions, but these are not part of the Hanafi sunnah.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi ruling
Begin by noting that adhan is prescribed only for the five obligatory daily prayers and Jumu'ah. This is the core ruling from the passage.
The phrase 'وخرج بالفرائض ما عداها' indicates exclusion of all else.
2
Identify the excluded prayers
List the prayers explicitly mentioned: witr, both 'Eids, janazah, eclipse, rain, tarawih, and the regular sunnah prayers. Also include vowed prayers as noted by al-Ramli.
These are considered 'follow-up' (اتبع) to the obligatory prayers.
3
Analyze the reasoning for witr
Witr is considered wajib in the Hanafi school, yet no adhan is prescribed for it. The reason given is that it is performed within the time of 'Isha, so the adhan of 'Isha suffices.
This shows the principle that adhan is tied to the prayer time, not the prayer itself.
4
Understand the Shafi'i perspective as expansion
The passage notes that Shafi'is may prescribe adhan for non-prayer occasions (newborn, distress, etc.). This is not the Hanafi view, but the author says there is no harm in it in our school.
The Hanafi position is limited, but other practices are not automatically rejected.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a mosque that wishes to call adhan for Tarawih. According to the Hanafi school, this is not sunnah; it is permissible but not recommended. The mufta bihi is not to do it.
This clarifies practical implementation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخرج بالفرائض ما عداها فلا أذان للوتر ولا للعيد ولا للجنائز ولا للكسوف والاستسقاء والتراويح والسنن الرواتب لأنها اتباع للفرائض والوتر وإن كان واجباً عنده لكنه يؤدي في وقت العشاء فاكتفي بأذانه لا لأن الاذان لهما على الصحيح كما ذكره الشارح . قوله (وخرج بالفرائض الخ قال الرملي : أي الصلوات الخمس فلا يسن للمنذورة. ورأيت في كتب الشافعية أنه قد يسن الأذان لغير الصلاة كما في أ أذن المولود والمهموم والمفزوع والغضبان ومن ساء خلقه من إنسان أو بهيمة، وعند مزدحم الجيش وعند الحريق. قيل : وعند إنزال الميت القبر قياساً على أول خروجه للدنيا لكن رده ابن حجر في شرح العباب. وعند تغول الغيلان أي عند تمرد الجن الخبر صحيح فيه. أقول : ولا بعد فيه عندنا
And he excluded other than the obligatory prayers: there is no adhan for witr, nor for the two 'Eids, nor for funerals, nor for eclipse prayer, nor for rain prayer, nor for tarawih, nor for the regular sunnah prayers, because they are follow-up to the obligatory prayers. Witr, although obligatory according to him (Abu Hanifa), is performed within the time of 'Isha' prayer, so the adhan of 'Isha' suffices, not because adhan is prescribed for it on the correct view. His saying: (And he excluded other than the obligatory prayers) al-Ramli said: i.e., the five prayers; it is not sunnah for the vowed prayer. And I have seen in books of the Shafi'is that adhan may be sunnah for other than prayer, such as the call in the ear of a newborn, and for the distressed, the frightened, the angry, the one with bad character, whether human or animal, and in crowded armies, and at fires. It is said: and at the lowering of the deceased into the grave by analogy with his first emergence into the world, but Ibn Hajar refuted this in Sharh al-'Ubab. And at the time of the ghouls' invasion, i.e., when jinn rebel; the hadith about this is authentic. I say: And there is no harm in it in our school.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage specifies that the sunnah of adhan is only for the five obligatory daily prayers and Jumu'ah. It is not prescribed for witr, 'Eid prayers, janazah, eclipse prayer, rain prayer, tarawih, or regular sunnah prayers. The reason given is that these are follow-up or subsidiary to the obligatory prayers. Regarding witr, although in the Hanafi school it is considered wajib (obligatory), since it is performed within the time of 'Isha, the adhan for 'Isha suffices. The commentator then adds a note from al-Ramli that the same applies to vowed prayers (salat al-nadhr). He also mentions that in the Shafi'i school, adhan is recommended for various occasions like calling in the ear of a newborn, for the distressed, etc. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq comments that there is no harm in such practices in the Hanafi school, implying permissibility.

Key Terms
فريضة (farīḍah): The five obligatory daily prayers and Jumu'ah, for which adhan is prescribed.
نافلة (nāfilah): Voluntary prayers not prescribed for adhan.
وتْر (witr): Obligatory (wajib) prayer performed after 'Isha; no adhan because it falls within 'Isha time.
اتباع (itbā'): Follow-up or subsidiary; non-obligatory prayers are considered follow-up to the fara'id.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason adhan is not prescribed for witr prayer?
A) Witr is not considered an obligatory prayer in the Hanafi school.
B) Witr is performed during the time of 'Isha, so the adhan of 'Isha suffices.
C) The Prophet never performed adhan for witr.
D) Witr is a sunnah prayer and thus does not require adhan.

Key Takeaway
Adhan is only prescribed for the five daily prayers and Jumu'ah; all other prayers, including witr, 'Eid, and janazah, do not have a separate call to prayer in the Hanafi school.

Ruling of Adding 'al-Salat Khairun min al-Nawm' in Fajr Adhan
Explains the mustahabb addition for Fajr adhan and its proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the addition in Fajr adhan, explain the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Bilal, and identify its correct placement according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The addition 'al-salat khairun min al-nawm' is mustahabb, not wajib, placed after 'hayya ala al-falah'.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on the phrase 'al-salat khairun min al-nawm' (prayer is better than sleep) added in the Fajr adhan. The passage explains that this addition is recommended (mustahabb) based on the Prophet's approval of Bilal's action. It also clarifies the correct placement within the adhan, refuting an alternative view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The addition of 'al-salat khairun min al-nawm' in the Fajr adhan. Determine the hukm level: fard, wajib, or mustahabb.
The passage explicitly states 'wa huwa lil-nadb' (it is for recommendation).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The hadith of Bilal who mentioned the phrase when the Prophet was asleep, and the Prophet approved it.
The dalil is a hadith ahad, transmitted with a single chain.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does this hadith prove recommendation? The Prophet said 'ma ahsana hadha' (how beautiful this is) and instructed 'ja'alhu fi adhanika' (put it in your adhan). The word 'ahsana' indicates praise, not a command of obligation.
Hanafi usul: commands that carry a qarina (context) of praise indicate nadb, not wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there a disagreement? Some scholars, like al-Fadli, hold that the phrase should be said after the entire adhan, not within it.
The passage explicitly refutes al-Fadli's view.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Why does the Hanafi school prefer the placement after 'hayya ala al-falah'? Because the matn says 'after success (falāh) of the Fajr adhan', and the hadith mentions the Prophet's approval of that placement.
The mufta bihi position is that it is mustahabb and placed after the second 'hayya ala al-falah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ويزيد بعد فلاح أذان الفجر الصلاة خير من النوم مرتين الحديث بلال حيث ذكرها حين وجد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نائماً فلما انتبه أخبره به فاستحسنه وقال اجعله في أذانك. وهو للندب بقرينة قوله «ما أحسن هذا وإنما خص الفجر به لأنه وقت نوم وغفلة فخص بزيادة الأعلام دون العشاء لأن النوم قبلها مكروه أو نادر وإنما كان النوم مشاركاً للصلاة في أصل الخيرية لأنه قد يكون عبادة كما إذا كان وسيلة إلى تحصيل طاعة أو ترك معصية، أو لأن النوم راحة في الدنيا والصلاة راحة في الآخرة فتكون الراحة في الآخرة أفضل. وفي قوله «بعد فلاح أذان الفجر» رد على من يقول إن محلها بعد الأذان بتمامه وهو اختيار الفضلي.
His statement: 'And he adds after the success of the Fajr adhan: 'The prayer is better than sleep' twice.' The hadith of Bilal, as he mentioned it when he found the Prophet ﷺ sleeping, and when he woke up, he informed him of it, so he approved it and said: 'Put it in your adhan.' And it is for recommendation (nadb) indicated by his saying: 'How beautiful this is.' And it is specifically for Fajr because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness, so it was specified with an increase of announcement, unlike Isha because sleep before it is disliked or rare. Sleep shares with prayer in the origin of goodness because it may be worship if it is a means to obedience or leaving sin, or because sleep is rest in this world and prayer is rest in the Hereafter, so the rest in the Hereafter is superior. And in his statement 'after the success of the Fajr adhan' is a refutation of those who say its place is after the adhan entirely, which is the choice of al-Fadli.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the addition of 'al-salat khairun min al-nawm' in the Fajr adhan. The author explains that this phrase is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib, based on the hadith of Bilal who mentioned it to the Prophet ﷺ, and the Prophet approved it saying 'ja'alhu fi adhanika' (put it in your adhan). The phrase 'ma ahsana hadha' indicates recommendation, not obligation. The Fajr adhan is singled out for this addition because it is a time of sleep and forgetfulness. The author refutes the view that it should be said after the entire adhan, arguing it comes after 'hayya ala al-falah'. The commentary also discusses the nature of sleep as potentially good.

Key Terms
الندب (al-nadb): Recommendation; a ruling that is not obligatory but meritorious.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Fard
B) Wajib

D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The addition 'al-salat khairun min al-nawm' is mustahabb, placed after 'hayya ala al-falah', based on the Prophet's approval of Bilal's action.

Ruling of Talhin in Adhan and Quran
Defines talhin and states its prohibition if it alters words

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define talhin and explain the Hanafi ruling on melodious chanting in adhan and Quran, distinguishing permissible beautification from prohibited alteration.

Core Idea
Talhin that changes the words is haram; beautifying the voice without alteration is permissible.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq defines talhin and clarifies its ruling in the Hanafi school. Many Muslims assume that any melodic recitation is either encouraged or prohibited outright. The Hanafi position offers a nuanced distinction: beautifying the voice (tahsin al-sawt) is permissible and even desirable, but talhin—defined as altering letters or vowels beyond permissible limits—is strictly prohibited in adhan and even more so in Quran recitation. We will explore the linguistic roots, the evidence from hadith, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Define talhin linguistically
Identify the word 'al-talhin' from the root L-H-N. The author cites al-Sihah: al-lahn is error in grammar, al-talhin is to find fault. But also, lahn has a second meaning: melody or intonation. Which meaning does the hadith use?
The hadith 'la'ala ba'dakum alhan bihujjatihi min ba'd' uses alhan meaning more eloquent, not out of tune.
2
Identify the relevant meaning
Ibn al-Malik interprets talhin here as taghanni (chanting) that leads to changing the words. So the relevant meaning is beautifying the voice to the extent of altering pronunciation.
This is the third meaning referred to in the text.
3
Extract the ruling
The author states that talhin as defined (changing words) is not permissible (la yahillu) in adhan. Beautifying the voice without singing is permissible, as per al-Khulasah. But Fath al-Qadir says tahsin al-sawt is desired.
There is nuance: leaving it is better according to some, but tahsin is desired.
4
Apply to adhan and Quran
The ruling applies to adhan and extends to Quran with greater emphasis. Listening to a mu'adhdhin who does talhin is also prohibited. Tafkhim (thickening lam) is allowed as dialect.
Al-Halwani allows elongation in hay'alah because it is dhikr.
5
Formulate the comprehensive definition
From the passage, talhin is defined as taking a letter beyond its permissible performance in recitation, by deficiency in letters, their qualities (harakat and sukun), or adding something. This is the technical definition for fatwa.
This distinguishes permissible beautification from prohibited alteration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من يفطن له غيره ومنه الحديث لعل بعضكم ألحن بحجته من بعض» وفي الصحاح : اللحن الخطأ في الإعراب والتلحين التخطئة والمناسب هنا المعنى الأول والثالث ولهذا فسره ابن الملك بالتغني بحيث يؤدي إلى تغيير كلماته، وقد صرحوا بأنه لا يحل فيه. وتحسين الصوت لا بأس به من غير تغن. كذا في الخلاصة وظاهره أن تركه أولى لكن في فتح القدير : وتحسين الصوت مطلوب ولا تلازم بينهما وقيده الحلواني بما هو ذكر فلا بأس بإدخال المد في الحيعلتين، فظهر من هذا أن التلحين هو إخراج الحرف عما يجوز له في الأداء من نقص الحروف أو من كيفياتها وهي الحركات والسكنات أو زيادة شيء فيها. وأشار إلى أنه لا يحل سماع المؤذن إذا لحن كما صرحوا به ودل كلامه أنه لا يحل في القراءة أيضاً بل أولى قراءة وسماعاً وقيده بالتلحين لأن التفخيم لا بأس به لأنه أحد اللغتين.
From it is the hadith: 'Perhaps some of you are more eloquent (alhan) in argument than others.' And in al-Sihah: al-lahn is error in grammar, and al-talhin is to find fault. The appropriate meaning here is the first and third, and for this reason Ibn al-Malik interpreted it as chanting (taghanni) that leads to changing its words, and they explicitly stated that it is not permissible in it. Beautifying the voice is fine without singing. Thus in al-Khulasah, and apparently leaving it is better, but in Fath al-Qadir: beautifying the voice is desired and there is no necessary connection between them. Al-Halwani restricted it to what is dhikr, so there is no harm in introducing elongation (madd) in the hay'alah. From this it appears that talhin is taking a letter beyond what is permissible in performance, by deficiency of letters or their qualities (harakat and sukun) or by adding something. And he indicated that it is not permissible to listen to the mu'adhdhin if he talhin, as they explicitly stated, and his statement indicates that it is not permissible in recitation either, rather more so in recitation and listening. And he restricted it to talhin because tafkhim (thickening) is fine because it is one of the two dialects.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage defines and rules on talhin (melodious chanting) in adhan and Quran. The author cites a hadith about 'alhan' and explains through lexicons that talhin means either beautifying the voice or making grammatical errors. The relevant meaning here is beautifying to the extent of changing words, which is impermissible (la yahillu). Beautifying the voice without such change is permissible. The author notes that according to Fath al-Qadir, beautifying the voice is desirable, but talhin is not. Al-Halwani exempts elongation in the hay'alah. Talhin is defined as pronouncing letters beyond permissible limits by deficiency or addition. Listening to a mu'adhdhin who does talhin is also impermissible, and the same applies even more to Quranic recitation. Tafkhim (thickening the lam in Allah) is allowed as it is a dialect.

Key Terms
التلحين (al-talhin): Melodious chanting that alters the correct pronunciation, whether by deficiency, excess, or incorrect articulation of letters and vowels.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on talhin (melodious chanting) in the adhan?
A) It is mustahabb to do it.
B) It is haram if it changes the words, but beautifying voice is permissible.
C) It is wajib to avoid all beautification.
D) It is makruh tanzihi even without change.

Key Takeaway
Talhin is defined as alteration of letters or vowels beyond permissible limits and is haram in adhan and Quran; beautifying without change is permissible and even desirable.

Similarity of Iqamah to Adhan in Sunnah and Structure
Explains that iqamah is like adhan in rulings but differs in tarji' and number

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the structure of iqamah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding the number of phrases.

Core Idea
The iqamah is like the adhan in being Sunnah and in having pairs (tathniyah); the Shafi'i claim of oddness is a misinterpretation of 'watir'.

This passage addresses a key practical difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: the number of times each phrase is repeated in the iqamah. While both schools agree that the iqamah is Sunnah for the five daily prayers, they differ on whether its phrases should be said in pairs (tathniyah) or odd (it'ar). The Hanafis hold that all phrases, including the takbir, are said twice, based on mutawatir reports from Bilal. The Shafi'is argue that the hadith 'make the iqamah odd' refers to the number of phrases. Al-Marghinani resolves this by interpreting 'odd' as rapid delivery, not odd count.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on iqamah phrase structure
Identify that Hanafis require each phrase of the iqamah to be said twice (tathniyah), including the takbir and 'qad qamat al-salah'.
This is based on mutawatir reports from Bilal.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Recognize that Shafi'is hold the iqamah should be odd (it'ar) based on the hadith 'shaffa' al-adhan wa watir al-iqamah'.
The hadith is from Bukhari.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
Understand the Hanafi interpretation of 'watir' as rapid delivery (hadr), not odd count, and note that Shafi'is themselves do not make the takbir odd in iqamah.
This internal inconsistency weakens the Shafi'i argument.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof: mutawatir reports and the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah
See that the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah gives iqamah as 17 phrases (implying pairs) and al-Tahawi states the reports from Bilal are mutawatir that he gave iqamah in pairs until death.
The strength of the Hanafi proof lies in its transmission certainty.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In practice, Hanafis repeat each phrase twice, while Shafi'is repeat only the takbir twice and the other phrases once.
This affects the recitation in mosques following different schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والإقامة مثله) أي مثل الأذان في كونه سنة الفرائض فقط وفي عدد كلماته وفي ترتيبها الحديث الملك النازل من السماء فإنه أذن مثنى مثنى، وأقام مثنى مثنى، ولحديث الترمذي عن أبي محذورة علمني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الأذان تسع عشرة كلمة والإقامة سبع عشرة كلمة. وإنما قال تسع عشرة كلمة لأجل الترجيع وإلا فالأذان عندنا خمس عشرة كلمة. وهذا الحديث لم يعمل بمجموعه الفريقان فإن الشافعية لا يقولون بتثنية الإقامة، والحنيفة لا يقولون بالترجيع. وأما ما رواه البخاري أمر بلال أن يشفع الأذان ويوتر الإقامة فمحمول على إيتار صوتها بأن يحدر فيها كما هو المتوارث ليوافق ما رويناه من النص الغير المحتمل لا إيتار ألفاظها، ويدل عليه أن الشافعية لا يقولون بإيتار التكبير بل هو مثنى في الإقامة عندهم، وقد قال الطحاوي : تواترت الآثار عن بلال أنه كان يثني الإقامة حتى مات.
His statement: 'And the iqamah is like it' meaning like the adhan in that it is Sunnah for the obligatory prayers only, in the number of its phrases, and in their order, based on the hadith of the angel descending from heaven for he gave adhan in pairs and iqamah in pairs, and the hadith of al-Tirmidhi from Abu Mahdhurah: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ taught me the adhan as nineteen phrases and the iqamah as seventeen phrases.' He only said nineteen phrases because of tarji', otherwise the adhan according to us is fifteen phrases. Neither school acts upon the entirety of this hadith: the Shafi'is do not say the iqamah is in pairs, and the Hanafis do not say there is tarji'. As for what al-Bukhari narrated: 'He ordered Bilal to make the adhan even (shaffa') and the iqamah odd (watir),' it is interpreted as making its voice odd by making it rapid (hadr) as is inherited, to agree with the text we narrated that is not susceptible, not making its phrases odd; and evidence for this is that the Shafi'is do not say the takbir is odd, rather it is in pairs in iqamah according to them. Al-Tahawi said: 'The reports from Bilal are mutawatir that he used to give iqamah in pairs until he died.'
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the iqamah's structure. The author explains that iqamah is similar to adhan in being Sunnah for the five daily prayers, in number of phrases (considering tarji' difference), and in order. The hadith of the angel and Abu Mahdhurah are cited. The Hanafi position is that iqamah is in pairs (like adhan except for tarji'in adhan) and takbir is also pairs. The Shafi'i position differs, claiming iqamah is odd but the Hanafis argue that the hadith of Bilal shows pairs, and the 'watir' in Bukhari refers to rapidity, not odd number of phrases. This is a key difference in practice.

Key Terms
التثنية (al-tathniyah): Saying each phrase twice in adhan and iqamah (except the final takbir).
الترجيع (al-tarji'): Repeating the two shahadas softly before the loud call in the adhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All phrases once except 'qad qamat al-salah' which is twice
B) All phrases twice (tathniyah)
C) All phrases odd (witir)
D) Only the takbir is repeated twice

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the iqamah, like the adhan, consists of phrases said in pairs, and the Shafi'i proof from 'watir' is interpreted as rapid delivery, not odd count.

Tarassul in Adhan and Hadr in Iqamah
States the recommended slowness in adhan and speed in iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended manner of delivering adhan and iqamah and distinguish tarassul from hadr.

Core Idea
Tarassul (slowness) is recommended for adhan; hadr (speed) is recommended for iqamah.

Adhan and iqamah are distinct calls to prayer with different recommended styles. This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on the manner of delivery, clarifying the definitions and basis for tarassul in adhan and hadr in iqamah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its recommended manner
The passage states that tarassul (slowness) is for the adhan, and hadr (speed) is for the iqamah. Note the specific recommendation for each call.
2
Define tarassul and hadr
Tarassul means pausing between the phrases of the adhan. Hadr means delivering the iqamah continuously without pauses.
The definition is given in the passage.
3
Understand the evidence and legal status
The ruling is based on inherited practice (tawaruth) and a hadith from al-Tirmidhi. The Hanafi school considers both acts mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.
This affects the merit, not the validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ويترسل فيه ويحدر فيها أي يتمهل في الأذان ويسرع في الإقامة، وحده أن يفصل بين كلمتي الأذان بسكتة بخلاف الإقامة للتوارث والحديث الترمذي أنه قال
His statement: 'And he does tarassul in it and hadr in it' meaning he takes time in the adhan and hurries in the iqamah. Its definition is that he separates between the words of the adhan by a pause, contrary to the iqamah, due to inherited practice and the hadith of al-Tirmidhi that he said...

Commentary
This is a clear ruling statement on the manner of delivery. Tarassul means to pronounce the adhan slowly, with a pause between each pair of phrases. Hadr means to deliver the iqamah quickly, without such pauses. This is based on inherited practice (tawaruth) and hadith evidence. The ruling is sunnah (mustahabb), not obligatory.

Key Terms
الترسل (al-tarassul): Slowness and deliberation in pronouncing the adhan, pausing between phrases.
الحدر (al-hadr): Speed and rapidity in pronouncing the iqamah, without prolonged pauses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Tarjī' in Adhan: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on tarjī' in adhan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on tarjī' in adhan, critique the Shafi'i proof using Hanafi usul, and identify the practical difference between the two schools.

Core Idea
The adhan is not recited with tarjī' because the hadith's 'even and odd' refers to voice, not word count.

Tarjī' – repeating the shahadah in a low voice then a high voice – is a point of contention between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafi school firmly holds that it is not part of the adhan, while the Shafi'i school considers it sunnah. This dispute hinges on the interpretation of a single hadith and the weight of mutawatir practice. Let's dissect the arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school holds regarding tarjī': it is not part of the adhan; the adhan is recited straightforwardly without repeating the shahadah in a lower voice.
The Hanafi view is based on the continuous practice (tawatur) of Bilal (RA).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i school considers tarjī' as sunnah and relies on a hadith in Sahih al-Bukhari: the Prophet (SAW) commanded Bilal to 'make the adhan even (shaf') and the iqamah odd (watr).'
Imam al-Shafi'i and his followers understand this as a command about the number of phrases.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the Bukhari hadith appears to suggest that adhan should have an even number of phrases and iqamah an odd number.
This would imply tarjī' because the shahadah is said twice in adhan (even) and once in iqamah (odd).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis reinterpret the hadith: 'even' and 'odd' refer to the voice quality – tarasul (slow, prolonged) for adhan and hadr (quick) for iqamah. Evidence: even the Shafi'is say the takbir in iqamah is dual (even), not odd, so the hadith cannot be literal about word count. Also, mutawatir reports confirm Bilal always recited the iqamah with dual phrases.
Al-Tahawi's statement about tawatur is key.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In a Hanafi mosque, the adhan is recited without tarjī'; in a Shafi'i mosque, the mu'adhdhin repeats the shahadah in a low voice once and then in a high voice once.
This difference is observable in daily practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالترجيع. وأما ما رواه البخاري أمر بلال أن يشفع الأذان ويوتر الإقامة فمحمول على إيتار صوتها بأن يحدر فيها كما هو المتوارث ليوافق ما رويناه من النص الغير المحتمل لا إيتار ألفاظها، ويدل عليه أن الشافعية لا يقولون بإيتار التكبير بل هو مثنى في الإقامة عندهم، وقد قال الطحاوي : تواترت الآثار عن بلال أنه كان يثني الإقامة حتى مات.
With tarjī'. As for what Bukhari narrated: 'He commanded Bilal to make the adhan even and the iqamah odd' — it is interpreted as making the voice odd by speeding it as has been transmitted, to agree with what we have narrated from the text that is not susceptible [to another interpretation], not making the words odd. And evidence for this is that the Shafi'is do not say that the takbir is odd, rather it is dual in the iqamah according to them. And al-Tahawi said: The reports from Bilal are mutawatir that he used to make the iqamah dual until he died.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding tarjī' (repetition) in the adhan. The Hanafi school holds that the adhan is not recited with tarjī', i.e., repeating the shahadah twice in a low voice then twice in a high voice. The author refutes the opposing view that relies on a hadith from Bukhari where the Prophet commanded Bilal to make the adhan even (shaf') and the iqamah odd (watr). The Hanafis interpret this as referring to the voice (making it odd, i.e., quick in iqamah) not the words. They cite that even the Shafi'is do not apply this to the takbir, which is repeated in iqamah. Furthermore, al-Tahawi reports mutawatir traditions that Bilal always recited the iqamah with dual phrases, proving that the oddness is not in the word count but in the pace.

Key Terms
الترجيع (al-tarjī'): Repeating the shahadah in adhan once in a low voice and once in a high voice.
الشفع (al-shaf'): Making even, i.e., repeating phrases twice.
الوتر (al-watr): Making odd, i.e., reciting phrases an odd number of times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The number of phrases in adhan and iqamah
B) The tone and speed of recitation (tarasul vs hadr)
C) The number of takbirs
D) The number of shahadahs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects tarjī' in adhan, interpreting the key hadith as about voice quality, supported by the mutawatir practice of Bilal.

One Person Adhan, Another Iqamah
Ruling on a different person performing iqamah with or without permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a different person gives iqamah, explain the condition of the mu'adhdhin's consent, and identify the intra-Hanafi differences on this issue.

Core Idea
It is permissible for another to give iqamah, but disliked without the mu'adhdhin's consent.

The adhan and iqamah are typically performed by the same person, but what if someone else steps in? The Hanafi school has an internal discussion on this matter, hinging on the consent of the original mu'adhdhin. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explores the ruling and the evidence behind it, also highlighting that iqamah is more emphasized than adhan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is another person giving iqamah after adhan. The ruling varies based on the mu'adhdhin's consent: with consent it is permissible; without consent it is disliked (makruh tanzihan).
This is the preferred view in the passage.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi positions
Imam Khwahrizadah holds that iqamah by another without consent is disliked. Others, relying on the absolute statement in al-Majma', hold it is absolutely permissible.
Ibn al-Malak claimed the dislike is agreed upon, but the author questions that.
3
Trace the proofs
The absolute view cites the general permissibility in al-Majma'. The disapproving view considers the mu'adhdhin's right and the principle that the one who gives adhan should complete the call.
The passage does not cite a specific hadith but uses general fiqh principles.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah states it is better for the mu'adhdhin to give iqamah, but if another does it, it is permissible. This is the relied-upon position.
The author indicates that the stronger sunnah of iqamah supports the preference.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the mu'adhdhin objects, iqamah by another is valid but makruh tanzihan. If the mu'adhdhin consents or is absent, it is full permissible without dislike.
This distinction affects daily mosque practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة: وإن أذن رجل وأقام آخر بإذنه لا بأس به، وإن لم يرض به الأول يكره، وهذا اختيار الإمام خواهر زاده وجواب الرواية أنه لا بأس به مطلقاً ويدل عليه إطلاق ما في المجمع حيث قال : ولا نكرهها من غيره فما ذكره ابن الملك في شرحه من أنه لو حضر ولم يرض بإقامة غيره يكره اتفاقاً فيه نظر. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية والأفضل أن يكون المقيم هو المؤذن ولو أقام غيره جاز، والظاهر أن الإقامة أكد في السنية من الأذان كما صرح به في فتح القدير، ولهذا قالوا: يكره تركها للمسافر دون الأذان وقالوا : إن المرأة تقيم ولا تؤذن.
And in al-Khulasa: If a man gave adhan and another gave iqamah with his permission, there is no harm. If the first does not consent, it is disliked. This is the choice of Imam Khwahrizadah. And the answer of the narration is that it is absolutely no harm, as indicated by the absolute statement in al-Majma' where he said: 'We do not dislike it from someone else.' So what Ibn al-Malak mentioned in his commentary that if he is present and does not consent to another's iqamah, it is disliked by agreement, is debatable. And in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: It is better that the one giving iqamah be the mu'adhdhin, but if another gives it, it is permissible. And it is apparent that iqamah is stronger in sunnah than adhan, as stated in Fath al-Qadir. Therefore they said: It is disliked for a traveler to omit iqamah but not adhan. And they said: A woman gives iqamah but does not give adhan.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ruling on whether a different person can perform the iqamah after the adhan. The preferred view is that it is permissible but disliked if the mu'adhdhin objects. Some scholars like Khwahrizadah say it is disliked without consent, while others say it is absolutely permissible based on the general permission in al-Majma'. The better practice is that the same person does both. The passage also notes that iqamah is more emphasized as sunnah than adhan, evidenced by the traveler omitting adhan but not iqamah (disliked), and women performing iqamah but not adhan.

Key Terms
الكراهة (al-karāhah): Disliked, referring to tanzīh (slight dislike) in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Makruh
C) Mustahab
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
It is permissible for another to give iqamah, but disliked if the mu'adhdhin objects; iqamah is more sunnah than adhan.

Ruling on Walking During Iqamah
Ruling on the mu'adhdhin walking during iqamah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the mu'adhdhin walking during iqamah and distinguish between the opinions regarding movement after 'qad qāmati al-salāh'.

Core Idea
Walking during iqamah is disliked, but after 'qad qāmati al-salāh' the mu'adhdhin may walk if he is the imam.

The iqamah is a sunnah call that immediately precedes the salah. Scholars differed on whether the mu'adhdhin may walk while delivering it. This lesson examines three Hanafi sources and their positions, clarifying the ruling for different scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
First, note that the general ruling from Rawdat al-Natifi is that it is disliked (makruh) for the mu'adhdhin to walk during iqamah. Understand that this is a ruling of karahah tanzihiyyah (lightly disliked).
The iqamah should be delivered with attentiveness and continuity.
2
Examine the concession in al-Khulasa
Al-Khulasa states that after reaching the phrase 'qad qāmati al-salāh', the mu'adhdhin may choose to complete the iqamah where he is or walk to the prayer place. This applies whether he is the imam or not.
This shows a permissive view within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the restriction in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj
According to al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, if the mu'adhdhin is not the imam, he must complete the iqamah at the starting place without moving. There is no disagreement on this specific point.
This creates a distinction based on the role of the mu'adhdhin.
4
Synthesize the positions
Combine the three views: the default is dislike; after 'qad qāmati al-salāh' there is a choice, unless the mu'adhdhin is not the imam, in which case he must stay put.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon opinion) is that it is better not to walk, but it is permissible if necessary, especially for the imam after that phrase.
5
Apply to practice
Consider practical scenarios: a mu'adhdhin giving iqamah in a large mosque who needs to move to the front. If he is the imam, he may walk after 'qad qāmati al-salāh'; if not, he should remain in place.
Respecting the rulings demonstrates adherence to the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي روضة الناطفي : أكره للمؤذن أن يمشي في إقامته. وفي الخلاصة: إذا انتهى المؤذن إلى قد قامت الصلاة إن شاء أتمها في مكانه وإن شاء مشى إلى مكان الصلاة إماماً كان المؤذن أو غيره. وفي السراج الوهاج : إن كان المؤذن غير الإمام أتمها في موضع البداية من غير خلاف.
And in Rawdat al-Natifi: I dislike for the mu'adhdhin to walk during his iqamah. And in al-Khulasa: When the mu'adhdhin reaches 'qad qāmati al-salāh', if he wishes he completes it in his place, and if he wishes he walks to the place of prayer, whether the mu'adhdhin is the imam or someone else. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If the mu'adhdhin is not the imam, he completes it at the place of beginning without any disagreement.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage gives rulings on the mu'adhdhin's movement during iqamah. In Rawdat al-Natifi and al-Khulasa, it is disliked for him to walk during the iqamah. However, after reaching 'qad qāmati al-salāh', he may choose to complete it where he is or walk to the prayer place, regardless of whether he is the imam or not. But in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, if the mu'adhdhin is not the imam, he must complete it at the starting point without moving; there is no disagreement on this specific case.

Key Terms
الإقامة (al-iqāmah): The second call to prayer, announcing the start of salah.
قد قامت الصلاة (qad qāmati al-salāh): The phrase in iqamah meaning 'the prayer has been established'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school generally discourages walking during iqamah, but after 'qad qāmati al-salāh' the ruling is lenient for the imam, while a non-imam should remain in place.

Tarasul and Hadr in Adhan and Iqamah
Defines tarasul and hadr and their rulings in adhan and iqamah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tarasul and hadr, state their legal rulings in adhan and iqamah, and explain the proof and wisdom behind them.

Core Idea
Tarasul (slow recitation) is sunnah in adhan; hadr (quick recitation) is sunnah in iqamah.

The way we recite the adhan and iqamah carries specific sunnah practices. This lesson defines two key terms—tarasul and hadr—and explains their rulings based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the underlying wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Read the passage and determine what the author says about tarasul in adhan and hadr in iqamah. Note the ruling: both are sunnah, and leaving them is makruh tanzih.
The ruling is stated explicitly in the text.
2
Define the terms
Extract the definitions of tarasul and hadr from the passage. Tarasul means separating words with a pause; hadr means quick, continuous recitation.
The author gives both a general and a specific definition.
3
Identify the proof (dalil)
The author cites the hadith of al-Tirmidhi where the Prophet said to Bilal: 'When you give adhan, make tarasul; when you give iqamah, make hadr.' This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is quoted in meaning, not verbatim.
4
Understand the wisdom (hikmah)
Reflect on why tarasul suits adhan (announcement) and hadr suits iqamah (commencement of prayer). The author explains that adhan is for notification, so slowness helps hearing; iqamah signals start, so speed is appropriate.
Wisdom reinforces the ruling but is not the core proof.
5
Confirm the applied ruling
Conclude that in practice, the mu'tamad (relied upon) position is that tarasul in adhan and hadr in iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah, and omitting them is makruh tanzih.
This is the Hanafi fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ويترسل فيه ويحدر فيها أي يتمهل في الأذان ويسرع في الإقامة، وحده أن يفصل بين كلمتي الأذان بسكتة بخلاف الإقامة للتوارث والحديث الترمذي أنه قال لبلال : إذا أذنت فترسل في أذانك وإذا أقمت فاحدر فكان سنة فيكره تركه، ولأن المقصود الأذان الإعلام والترسل بحاله أليق ومن الإقامة الشروع في الصلاة والحدر بحاله أليق. وفسر الترسل في الفوائد بإطالة كلمات الأذان والحدر قصرها وإيجازها.
His statement: 'And he makes tarasul in it (adhan) and hadr in it (iqamah)' means he takes his time in adhan and speeds in iqamah. Its definition is that he separates between the words of adhan with a pause, contrary to iqamah, due to transmitted practice and the hadith of al-Tirmidhi that he said to Bilal: 'When you give adhan, make tarasul in your adhan, and when you give iqamah, make hadr.' So it became sunnah, thus leaving it is disliked. Because the purpose of adhan is notification, and tarasul is more suitable, while iqamah is commencement of prayer, and hadr is more suitable. And tarasul is explained in al-Fawa'id as lengthening the words of adhan, and hadr as shortening and abridging them.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage defines and provides the ruling for tarasul (slow, deliberate recitation) in adhan and hadr (quick recitation) in iqamah. The author explains that the practice is sunnah based on the hadith from al-Tirmidhi where the Prophet instructed Bilal. The wisdom: adhan is for announcement, so slow recitation aids hearing; iqamah signals immediate start, so speed is suitable. The definition: tarasul means separating each word with a pause in adhan, while hadr means joining words quickly in iqamah. Leaving this sunnah is disliked (makruh tanzih).

Key Terms
الترسل (al-tarasul): Slow, deliberate recitation with pauses between words in adhan.
الحدر (al-hadr): Quick, continuous recitation without pauses in iqamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal ruling for leaving tarasul in adhan according to the Hanafi school?
A) The adhan becomes invalid
B) It is makruh tanzih (disliked)
C) It is haram
D) It is permissible without dislike

Key Takeaway
Tarasul in adhan and hadr in iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah established by hadith and wisdom; omitting them is disliked (makruh tanzih).

The Dispute on Mistaking Adhan for Iqamah
Intra-Hanafi dispute with two contrasting rulings on mistaken adhan/iqamah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conflicting Hanafi positions on making adhan into iqamah and vice versa, and explain the rationale behind each.

Core Idea
The ruling flips depending on whether the change is in the words or the style.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi conflict. Two sources, al-Zahiriyyah and al-Muhit, give opposite rulings on what to do when someone mistakenly intermixes the phrases or styles of adhan and iqamah. Understanding the reasoning helps resolve apparent contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sources
Note which source (al-Zahiriyyah or al-Muhit) gives which ruling. Al-Zahiriyyah says repeat adhan if made into iqamah; al-Muhit says repeat iqamah if made into adhan.
The dispute is among later fatwa works, not the classical six books.
2
Extract the rationale
Al-Zahiriyyah relies on the idea that repeating adhan is legislated whereas repeating iqamah is not. Al-Muhit focuses on the change: making iqamah into adhan changes the entire sunnah (hadr), while making adhan into iqamah only changes the end.
The reasoning is based on sunnah elements: tarasul for adhan, hadr for iqamah.
3
Apply to a scenario
Given a person who says 'Allahu Akbar' twice with hadr in adhan, which ruling applies? The student must identify which source's reasoning addresses the type of change.
Practice distinguishing between a change in wording vs. style.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية : ولو جعل الأذان إقامة يعيد الأذان، ولو جعل الإقامة أذاناً لا يعيد لأن تكرار الأذان مشروع دون الإقامة، فما ذكره المصنف في الكافي من أنه لو ترسل فيهما أو حدر فيهما أو ترسل في الإقامة وحدر في الأذان جاز لحصول المقصود وهو الإعلام وترك ما هو زينة لا يضر، يدل على عدم الكراهة والإعادة وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : أذن ومكث ساعة ثم أخذ في الإقامة فظنها أذاناً فصنع كالأذان فعرف يستقبل الإقامة لأن السنة في الإقامة الحدر فإذا ترسل ترك سنة الإقامة وصار كأنه أذن مرتين اهـ. لكن قال في المحيط : ولو جعل الأذان إقامة لا يستقبل، ولو جعل الإقامة أذاناً يستقبل لأن في الإقامة التغير وقع من أولها إلى آخرها لأنه لم يأت بسنتها وهو الحدر ، وفي الأذان التغير من آخره لأنه أتى بسنته في أوله وهو الترسل يعيد اهـ . وهو مخالف لما في الظهيرية لكن تعليله يفيد أن المراد بجعل الأذان إقامة أنه أتى فيه بقوله قد قامت الصلاة مرتين فليكن هو المراد مما في الظهيرية، وتصير مسألة أخرى غير ما في الخانية والكافي وهو الظاهر ويسكن كلمات الأذان والإقامة لكن في ينوي الحقيقة، وفي الإقامة ينوي الوقف. ذكره الشارح وفي المبتغى : والتكبير جزم.
And in al-Zahiriyyah: If he made the adhan into iqamah, he repeats the adhan; and if he made the iqamah into adhan, he does not repeat, because repeating adhan is legislated but not repeating iqamah. So what the author mentioned in al-Kafi that if he made tarasul in both or hadr in both, or tarasul in iqamah and hadr in adhan, it is permissible because the purpose (notification) is achieved, and leaving what is embellishment does not harm. This indicates no dislike or repetition. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: He gave adhan and waited an hour, then started iqamah but thought it was adhan, so he did it like adhan. When he realizes, he must repeat the iqamah because the sunnah in iqamah is hadr; if he made tarasul, he left the sunnah of iqamah and it becomes as if he gave adhan twice. But in al-Muhit: If he made adhan into iqamah, he does not repeat; and if he made iqamah into adhan, he repeats because in iqamah the change occurred from beginning to end since he did not perform its sunnah (hadr), and in adhan the change was only at the end since he performed its sunnah (tarasul) at the beginning. This contradicts al-Zahiriyyah, but his reasoning shows that 'making adhan into iqamah' means he inserted 'qad qāmati al-salāh' twice, so that is what is meant in al-Zahiriyyah, and it becomes a different issue from what is in al-Khaniyyah and al-Kafi, which is apparent. And he pauses the words of adhan and iqamah, but in adhan he intends the full form, and in iqamah he intends stopping. The commentator mentioned it, and in al-Mubtagha: The takbir is pronounced with sukun (jazm).
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage deals with intra-Hanafi disputes about when someone mistakenly uses the wrong formula. There are two main scenarios: (1) Making adhan into iqamah (e.g., inserting 'qad qāmati al-salāh' and using hadr? Actually, the definition is ambiguous). According to al-Zahiriyyah, if he makes adhan into iqamah, he must repeat the adhan; but if he makes iqamah into adhan, he does not repeat. The reasoning: repeating adhan is legislated (like for a second congregation) while repeating iqamah is not. However, al-Muhit gives the opposite ruling: if he makes adhan into iqamah, he does not repeat; if he makes iqamah into adhan, he does repeat. The author attempts to reconcile by saying that the subject in al-Zahiriyyah is different: 'making adhan into iqamah' means he added the phrase 'qad qāmati al-salāh' while keeping tarasul, so the adhan is still valid but he should repeat it as a precaution? Actually the text is complex. The key point is that the ruling depends on whether the sunnah elements (tarasul/hadr) are observed. The passage also notes the pronunciation of the words: in adhan, one intends the full pronunciation (with vowels), while in iqamah, one intends to pause (stop). Takbir is pronounced with jazm (sukun).

Key Terms
جعل الأذان إقامة (ja'la al-adhāna iqāmatan): Reciting the adhan with the phrases and style of iqamah, e.g., adding 'qad qāmati al-salāh' and using hadr.
الترسل (al-tarasul): The recommended slow, measured pace in adhan.
الحدر (al-hadr): The recommended rapid pace in iqamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Zahiriyyah, what is the ruling if someone makes the adhan into iqamah?
A) He must repeat the iqamah only
B) He must repeat the adhan only
C) He must repeat both
D) He does not need to repeat anything

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two conflicting narrations on when to repeat adhan/iqamah, but the author reconciles them by differentiating between adding a phrase and changing the style.

Reconciling the Dispute: The Role of Wording and Style
Author's reconciliation of intra-Hanafi dispute and a ruling on pronunciation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the author distinguishes between two different meanings of 'making adhan into iqamah' and state the ruling on the pronunciation of adhan and iqamah words.

Core Idea
The apparent contradiction dissolves when 'making adhan into iqamah' is understood as adding the phrase 'qad qamati al-salah' versus simply changing the melodic style.

The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq resolves the conflict between al-Zahiriyyah and al-Muhit by pointing out that they address different scenarios: al-Zahiriyyah refers to inserting the specific iqamah phrase into adhan, while al-Muhit refers to changing the overall rhythmic delivery (tarasul vs hadr). He also notes a subtle rule about the pronunciation of the words themselves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two meanings
Al-Zahiriyyah's 'making adhan into iqamah' means adding 'qad qamati al-salah' (the distinctive iqamah phrase). Al-Muhit's case involves altering the delivery style (using hadr instead of tarasul).
The author's linguistic analysis clarifies the conflict.
2
Apply the author's distinction
Given a scenario where the mu'adhdhin says 'as-salatu khayrun min al-nawm' twice instead of once, which ruling applies? The student must categorize the change.
The distinction hinges on whether the change is at the beginning or end of the formula.
3
Note the pronunciation rule
In adhan, one intends to fully pronounce the words (with vowels); in iqamah, one intends to pause (stopping on the last letter). The takbir is said with jazm (sukun).
This rule affects the tajwid of the call.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms
قد قامت الصلاة (qad qāmati al-salāh): The distinctive phrase of iqamah meaning 'The prayer has been established'.
ينوي الحقيقة (yanwī al-ḥaqīqah): In adhan, one intends the full pronunciation of the word (with vowels).
ينوي الوقف (yanwī al-waqf): In iqamah, one intends to pause (stop) the word, not fully pronounce it.
