Tarsil and Hadr in Adhan and Iqamah: Sunnah and Reversal Ruling
Explaining the sunnah of tarsil and hadr and the ruling on reversing them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah method for adhan and iqamah and apply the mufta bihi ruling when the method is reversed.

Core Idea
Tarsil in adhan and hadr in iqamah are sunnah; reversal is valid but makruh, and repetition is only recommended.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the sunnah of delivering adhan with lengthening (tarsil) and iqamah with shortening (hadr). It then navigates through several Hanafi sources that appear to conflict on what happens if one reverses these methods. The commentator reconciles these views, concluding that while leaving the sunnah is disliked, the act remains valid, and any required repetition is only recommended (afdal), not obligatory. Understanding this reconciliation shows how later Hanafi scholars harmonize apparent contradictions within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah method for adhan and iqamah
From the hadith of Bilaal, the sunnah is tarsil (lengthening) for adhan and hadr (shortening) for iqamah. Understand the rationale: adhan aims to inform, so slow delivery suits; iqamah signals start, so haste suits.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute on reversal
Different Hanafi sources (al-Kafi, Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Muhit) differ on whether reversing the methods requires repetition. Note the specific scenarios: leaving sunnah entirely vs. adding iqamah words while retaining tarsil.
3
Follow the reconciliation process
The commentator distinguishes between two meanings of 'making adhan an iqamah': (1) omitting tarsil (al-Zahiriya) vs. (2) adding iqamah wording (al-Muhit). In the first, repetition is needed; in the second, not. This resolves the apparent contradiction.
4
State the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position (from al-Bada'i and al-Nahr) is that reversal is valid (jaa'iz) but disliked; repetition is recommended (afdal) but not obligatory. The essential purpose is fulfilled.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a person gives adhan with hadr (shortening), the adhan is valid and makruh; it is better to repeat it with tarsil. Similarly for iqamah with tarsil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لبلال : إذا أذنت فترسل في أذانك وإذا أقمت فاحدر فكان سنة فيكره تركه، ولأن المقصود الأذان الإعلام والترسل بحاله أليق ومن الإقامة الشروع في الصلاة والحدر بحاله أليق. وفسر الترسل في الفوائد بإطالة كلمات الأذان والحدر قصرها وإيجازها. وفي الظهيرية : ولو جعل الأذان إقامة يعيد الأذان، ولو جعل الإقامة أذاناً لا يعيد لأن تكرار الأذان مشروع دون الإقامة، فما ذكره المصنف في الكافي من أنه لو ترسل فيهما أو حدر فيهما أو ترسل في الإقامة وحدر في الأذان جاز لحصول المقصود وهو الإعلام وترك ما هو زينة لا يضر، يدل على عدم الكراهة والإعادة وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : أذن ومكث ساعة ثم أخذ في الإقامة فظنها أذاناً فصنع كالأذان فعرف يستقبل الإقامة لأن السنة في الإقامة الحدر فإذا ترسل ترك سنة الإقامة وصار كأنه أذن مرتين اهـ. لكن قال في المحيط : ولو جعل الأذان إقامة لا يستقبل، ولو جعل الإقامة أذاناً يستقبل لأن في الإقامة التغير وقع من أولها إلى آخرها لأنه لم يأت بسنتها وهو الحدر ، وفي الأذان التغير من آخره لأنه أتى بسنته في أوله وهو الترسل يعيد اهـ . وهو مخالف لما في الظهيرية لكن تعليله يفيد أن المراد بجعل الأذان إقامة أنه أتى فيه بقوله قد قامت الصلاة مرتين فليكن هو المراد مما في الظهيرية، وتصير مسألة أخرى غير ما في الخانية والكافي وهو الظاهر ويسكن كلمات الأذان والإقامة لكن في ينوي الحقيقة، وفي الإقامة ينوي الوقف. ذكره الشارح وفي المبتغى : والتكبير جزم. فلهذا لا الأذان أنه يعاد بينهما في ذلك فلا يرد ما ذكر فافهم قوله : (مرتين) أي مع الإتيان بالترسل أيضاً قوله : (فليكن هو المراد مما في الظهيرية الخ قال في النهر : أقول كيف يكون هو المراد مما في الظهيرية مع على ما فيها لا على ما في المحيط، والحق أن اختلاف الجواب لاختلاف الموضوع وذلك أن معنى جعل الأذان إقامة على ما في الظهيرية أنه ترك الترسل فيه فيعيد لفوات تمام المقصود منه، وعلى ما في المحيط أنه زاد فيه لفظ الإقامة فلا يعيد لوجود الترسل فيه كما صرح به. نغم لو جعل الإقامة أذاناً لا يعيده على ما في الظهيرية ويعيده على ما في الخانية وكأن الإعادة إنما جاءت على القول المقابل للراجح السابق، وبهذا تتفق النقول. ثم الإعادة إنما هي أفضل فقط كما في البدائع.
From Bilaal: 'When you give the adhaan, lengthen it, and when you give the iqamah, shorten it.' So it became a sunnah, and leaving it is disliked. Because the purpose of the adhaan is to inform, and lengthening is more suitable for that, while the purpose of the iqamah is to commence the prayer, and shortening is more suitable for that. Tarsil (lengthening) in al-Fawa'id is explained as prolonging the words of the adhaan, and hadr (shortening) as shortening and condensing them. In al-Zahiriya: If one makes the adhaan an iqamah, he repeats the adhaan; if he makes the iqamah an adhaan, he does not repeat, because repeating the adhaan is prescribed while repeating the iqamah is not. That which the author mentioned in al-Kafi, that if one lengthens in both or shortens in both or lengthens in the iqamah and shortens in the adhaan, it is permissible because the purpose (informing) is achieved, and leaving what is decorative does not harm, indicates that there is no dislike or repeat. In Fatawa Qadikhan: He gave the adhaan and paused for an hour, then started the iqamah thinking it was adhaan, so he acted like adhaan. When he realized, he should repeat the iqamah because the sunnah in iqamah is shortening, so if he lengthened, he left the sunnah of iqamah and became as if he gave adhaan twice. End quote. But in al-Muhit: If one makes the adhaan an iqamah, he does not repeat; if he makes the iqamah an adhaan, he repeats, because in the iqamah the change occurs from its beginning to its end since he did not fulfill its sunnah (shortening), while in the adhaan the change occurs at its end because he fulfilled its sunnah at its beginning (lengthening), so he repeats. End quote. This contradicts what is in al-Zahiriya, but his reasoning indicates that what is meant by 'making adhaan an iqamah' is that he said 'qad qamat al-salah' twice in it. So let that be what is meant from al-Zahiriya, and it becomes a different issue from that in al-Khaniya and al-Kafi, and this is apparent. And he pauses the words of adhaan and iqamah, but in adhaan he intends the real form, and in iqamah he intends stopping. The commentator mentioned it, and in al-Mubtagha: 'The takbeer is jazm.' Therefore, the adhaan is not repeated between them in that regard, so what was mentioned does not refute it. Understand. His statement: (twice) meaning with also performing tarsil. His statement: (so let it be the intended meaning from al-Zahiriya, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: I say, how could it be the intended meaning from al-Zahiriya while it is according to what is in it, not according to what is in al-Muhit? The truth is that the difference in answer is due to difference in subject. That is, the meaning of 'making adhaan an iqamah' according to al-Zahiriya is that he left tarsil in it, so he repeats due to missing the complete purpose. According to al-Muhit, it is that he added the wording of iqamah, so he does not repeat because tarsil is present, as is clearly stated. Similarly, if he makes iqamah an adhaan, he does not repeat according to al-Zahiriya, and repeats according to al-Khaniya. It seems that the repetition only comes on the opinion opposite to the preponderant one. And by this the transmissions agree. Then repetition is only better (afdal) as in al-Bada'i.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi discussion on the sunnah of tarsil (lengthening) in adhaan and hadr (shortening) in iqamah. It begins with the hadith of Bilaal (radyallahu anhu) which establishes these as sunnah; leaving them is makruh. The commentator explains the rationale: adhaan aims to inform, so slow delivery suits it; iqamah signals commencement, so haste suits it. Then various Hanafi sources (al-Zahiriya, al-Kafi, Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Muhit) present seemingly contradictory rulings on what happens if one reverses the prescribed delivery—e.g., making adhaan with hadr or iqamah with tarsil, or confusing the two. The commentator reconciles by distinguishing scenarios: in al-Zahiriya the case is one who omits tarsil entirely adhaan, so repetition is needed; in al-Muhit the case is one who adds iqamah words but still does tarsil, so no repetition. The final conclusion from al-Bada'i is that repetition (i'ada) is only recommended (afdal), not wajib. Students should understand that the core ruling is that the sunnah method is tarsil in adhaan and hadr in iqamah; deviating is makruh but the act remains valid. The detailed discussion shows how Hanafi scholars harmonize different reports.

Key Terms
التَّرَسُّل (al-tarassul): Lengthening the words of adhaan, stretching them.
الحَدْر (al-hadr): Shortening, quick delivery in iqamah.
الإِعَادَة (al-i'ada): Repetition of the adhaan or iqamah due to a defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person performs tarsil (lengthening) in iqamah?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid but disliked; repetition is recommended.
C) It is mustahabb to do so.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah styles for adhan and iqamah are tarsil and hadr respectively; if reversed, the act remains valid but is disliked, and repeating is recommended but not obligatory.

The Ruling on Pausing in Adhaan and Iqamah
Extract from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifying the pause in adhaan and iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting adhaan and iqamah with pauses, and distinguish between the real pause in adhaan and the intended pause in iqamah.

Core Idea
The words of adhaan and iqamah are recited with sukun; in adhaan the pause is real, in iqamah it is intended.

In this lesson, we examine the correct pronunciation of the adhaan and iqamah according to the Hanafi school. The source passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that these words are not fully inflected but are paused, based on the practice of the salaf. Understanding this ruling ensures the adhaan is performed in accordance with the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting the words of adhaan and iqamah with pause (sukun). The Hanafi ruling is that this is sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The source cites the report from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the predecessors used jazm (pause) for adhaan and iqamah.
This is a practice of the salaf, which is strong evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'they used not to inflect them fully' indicates that the original practice was to pause, not to apply full i'rab.
4
Note the nuance between adhaan and iqamah
In adhaan, the pause is real (i.e., the word itself is pronounced with sukun), while in iqamah, one intends to pause (as an artificial waqf).
This nuance is important for correct application.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) and is accepted across the school.
No major ikhtilaf within the Hanafi madhhab on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (لكن ينوي الحقيقة) لا دخل لذكر ينوي هنا وليس في عبارة الشارح ونصها ويسكن كلماتها لما روي عن إبراهيم النخعي أنه قال شيئان يجزمان كانوا لا يعربونهما الأذان والإقامة. يعني على الوقف لكن في الأذان حقيقة وفي الإقامة ينوي الوقف .اهـ. وفي شرح الدرر والغرر للشيخ إسمعيل : وما في البحر من أن المبتغى والتكبير جزم ففيه نظر، لأن سياق كلام المبتغى يقتضي أن" المراد منه تكبير الصلاة ولفظه : ولو قال الله أكبر بالرفع يجوز والأصل فيه الجزم لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : : «التكبير جزم والتسميع جزم (۱) اهـ. بقرينة المقابلة. ثم في اللفظ مجاز والمراد أن كلاً في الأذان. وفي المضمرات : إنه بالخيار في التكبيرات إن شاء ذكره بالرفع وإن شاء ذكره بالجزم وإن كرر التكبير مراراً فالاسم الكريم مرفوع في كل مرة وذكر أكبر فيما عدا المرة الأخيرة بالرفع وفي المرة الأخيرة هو بالخيار إن شاء ذكره بالرفع وإن شاء ذكره بالجزم.
His statement: (but he intends the real form) The mention of 'intends' has no relevance here and is not in the expression of the commentator; his text is: 'He pauses the words of adhaan and iqamah based on what was narrated from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i who said: Two things are recited with jazm (pause) and they used not to inflect them fully: the adhaan and iqamah. That means with stopping. But in adhaan it is real (i.e., the pause is part of the word), and in iqamah he intends pausing.' End quote. In Sharh al-Durar wa al-Ghurar by Sheikh Isma'il: 'What is in al-Bahr that al-Mubtagha and al-Takbir are jazm is questionable, because the context of al-Mubtagha's words indicates that what is meant by it is the takbeer of the prayer, and its wording: "If he says Allahu Akbar with raf', it is permissible; the original is jazm based on his statement, peace be upon him: "The takbeer is jazm and the tasmee' is jazm." End quote, by way of contrast. Then there is a metaphor in the wording, and what is meant is that each is in the adhaan.' In al-Mudmarat: He has a choice in the takbeers: if he wishes he says it with raf', and if he wishes he says it with jazm. And if he repeats the takbeer multiple times, the noble name is in raf' each time, and mention of 'Akbar' in other than the last time is with raf', and in the last time he has the choice: if he wishes he says it with raf', and if he wishes he says it with jazm.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage addresses the correct pronunciation of the words of adhaan and iqamah. The commentator clarifies that the words are recited with pause (sukun) rather than with full inflection (i'rab). The basis is a report from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the predecessors used to recite them with 'jazm' (stopping). However, there is a subtlety: in adhaan, the pausing is intended as the real form of the word (i.e., it is part of the word's pronunciation), whereas in iqamah, one intends to stop (waqf) artificially. Then the discussion moves to the takbeer (Allahu Akbar). A hadith states 'al-takbir jazm', meaning the word 'Akbar' is pronounced with a sukun on the ra'. But some later scholars note that if the mu'adhdhin says it with raf' (nominative), it is permissible. The original sunnah is jazm, but the mukhtar (chosen) view is that one has a choice, especially in the last repetition of takbeer. The key point for students: the adhaan is recited with pauses, not with full i'rab, but the takbeer can be recited in either way.

Key Terms
التَّسْكِين (al-taskeen): Pausing, i.e., reciting with sukun.
الجَزْم (al-jazm): The state of having no vowel; used for the takbeer.
الوَقْف (al-waqf): Intentionally stopping/pausing in iqamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on reciting the words of adhaan with sukun?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is sunnah.
C) It is makruh.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Reciting adhaan and iqamah with pauses (sukun) is a confirmed sunnah; in adhaan the pause is real, in iqamah it is intended.

The Ruling on the Takbeer in Adhaan: Jazm or Raf'?
Extract from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discussing the takbeer in adhaan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the takbeer in adhaan, including the original sunnah of jazm and the permissibility of raf'.

Core Idea
The original sunnah is to say 'Allahu Akbar' with jazm, but saying it with raf' is permissible, with a choice in the last repetition.

This lesson focuses specifically on the takbeer (Allahu Akbar) in adhaan. The source passage expands on the hadith 'al-takbir jazm' and explores whether the takbeer must be pronounced with a sukun on the ra' or if it can be with a nominative case. The Hanafi school adopts a position that balances the original sunnah with practical ease.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is pronouncing the takbeer 'Allahu Akbar' in adhaan. The original sunnah is jazm (sukun on the ra'), but raf' is permissible.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'al-takbir jazm wa al-tasmee' jazm' is cited as evidence for jazm.
Hadith from Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'jazm' indicates that the letter ra' in 'Akbar' is to be pronounced without a vowel (sukun). This is the original ruling.
4
Identify the permission for raf'
Later authorities, as mentioned in al-Mudmarat, state that the mu'adhdhin has a choice: he may say it with raf' (nominative) or with jazm. This is especially allowed in the last repetition.
The choice is based on ease and to avoid confusion in prolonged adhaan.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that jazm is sunnah but raf' is permissible. The later scholars gave the choice, particularly in the last takbeer.

Source Text

End quote, by way of contrast. Then there is a metaphor in the wording, and what is meant is that each is in the adhaan.' This passage addresses the correct pronunciation of the words of adhaan and iqamah. The commentator clarifies that the words are recited with pause (sukun) rather than with full inflection (i'rab). The basis is a report from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the predecessors used to recite them with 'jazm' (stopping). الرَّفْع (al-raf'): Pronouncing with the nominative case (dammah).

Key Takeaway

Facing Qiblah, Silence, and Turning in Adhaan
Listing sunan of adhaan and iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunan of adhaan and iqamah and identify which omissions are makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
The adhaan remains valid if sunan are omitted, but deliberate neglect is makruh tanzihi.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author details three key sunan of adhaan and iqamah: facing the qiblah, refraining from speech, and turning for the call phrases. These acts are recommended, not obligatory, but their omission without excuse is disliked. We will examine each sunnah, its evidence, and the exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sunan
List the three sunan explicitly mentioned: facing qiblah, refraining from speech, and turning for 'as-salah' and 'al-falah'.
Facing qiblah is stressed for adhaan and iqamah; turning is specific to the two phrases.
2
Understand the ruling on omission
If the mu'adhdhin omits facing qiblah, the adhaan is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi). For speech: if it is a little, no restart; if a lot, must restart. For turning, it remains sunnah even when alone.
The source cites al-Muhit and al-Khulasa for these details.
3
Note intra-Hanafi differences
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Halwani) held that turning is not required when alone. The relied-upon view is that it is still sunnah. Also, Abu Yusuf said responding to salam during adhaan is not obligatory.
The source uses Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and Fatawa Qadikhan for tarjih.
4
Recognize exceptions
Facing qiblah is not sunnah when riding. Clearing the throat is disliked unless to improve voice. Responding to salam is not required per Abu Yusuf.
Exceptions are from al-Zahiriya and Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ويستقبل بهما القبلة أي بالأذان والإقامة لفعل الملك النازل من السماء وللتوارث عن بلال، ولو ترك الاستقبال جاز لحصول المقصود ويكره لمخالفة السنة. كذا في الهداية . والظاهر أنها كراهة تنزيه لما في المحيط : وإذا انتهى إلى الصلاة والفلاح حول وجهه يمنة ويسرة ولا يجول قدميه لأنه في حالة الذكر والثناء على الله تعالى والشهادة له بالوحدانية ولنبيه بالرسالة فالأحسن أن يكون مستقبلاً، فأما الصلاة والفلاح دعاء إلى الصلاة وأحسن أحوال الداعي أن يكون مقبلاً على المدعوين ويستثنى من سنية الاستقبال ما إذا أذن راكباً فإنه لا يسن الاستقبال بخلاف ما إذا كان ماشياً. ذكره في الظهيرية عن محمد. قوله (ولا يتكلم فيهما) أي في الأذان والإقامة لما فيه من ترك الموالاة ولأنه ذكر معظم كالخطبة. أطلقه فشمل كل كلام فلا يحمد لو عطس هو ولا يشمت عاطساً ولا يسلم ولا يرد السلام وفيه خلاف، والصحيح ما عن أبي يوسف أنه لا يلزمه الرد لا بعده ولا قبله في نفسه. وكذا لو سلم على المصلي أو القارىء أو الخطيب، وأجمعوا أن المتغوط لا يلزمه الرد في الحال ولا السلام عليه حرام بخلاف من في الحمام إذا كان بمئزر . وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : إذا سلم على القاضي والمدرس قالوا لا يجب عليه الرد .اهـ. ومثله ذكر في سلام المكدي : ولو تكلم المؤذن أذانه استأنفه. كذا في فتح القدير وفي الخلاصة : وإن تكلم بكلام يسير لا يلزمه الاستقبال. وفي الظهيرية والتنحنح في الأذان مكروه إذا لم يكن لتحصيل الصوت. وفي الخلاصة: وكذا في الإقامة وإن قدم في أذانه وإقامته شيئاً بأن قال أولاً أشهد أن محمداً رسول الله ثم قال أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله فعليه أن يعيد الأول قوله (ويلتفت يميناً وشمالاً بالصلاة والفلاح) لما قدمناه ولفعل بلال رضي الله عنه على ما رواه الجماعة، ثم أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان وحده على الصحيح لكونه سنة الأذان فلا يتركه خلافاً للحلواني لعدم الحاجة إليه . وفي السراج الوهاج: إنه من سنن الأذان فلا يخل المنفرد بشيء منها حتى قالوا في الذي يؤذن للمولود ينبغي أن يحوّل .اهـ. وقيد باليمين والشمال لأنه لا يحول وراءه لما فيه من استدبار القبلة، ولا أمامه لحصول الإعلام في الجملة بغيرها من كلمات الأذان. وقوله بالصلاة والفلاح لف ونشر مرتب يعني أنه يلتفت يميناً بالصلاة وشمالاً بالفلاح وهو في الأذان والإقامة. بعده كونها مسكناً بالوقف عليه قوله: (ولم يبين وجهه) قال في النهر : لعل وجهه أن كونه خطاباً للقوم فيواجههم به لا يخص أهل اليمين واليسار بل يعم الجميع، وحينئذ فاختصاص اليمين بالصلاة والشمال بالفلاح تحكم . قال الرملي لكن الصحيح هو الأول لأنه المنقول عن السلف. كذا في البحر الرائق ج ١ م ٢٩
His statement: (and he faces the qiblah with both) i.e., with the adhaan and iqamah, following the action of the angel descending from heaven and the continuous practice from Bilaal. If he leaves facing the qiblah, it is permissible because the purpose is achieved, but it is disliked for contradicting the sunnah. This is in al-Hidayah. And it appears that this is tanzihi dislike, as is in al-Muhit: When he reaches 'as-salah' and 'al-falah', he turns his face right and left, and does not move his feet because he is in a state of dhikr and praise of Allah, and testimony of His oneness and of His prophet's messengership, so it is better to face qiblah. As for 'as-salah' and 'al-falah', it is a call to prayer, and the best state of the caller is to face those being called. An exception to the sunnah of facing qiblah is when the mu'adhdhin is riding; then facing qiblah is not sunnah, unlike when he is walking. This is mentioned in al-Zahiriya from Muhammad. His statement: (and he does not speak in them) i.e., in adhaan and iqamah, because of the loss of continuity (muwalat) and because it is a great dhikr like the khutbah. He made it absolute, so it includes all speech: he does not praise if he sneezes, nor does he respond to a sneezer, nor does he give salam, nor respond to salam. There is a difference of opinion, and the correct view is from Abu Yusuf that he is not obliged to respond, neither after nor before, in his own mind. Similarly, if one gives salam to a person in prayer, or reciting, or giving khutbah. And they agreed that a person defecating is not obliged to respond immediately, and giving salam to him is haram, unlike one in the bathroom if he is wearing an izaar. In Fatawa Qadikhan: If one gives salam to a judge or teacher, they said he is not obliged to respond. End quote. Similarly mentioned in Salam al-Makdi: If the mu'adhdhin speaks, he should restart his adhaan. This is in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Khulasa: If he speaks a little, he is not required to restart. In al-Zahiriya: Clearing the throat in adhaan is disliked if not for obtaining the voice. In al-Khulasa: Similarly in iqamah. If he introduces something in his adhaan or iqamah, such as first saying 'Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasulullah' then 'Ashhadu an la ilaha illallah', he must repeat the first. His statement: (and he turns right and left with 'as-salah' and 'al-falah') due to what we mentioned and the action of Bilaal (رضي الله عنه) as narrated by the group. Then he made it absolute, so it includes when he is alone, according to the correct view, because it is a sunnah of adhaan, so he should not leave it, contrary to al-Halwani who said there is no need for it. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: It is from the sunan of adhaan, so the one praying alone should not omit any part of it, even to the extent that they said regarding one who gives adhaan for a newborn, he should turn. End quote. And it is restricted to right and left because he does not turn behind him due to turning his back to the qiblah, nor in front of him because the general informing is achieved by other words of the adhaan. His statement: 'with as-salah and al-falah' is a laf wa nashr murattab, meaning he turns right with 'as-salah' and left with 'al-falah', both in adhaan and iqamah. Afterwards, they are with sukun by pausing. His statement: (and he did not explain his face) said in al-Nahr: Perhaps his face is that since it is an address to the people, he faces them with it, and it does not specifically apply to the people on the right and left but to everyone. Therefore, the specification of right with salah and left with falah is arbitrary. Al-Ramli said: But the correct is the first because it is transmitted from the salaf. As in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, vol. 1, p. 29.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage enumerates several sunan (recommended acts) of adhaan and iqamah. First, facing the qiblah during the entire adhaan is sunnah; leaving it is permissible but makruh tanzihi. An exception is made when the mu'adhdhin is riding—then facing qiblah is not stressed. Second, speaking during adhaan or iqamah is prohibited because it breaks continuity (muwalat) and the adhaan is a great dhikr. The mu'adhdhin should not respond to salam, return greetings, or even praise Allah if he sneezes. If he speaks a little, according to al-Khulasa, the adhaan is not invalidated, but if he speaks a lot, he must restart. Clearing the throat unnecessarily is also disliked. Third, it is sunnah to turn the face right when saying 'hayya ala as-salah' and left when saying 'hayya ala al-falah'. This practice is from Bilaal and applies even when the mu'adhdhin is alone. The commentator notes that the specification of right for salah and left for falah is established from the salaf, though some questioned it. Students should remember that these are recommended actions; neglecting them is makruh but does not invalidate the adhaan.

Key Terms
الاسْتِقْبَال (al-istiqbal): Facing the qiblah during adhaan and iqamah.
المُوَالَاة (al-muwalah): Continuity in the recitation of adhaan.
الاِلْتِفَات (al-iltifat): Turning the face right and left for 'as-salah' and 'al-falah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the mu'adhdhin speaks a few words during adhaan?
A) The adhaan is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The adhaan is valid and no repetition needed.
C) The adhaan is valid but disliked.
D) The adhaan becomes invalid only if the speech is unrelated.

Key Takeaway
Facing qiblah, refraining from speech, and turning with the call are sunan of adhaan; their omission does not invalidate but is disliked.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
15 min
Rulings of the Adhan: Facing Qibla, Speaking, Turning, and Responding
Commentary on the sunan and rulings of adhan and iqama from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on facing qibla, turning, speaking during adhan, and responding to the adhan, and identify the proofs and points of ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Facing qibla in adhan is sunnah, not fard; turning at hayya is sunnah; speaking is makruh; responding is fadila.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explains the sunan and rulings of the adhan and iqama. It covers four key areas: facing the qibla, speaking during the call, turning at the phrases 'hayya ala as-salah' and 'hayya ala al-falah', and the obligation of responding. The commentator presents the Hanafi positions with their proofs and notes intra-school differences. Understanding these rulings helps ensure the call to prayer is performed in accordance with the sunnah and avoids disliked or invalidating actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
For each sunnah or ruling (facing qibla, turning, speaking, responding), determine whether it is sunnah, wajib, makruh, etc. as per the Hanafi school.
The passage uses terms like 'sunnah', 'makruh', 'ja'iz', and 'fadila'.
2
Locate the dalil for each ruling
Find the evidence cited in the passage: actions of the angel and Bilal for facing qibla, hadith of Bilal for turning, hadith from Darqutni for not moving feet, and the hadith about responding with the foot.
The proofs are from sunnah (ahad) and practice of the Salaf.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify differences: Abu Yusuf on returning greeting, the disagreement on turning in iqama, and the obligation of responding.
The passage presents both sides and often indicates the preferred view (e.g., from an-Nahr, Fatawa Qadikhan).
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Based on the tarjih in the passage, state the relied-upon position for fatwa: facing qibla is sunnah, turning is sunnah, speaking is makruh, and responding is fadila.
The commentator relies on ar-Ramli and an-Nahr for the preferred views.
5
Apply the rulings in practice
Consider the practical implications: a caller who fails to face qibla commits makruh but the adhan is valid; speaking a little does not require restarting; responding verbally is not obligatory.
This step connects the rulings to actual performance.

منهما يكون مسكناً بالوقف عليه قوله: (ولم يبين وجهه) قال في النهر : لعل وجهه أن كونه خطاباً للقوم فيواجههم به لا يخص أهل اليمين واليسار بل يعم الجميع، وحينئذ فاختصاص اليمين بالصلاة والشمال بالفلاح تحكم . قال الرملي لكن الصحيح هو الأول لأنه المنقول عن السلف. كذا في البحر الرائق ج ١ م ٢٩

خلافاً لمن قال إن الصلاة باليمين والشمال والفلاح كذلك وفي فتح القدير: إنه الأوجه ولم يبين وجهه . وقيد بالالتفات لأنه لا يحول قدميه لما رواه الدارقطني عن بلال قال : أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا أذنا أو أقمنا أن لا نزيل أقدامنا عن مواضعها. وأطلق في الالتفات ولم يقيده بالأذان وقدمنا عن الغنية أنه يحول في الإقامة أيضاً. وفي السراج الوهاج : لا يحول فيها لأنها لإعلام الحاضرين بخلاف الأذان فإنه إعلام للغائبين، وقيل يحوّل إذا كان الموضع متسعاً. قوله (ويستدير في صومعته يعنى إن لم يتم الإعلام بتحويل وجهه مع ثبات قدميه فإنه يستدير في المئذنة ليحصل التمام والصومعة المنارة وهي في الأصل متعبد الراهب. ذكره العيني. ولم يكن في زمنه ل مئذنة لكن روى أبو داود من حديث عروة بن الزبير عن امرأة من بني النجار قالت: كان بيتي من أطول بيت بحول المسجد فكان بلال يأتي بسحر فيجلس عليه ينظر إلى الفجر، فإذا رآه أذن . وفي القنية : يؤذن المؤذن فتعوي الكلاب فله ضربها إن ظن أنها تمتنع بضربه وإلا فلا. وفي الخلاصة : ومن سمع الأذان فعليه أن يجيب وإن كان جنباً لأن إجابة المؤذن ليست بأذان. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : إجابة المؤذن فضيلة وإن تركها لا يأثم . وأما قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام من لم يجب الاذان فلا صلاة له فمعناه الإجابة بالقدم لا باللسان فقط. وفي المحيط : يجب على السامع للأذان الإجابة ويقول مكان حي على الصلاة» لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله، ومكان حي على الفلاح ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن، لأن إعادة ذلك يشبه الاستهزاء لأن ليس بتسبيح ولا تهليل وكذا إذا قال الصلاة خير من النوم» فإنه يقول صدقت وبررت ولا يقرأ السامع ولا . ولا يسلم ولا يرد السلام ولا يشتغل بشيء سوى الاجابة،

الغاية. قوله: (وفي السراج الوهاج لا يحول الخ ) قال في النهر الثاني أعدل الأقوال. قوله: (ولم يكن في زمنه مئذنة) قال في شرح الدرر والغرر وفي أوائل السيوطي أن أول من رقى منارة للأذان شرحبيل بن عامر المرادي وفي عرافته بني سلمة المنائر للأذان بأمر معاوية، ولم تكن قبل ذلك. وقال ابن سعد بالسند إلى أم زيد بن ثابت : كان بيتي أطول بيت حول المسجد فكان بلال يؤذن فوقه من أول ما أذن إلى أن بني رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فكان يؤذن بعد على ظهر المسجد وقد رفع له شيء فوق ظهره. قوله : (وقال الحلواني الخ) قال في النهر أقول: ينبغي أن لا تجب باللسان اتفاقاً على قول الإمام في الأذان بين يدي الخطيب، وأن تجب بالقدم اتفاقاً ، في الأذان الأول من الجمعة حيث لم يكن في المسجد. وباللسان أيضاً على الأول إلا أن يقال الواجب إنما هو السعي لا إجابة المؤذن وأثر الخلاف يظهر فيما لو سمع الأذان وهو يقرأ قطع القراءة على الأول للإجابة لا على الثاني. وصرح في المحيط والتحفة بأنه على الأول لا يسلم ولا يشتغل بما سوى الإجابة وهو صريح في كراهة الكلام عند الأذان، فما في التنجيس من أنه لا يكره إجماعاً استدلالاً باختلافهم في كراهته عند أذان الخطبة فإن الإمام إنما كرهه لإلحاق هذه الحالة بحالة الخطبة فكان هذا
Book of Prayer - Chapter of Adhan. In it: He faces the qibla with both, does not speak in them, and turns right and left at as-salah and al-falah. In al-Mudmarat: He has choice in the takbirs, if he wishes he mentions them with raf' and if he wishes with jazm, and if he repeats the takbir multiple times, the noble name is raised in every time, and the mention of 'akbar' except in the last time is with raf', and in the last time he has choice. His saying: 'He faces the qibla with both' meaning the adhan and iqama, due to the action of the angel descending from heaven and due to transmission from Bilal. If he leaves facing qibla, it is permissible because the purpose is achieved, but it is disliked for contradicting the sunna. Thus in al-Hidaya, and it appears it is tanzihi dislike. In al-Muhit: When he reaches as-salah and al-falah, he turns his face right and left and does not move his feet because he is in a state of remembrance and praise. Turning is only at these phrases. Exception: if the caller is riding, facing is not sunna, unlike if walking. In az-Zahiriya from Muhammad. His saying: 'He does not speak in them' meaning in adhan and iqama, due to lack of continuity and because it is great dhikr like the khutba. It is general, so he does not praise if he sneezes, nor does he respond to a sneeze, nor greet, nor return greeting. There is difference, the correct is from Abu Yusuf that he is not obliged to return greeting. Similarly if someone greets the one praying, reading, or delivering khutba. They agreed that one defecating is not obliged to return greeting at that time, and greeting him is haram. In Fatawa Qadikhan: If one greets a judge or teacher, they say he is not obliged to respond. Similarly for a beggar's greeting. If the caller speaks during his adhan, he restarts it. In Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasa: If he speaks a little, he is not obliged to restart. In az-Zahiriya: Clearing the throat in adhan is disliked if not for improving voice. In al-Khulasa: Same in iqama. If he puts something forward in his adhan and iqama, e.g., first saying 'ashhadu anna Muhammadan rasulullah' then 'ashhadu an la ilaha illallah', he must repeat the first. His saying: 'He turns right and left at as-salah and al-falah' due to what we mentioned and the action of Bilal, radi Allahu anhu, as narrated by the group. It includes even if alone, contrary to al-Halwani. In as-Siraj al-Wahhaj: It is from the sunan of adhan, so the one alone does not omit it. They even said for the one who calls adhan for a newborn, he should turn. It is restricted to right and left because he does not turn behind due to turning away from qibla, nor in front because the notification is achieved by other words. His saying 'by as-salah and al-falah' is a lubb wa nashr arranged, meaning he turns right at as-salah and left at al-falah. The phrase 'wa lam yubayyin wajhahu' – in an-Nahr: Perhaps its reasoning is that it is addressed to the people, facing them is not specific to right and left but general. Then specifying right with salah and left with falah is arbitrary. Ar-Ramli said the correct is the first because it is transmitted from the Salaf. Thus in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. He turns in his minaret, puts his fingers in his ears, does tathwib, and sits between them in maghrib. He gives adhan correctly, contrary to those who say salah is with right and left similarly. In Fath al-Qadir: It is the most suitable and he did not explain his reasoning. It is restricted to turning because he does not move his feet due to the hadith of Darqutni from Bilal: The Messenger of Allah, sallallahu alayhi wa sallam, ordered us when we called adhan or iqama not to move our feet from their places. He made it general in turning and did not restrict to adhan. We previously mentioned from al-Ghunya that he turns in iqama also. In as-Siraj al-Wahhaj: He does not turn in iqama because it is for informing those present, unlike adhan which is for informing those absent. It is said he turns if the place is spacious. His saying: 'He turns in his minaret' means if notification is not completed by turning his face while feet are fixed, he turns in the minaret to complete it. The minaret is originally the monk's place of worship. It is mentioned by al-Ayni. There was no minaret in his time, but Abu Dawud narrated from Urwa ibn Zubayr from a woman of Bani Najjar: My house was the tallest house near the mosque, and Bilal would come at dawn and sit on it looking for dawn, and when he saw it he called adhan. In al-Qunyah: If the caller calls adhan and dogs bark, he may hit them if he thinks they will stop by his hitting, otherwise not. In al-Khulasa: Whoever hears the adhan must respond even if in a state of janaba, because responding to the caller is not adhan. In Fatawa Qadikhan: Responding to the caller is a virtue; if he leaves it he does not sin. As for his saying, sallallahu alayhi wa sallam, 'Whoever does not respond to the adhan, there is no prayer for him' its meaning is responding with the foot, not only with the tongue. In al-Muhit: It is obligatory upon the hearer of adhan to respond, and he says in place of 'hayya ala as-salah' 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah', and in place of 'hayya ala al-falah' 'ma sha' allah kana wa ma lam yasha' lam yakun', because repeating it resembles mockery since it is not tasbih or tahlil. Similarly when he says 'as-salatu khairun min an-nawm', he says 'sadaqta wa bararta'. The hearer does not read, does not greet, does not return greeting, and does not occupy himself with anything other than response. The end. His saying: 'In as-Siraj al-Wahhaj he does not turn etc.' – in an-Nahr the second: the most balanced opinion. His saying: 'There was no minaret in his time' – in Sharh ad-Durar wa al-Ghurar and in Awail as-Suyuti: The first to ascend a minaret for adhan was Shurahbil ibn Amir al-Muradi, and in the caliphate of Bani Salma, minarets were built for adhan by order of Muawiyah, and there were none before that. Ibn Sa'd said with chain to Umm Zaid ibn Thabit: My house was the tallest house near the mosque, and Bilal used to call adhan on top of it from the first time he called until the Messenger of Allah, sallallahu alayhi wa sallam, built his mosque, then he would call adhan on the roof of the mosque, and something was raised for him above the roof. His saying: 'Al-Halwani said etc.' – in an-Nahr: I say: It is not obligatory with the tongue by agreement according to Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the adhan in front of the khatib. And it is obligatory with the foot by agreement in the first adhan of Friday when the mosque is not present. Also with the tongue according to the first, unless it is said that the obligatory is only the going, not responding to the caller. The effect of the difference appears if he hears the adhan while reciting: he stops recitation according to the first to respond, not according to the second. It is stated explicitly in al-Muhit and at-Tuhfa that according to the first, he does not greet nor occupy himself with anything other than response, which is explicit in the dislike of speech during adhan. So what is in at-Tanqih that it is not disliked by consensus is defeated by their difference regarding its dislike at the adhan of the khutba, for the Imam disliked it only to attach this situation to the situation of the khutba, so this is...
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the chapter of adhan from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It covers multiple sunan and rulings of the adhan and iqama. The commentator begins by explaining the ruling of facing the qibla during adhan and iqama. This is a sunnah based on the action of the angel who descended from heaven and the practice of Bilal (RA). Leaving it is permissible (ja'iz) but disliked (makruh tanzihi) because it contradicts the sunnah. The commentator then distinguishes between the time of facing qibla and turning: when reciting the takbirs, one faces qibla; only at 'hayya ala as-salah' and 'hayya ala al-falah' does one turn right and left. The text then addresses the prohibition of speaking during adhan and iqama. Speaking breaks the continuity (muwalat) and is akin to speaking during a khutbah. The commentator notes exceptions and differences: returning a greeting is not required according to Abu Yusuf, and only a little speech does not necessitate restarting the adhan. The next section discusses the specific turning at 'as-salah' and 'al-falah'. This is a distinct sunnah based on the practice of Bilal (RA). The turning is only done with the head and face, not the feet, as per the hadith from Darqutni. There is a difference of opinion whether one turns in the iqama as well; the preferred view in the text is that one does not turn in iqama because it is for those present. The commentator then covers additional sunan: turning in the minaret (if the minaret is high enough that turning the head is insufficient), putting fingers in ears, tathwib (saying 'as-salatu khairun min an-nawm' in the fajr adhan), and sitting between adhan and iqama in maghrib. The final portion of the passage discusses the obligation of responding to the adhan. There is a difference: some say it is obligatory (wajib), others say it is a virtue (fadila). The text reconciles by explaining that the hadith 'whoever does not respond, no prayer for him' refers to responding by going to the mosque (with the foot), not just verbal response. The preferred Hanafi position is that verbal response is recommended, not obligatory, and the hearer should avoid speech during the adhan. The passage ends with a discussion of the historical context of minarets and the early practice of Bilal (RA).

Key Terms
أذان (adhan): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases, a sunnah muakkadah for the five daily prayers and the Friday prayer.
إقامة (iqama): The second call that indicates the prayer is about to begin, similar to adhan but shorter and with some differences.
موالاة (muwalat): Continuity; in adhan and iqama, the phrases should be recited without significant interruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what is the ruling on facing the qibla during the adhan?
A) It is fard; omitting it invalidates the adhan.
B) It is sunnah; leaving it is makruh tanzihi.
C) It is mustahab; leaving it is not disliked.
D) It is haram to face away.

Key Takeaway
Facing qibla, turning at hayya, and refraining from speech are sunan of adhan; responding verbally is a virtue, not an obligation.

Responding to the Adhan: Obligation by Tongue or Foot?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on response to adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on responding to the adhan and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between them.

Core Idea
The obligation to respond to the adhan is twofold: by tongue and by foot; scholars differ on which is primary.

The adhan calls believers to prayer, but how should they respond? This lesson examines a classical Hanafi debate on whether the response is by repeating the mu'adhdhin's words or by physically proceeding to the mosque. Understanding this dispute clarifies the correct action upon hearing the adhan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Within the Hanafi school, some scholars (like al-Hulwani) hold that response is only by foot (going to the mosque). The majority hold that response is by both tongue (repeating words) and foot, with the obligation of foot linked to congregational prayer.
This is an intra-madhhab dispute, not between schools.
2
Examine the evidence for each
The majority relies on the hadith 'When you hear the mu'adhdhin, say the like of what he says' – command indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. Al-Hulwani interprets 'whoever does not respond to the adhan, no prayer for him' as referring to foot (going to the mosque).
Both sides use hadith evidence; the difference is in interpretation (wajh al-dalalah).
3
Note the practical difference
If a man hears the adhan while at home, according to al-Hulwani he must go to the mosque (response by foot) but need not repeat the words. According to the majority, he must both repeat the words and go. If he is reciting Quran, the majority says he stops for the response; al-Hulwani says he only stops if he intends to go.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf – the concrete difference in practice.
4
Understand the reconciliation
Later Hanafi scholars like Ibn Nujaym attempt to reconcile by noting that the obligation to go to the mosque arises from the obligation of congregational prayer, which is itself indicated by the adhan. Thus, both obligations are fulfilled by going at the adhan time.
The author points to the issue of repeating congregation in a mosque as a related concern.

And in al-Khulasa: Whoever hears the adhan, it is incumbent upon him to respond even if he is junub, because responding to the mu'adhdhin is not adhan. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: Responding to the mu'adhdhin is a virtue; if one abandons it he does not sin. As for his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever does not respond to the adhan, there is no prayer for him,' its meaning is response by the foot, not by the tongue alone. And in al-Muhit: It is obligatory upon the hearer of the adhan to respond, and he says instead of 'Hayya 'ala al-salah': 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah', and instead of 'Hayya 'ala al-falah': 'Masha Allahu kana wa ma lam yasha' lam yakun', because repeating it resembles mockery since it is not tasbih nor tahlil. Likewise, when he says 'Al-salat khayr min al-nawm', he says 'Sadaqta wa barirta'. The hearer does not recite, does not greet, does not return the greeting, and does not occupy himself with anything other than the response. (Marginal note?) His statement: (In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: he does not turn...) He said in al-Nahr al-Thani: the most balanced of sayings. His statement: (There was no minaret in his time...) He said in Sharh al-Durar wa al-Ghurar: and in the beginning of al-Suyuti that the first to ascend a minaret for adhan was Shurahbil ibn 'Amir al-Muradi, and in his tenure the sons of Salamah built minarets for adhan by order of Mu'awiyah, and they were not before. And Ibn Sa'd narrated with chain from Umm Zayd ibn Thabit: My house was the tallest house around the mosque, so Bilal gave the adhan from it from the first time he gave the adhan until the Messenger of Allah built, so he gave the adhan afterwards from the roof of the mosque and something was raised for him above the roof. His statement: (And al-Hulwani said...) He said in al-Nahr: I say: It should not be obligatory by tongue unanimously according to the Imam's statement regarding the adhan before the khatib, and it is obligatory by foot unanimously in the first adhan of Friday when he is not in the mosque. And by tongue also according to the first, except if it is said that the obligatory is only the going (sa'y), not responding to the mu'adhdhin. The effect of the difference appears in the case of one who hears the adhan while reciting: he stops reciting according to the first for the response, not according to the second. And it is explicit in al-Muhit and al-Tuhfa that according to the first he does not greet nor occupy himself with anything other than the response, which is explicit in the dislike of talking during the adhan. As for what is in al-Tanjis that it is not disliked by consensus, using as evidence their difference on its dislike during the adhan of the khutbah, because the Imam only disliked it to connect this situation to the situation of the khutbah, so this... Heard the adhan: even if the hearer is reciting, he stops reciting and responds. And al-Hulwani said: The response is by the foot, not by the tongue, so that if he responds by tongue and does not walk to the mosque, he is not considered responding. And if he is in the mosque, then there is no response upon him. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If a man is in the mosque reciting the Quran and hears the adhan, he does not leave off recitation because he is responding by being present. But if he is in his house, he leaves off recitation and responds. Perhaps this branches off from al-Hulwani's statement. And the apparent view is that response by tongue is obligatory because of the apparent command in his saying, peace be upon him: 'When you hear the mu'adhdhin, say the like of what he says' since no contextual indicator diverts it; rather, the dislike of abandoning it appears. And in Sharh al-Niqayah: Whoever hears, there is no harm in his occupying himself with supplication during both. And in Fath al-Qadir: Responding to the iqamah is recommended. And in what resembles the iqamah, he does not respond. That it is not disliked in other than this case is prevented. Know that al-Hulwani's statement of the obligation of response by foot is problematic, because it would necessitate the obligation of performing prayer at the beginning of the time and in the mosque, since there is no meaning to obligating going without prayer. And what is in Shihadat al-Muhtabi: He heard the adhan and waited for the iqamah in his house, his testimony is not accepted, is built upon his statement, as is not hidden. I asked our esteemed teacher about this and he did not give an answer. And it can be answered that this is based on what was in the time of the Salaf: only one congregational prayer and no repetition, as in his time (the Prophet's) he would pray with his companions. So if one lagged behind, he would miss the congregation. And it will come that the preponderant view in the madhhab is that congregation is obligatory, so one must go to it at its time, and that is indicated by the adhan, just as going on Friday is obligated by the adhan for the sake of prayer, not for itself. So reflect on that, perhaps it will achieve reconciliation between the two views. This is supported by what will come: that repeating congregation in one mosque is disliked. He said in Sharh al-Durar wa al-Ghurar: In al-Kafi, congregation is not repeated. And al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible, as in the mosque on the thoroughfare. Our proof: We are commanded to increase the congregation, and repeating congregation in one mosque reduces it, because if they know that they will miss the congregation, they hasten to attend, so the congregation increases. In al-Miftah: If a group enters a mosque whose people have already prayed, it is disliked for them to pray in congregation with adhan and iqamah, but they pray individually without adhan and without iqamah, because the Prophet went out to reconcile between the Ansar and appointed 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf as his deputy. He returned after he had prayed, so the Messenger of Allah entered his house and gathered his family and prayed with them with adhan and iqamah. If repeating congregation in the mosque were permissible, he would not have left praying in it, and praying in it is more virtuous. So it has become clear to you that the statement of the obligation of going by foot is apparent, because lagging behind necessitates one of two things: missing the congregation or repeating it, and both are not permissible. If you say: The implication of what I said is that the apparent view is al-Hulwani's statement, contrary to what the commentator and others here preferred. I say: No, because if he prays with his family, he has attained the virtue of congregation as he will mention there, and we will mention from al-Qunyah that it is the soundest. If you say: Thus, on this, neither of the two harms I mentioned would apply. I say: No, they do apply, because the discussion is built on al-Hulwani's statement. And it will come in the chapter on Imamate that he was asked about one who occasionally prays with his family: does he attain the reward of congregation? He said: No, and it is an innovation and disliked without excuse. We will mention there that the apparent view is that this is built on his statement of obligating response by foot, and Allah knows best. So the matter has become clear and the problem has vanished. His statement: (Say like what he says...) The apparent meaning of likeness here is similarity in mere speech, not in...
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed discussion on whether responding to the adhan is obligatory, and if so, what constitutes a proper response. It begins by citing conflicting rulings: al-Khulasa says it is obligatory (even for a junub), while Fatawa Qadikhan says it is a virtue and not sinful to leave. The famous hadith 'Whoever does not respond to the adhan, no prayer for him' is interpreted as response by going to the mosque (by foot), not just by tongue. Then al-Muhit states it is obligatory and gives specific formulas: instead of 'Hayya 'ala al-salah' say 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah', etc., because repeating the exact words would resemble mockery. The hearer should not recite, greet, or occupy himself with anything else. This leads to the position that talking during adhan is disliked. Then al-Hulwani's view is presented: response is by foot only, not by tongue; if one responds by tongue but does not go to the mosque, he has not responded. If one is already in the mosque, no response is required. The passage then presents a debate between those who hold response by tongue is obligatory (based on the command to say like the mu'adhdhin) and those who hold it is by foot. The author attempts to reconcile by noting that the obligation to go to the mosque arises from the obligation of congregational prayer, which is itself indicated by the adhan. The discussion then moves to the issue of repeating congregation in one mosque, which is disliked in the Hanafi school (unlike Shafi'i who allows it). The reasoning is that repetition reduces the number of attendees in the first congregation, as people would rely on later ones. The Prophet's own action of praying with his family at home after the congregation had finished is cited as evidence that if repeating in the mosque were fine, he would have done so. Finally, the passage concludes that the view of responding by foot (going to the mosque) is supported because missing the congregation or repeating it are both problematic. The text ends with a note on the meaning of 'like what he says' in the hadith, i.e., similarity in wording only, not in melody or volume.

Key Terms
إجابة (ijaba): Responding to the adhan, either by repeating the words (by tongue) or by going to the mosque (by foot).
تثويب (tathwib): The phrase 'as-salat khayr min al-nawm' said in the Fajr adhan.
تخفيف (takhfif): Not explicitly in chunk, but related to the concept of lightening the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hulwani, what constitutes a valid response to the adhan?
A) Repeating the words of the adhan
B) Walking to the mosque
C) Both A and B
D) Only saying 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether responding to the adhan is by tongue, foot, or both; the practical ruling is to combine both actions to be safe.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Obligation of Responding to the Adhan: Verbal or Physical?
Analyzing whether the response to adhan is verbal or by going to the mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on responding to the adhan, identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement between al-Halwani and the majority, and apply the hadith proof to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
Responding to the adhan requires both verbal repetition and physical attendance at the mosque.

When you hear the adhan, what must you do? The Hanafi school holds that responding to the call is wajib, but there is an important internal debate: is the response primarily by the tongue (repeating the words) or by the foot (going to the mosque)? This lesson examines the evidence from the hadith and the practical consequences of the different views, including the prohibition of repeating congregation in the same mosque.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is responding to the adhan. The passage states that it is wajib. The person must stop recitation and respond.
The ruling is based on the hadith command.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the hadith: 'When you hear the mu'adhdhin, say the like of what he says.' The imperative 'qulu' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is ahad, so zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'qulu' is a command; Hanafi usul holds that al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless there is a contrary indication. Here, no such indication exists, so the verbal response is wajib.
However, the purpose of the adhan is to call to congregational prayer, so physical attendance is also implied.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Halwani argues that the true response is physical (going to the mosque), not merely verbal. The majority holds that verbal response is obligatory, but both agree on the importance of attending the mosque.
The disagreement affects whether one who only repeats verbally but does not go has fulfilled the obligation.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author reconciles by stating that both are required. The physical response is the ultimate goal, supported by the ruling that repeating congregation in one mosque is makruh.
The mufta bihi is that both verbal and physical responses are emphasized.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب الأذان
سمع الأذان ولو كان السامع يقرأ يقطع القراءة ويجيب. وقال الحلواني : الإجابة بالقدم لا باللسان حتى لو أجاب باللسان ولم يمش إلى المسجد لا يكون مجيباً، ولو كان في المسجد حين ليس عليه الإجابة. وفي الظهيرية ولو كان الرجل في المسجد يقرأ القرآن فسمع الأذان لا يترك القراءة لأنه إجابة بالحضور، ولو كان في منزله يترك القراءة ويجيب، ولعله متفرع على قول الحلواني، والظاهر أن الإجابة باللسان واجبة لظاهر الأمر في قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «إذا سمعتم المؤذن فقولوا مثل ما يقول» إذ لا تظهر قرينة تصرف عنه بل ربما يظهر استنكار تركه لأنه الالتفات إليه والتشاغل عنه. وفي شرح النقاية : ومن سمع ولا بأس بأن يشتغل بالدعاء عندهما وفي فتح القدير: إن إجابة الإقامة مستحبة. وفي شهادات المحتبى: سمع الأذان وانتظر الإقامة في بيته لا تقبل شهادته مخرج على قوله كما لا يخفى، وقد سألت شيخنا الأخ عن هذا فلم يبد جواباً .اهـ. وقد يجاب بأن ذلك مبني على ما كان في زمن السلف من صلاة الجماعة مرة واحدة وعدم تكررها كما هو في زمنه فإنه هو الذي كان يصلي بأصحابه، فإذا فرع فمن تخلف تفوته الجماعة، وسيأتي أن الراجح عند أهل المذهب وجوب الجماعة فيجب السعي إليها عند وقتها وذلك بالأذان كما في السعي يوم الجمعة يجب بالأذان لأجل الصلاة لا لذاته فتأمل ذلك فلعله يحصل به التوفيق بين كل من القولين. ويؤيد هذا ما سيأتي من أن تكرار الجماعة في مسجد واحد مكروه. قال في شرح الدرر والغرر: وفي الكافي ولا تكرر جماعة. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : يجوز كما في المسجد الذي على قارعة الطريق. لنا أنا أمرنا بتكثير الجماعة وفي تكرار الجماعة في مسجد واحد تقليلها لأنهم إذا عرفوا أنهم تفوتهم الجماعة يتعجلون للحضور فتكثر الجماعة. وفي المفتاح : إذا دخل القوم مسجداً قد صلى فيه أهله كره جماعة بأذان وإقامة، ولكنهم يصلون وحداناً بغير أذان ولا إقامة لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خرج ليصلح بين الأنصار فاستخلف عبد الرحمن بن عوف رضي الله تعالى عنه فرجع بعدما صلى فدخل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بيته وجمع أهله فصلى بهم بأذان وإقامة . فلو كان يجوز إعادة الجماعة في المسجد لما ترك الصلاة فيه والصلاة فيه أفضل اهـ. فقد ظهر لك أن القول بوجوب السعي بالقدم ظاهر لأن التخلف يلزمه أحد أمرين : تفويت الجماعة أو إعادتها، وكل منهما غير جائز، فإن قلت مقتضى ما قلته أن يكون الظاهر قول الحلواني خلافاً لما استظهره الشارح هنا وغيره قلت: لا لأنه لو جمع بأهله فقد أتى بفضيلة الجماعة كما سيذكره هناك، وسنذكر عن القنية أنه الأصح. فإن قلت : فعلى هذا لا يلزم أحد المحذورين اللذين ذكرتهما قلت : لا بل يلزم لأن الكلام مبني على قول الحلواني وسيأتي في باب الإمامة أنه سأل عمن يجمع بأهله أحياناً هل ينال ثواب الجماعة قال : لا ويكون بدعة ومكروهاً بلا عذر، وسنذكر هناك أن الظاهر أن ذلك مبني على قوله بوجوب الإجابة بالقدم والله تعالى أعلم. فقد اتضح الحال وطاح الإشكال . قوله : (فقولو مثل ما يقول الخ) الظاهر أن المراد بالمماثلة ههنا المشابهة في مجرد القول لا في صفته كرفع الصوت. اهـ. سید زاده قوله : (وقد رأينا من مشايخ السلوك الخ) أقول : من كان يقول بالجمع من مشايخ السلوك سلطان العارفين سيدي محيي الدين بن العربي كما ذكره في كتابه الفتوحات المكية . قوله : (وينبغي أنه إن طال الفصل الخ) سبقه إليه من الشافعية العلامة ابن حجر رحمه الله تعالى. وبهذا ظهر أن ما في غاية البيان من أن سامع الحيعلة لا يقول مثل ما يقول المؤذن لأنه يشبه الاستهزاء وما يفعله بعض الجهلة فذاك ليس بشيء .اهـ. ليس بشيء اهـ . لأنه كيف فاعله إلى الجهل مع وروده في بعض الأحاديث والأصول تشهد له لأن عندنا المخصص الأول ما لم يكن متصلاً لا يخصص بل يعارض أو يقدم العام، وقال به بعض مشايخنا كما في الظهيرية. وفي فتح القدير : وقد رأينا من مشايخ السلوك من كان يجمع بينهما فيدعو نفسه ثم يتبرأ من الحول والقوة ليعمل بالحديثين. وفي حديث عمرو بن أبي أمامة التنصيص على أن لا يسبق المؤذن بل يعقب كل جملة منه بجملة منه اهـ. ولم أر حكم ما إذا فرغ المؤذن ولم يتابعه السامع هل يجيب بعد فراغه وينبغي أنه إن طال الفصل لا يجيب وإلا يجيب. وفي المجتبى : في ثمانية مواضع إذا الأذان لا يجيب: في الصلاة، واستماع خطبة الجمعة، وثلاث خطب الموسم والجنازة وفي تعلم العلم وتعليمه، والجماع والمستراح، وقضاء الحاجة والتغوط قال أبو حنيفة : لا يثني بلسانه. وكذا الحائض والنفساء لا يجوز أذانهما وكذا ثناؤهما .اهـ. والمراد بالثناء الإجابة وكذا لا تجب الإجابة عند سماع صوت المؤذن من المذياع ونحوه على المعتمد لأن صوت المسجل ليس بأذان حقيقة.
The Book of Prayer - Chapter of Adhan: He hears the adhan, and if the hearer is reciting, he stops recitation and responds. Al-Halwani said: The response is by the foot, not by the tongue, such that if he responds by the tongue but does not walk to the mosque, he is not considered responding. And if he was in the mosque at that time, there is no response upon him. In al-Zahira: If a man is in the mosque reciting the Quran and hears the adhan, he does not leave recitation because his presence is a response. And if he was in his home, he leaves recitation and responds. And perhaps this is derived from al-Halwani's statement. The apparent view is that the response by the tongue is obligatory due to the apparent command in his statement, peace be upon him: 'When you hear the mu'adhdhin, say the like of what he says,' as there is no contrary indication, rather it may be that leaving it is disapproved. In Sharh al-Niqaya: Whoever hears, there is no harm in engaging in supplication according to them. And in Fath al-Qadir: The response to the iqama is recommended. In al-Muqtaba: He heard the adhan and waited for the iqama in his house, his testimony is not accepted – this is based on his statement, as is clear. And I asked our shaykh about this but he gave no answer. It may be answered that this is based on what was in the time of the Salaf: congregational prayer only once and not repeated, as it was in his time. So if one lags, he misses the congregation. It will come that the preferred view in the madhhab is the obligation of congregation, so one must go to it at its time, and that is indicated by the adhan, like the need to go to Friday prayer based on the adhan, for the prayer itself, not for the adhan. This may reconcile the two views. This is supported by what will come: that repeating congregation in one mosque is disliked. In Sharh al-Durar wa al-Ghurar: In al-Kafi: Congregation is not to be repeated. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: It is permissible, as in a mosque on the main road. Our proof: We are commanded to increase the congregation, and repeating congregation in one mosque reduces it, because when people know they will miss the congregation, they hasten to attend, thus increasing the congregation. In al-Miftah: If people enter a mosque whose people have already prayed, it is disliked for them to form a congregation with adhan and iqama, but they pray individually without adhan or iqama, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, went out to reconcile between the Ansar, leaving 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf in charge. He returned after having prayed, entered his house, gathered his family, and prayed with them with adhan and iqama. If repeating congregation in the mosque were permissible, he would not have left praying in it, while praying in it is better. So it is clear that the view of obligation to go by foot is apparent, because lagging behind necessitates one of two things: missing the congregation or repeating it, and both are not permissible. If you say: what I said implies that al-Halwani's view is apparent, contrary to what the commentator and others deemed apparent. I say: No, because if he prays with his family, he has attained the virtue of congregation, as will be mentioned. We will mention from al-Qunya that it is the most correct. If you say: then on this basis, neither of the two harms you mentioned follow. I say: No, rather they follow, because the discussion is based on al-Halwani's view. It will come in the chapter of Imama that he was asked about one who occasionally prays with his family: does he attain the reward of congregation? He said: No, and it is an innovation and disliked without excuse. We will mention there that the apparent view is that this is based on his view of the obligation to respond by foot. And Allah knows best. So the matter is clear and the problem is eliminated. His statement: (Say the like of what he says, etc.): The apparent meaning of 'like' here is similarity in mere speech, not in its quality like raising the voice. Sayyid Zada: His statement: (We have seen from the shaykhs of spiritual wayfaring, etc.): I say: The one who said combination from the shaykhs of spiritual wayfaring is the Sultan of the Gnostics, Sayyidi Muhyi al-Din ibn al-'Arabi, as he mentioned in his book al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya. His statement: (It should be that if the interval is long, etc.): The 'Allamah Ibn Hajar from the Shafi'is preceded him. And by this it is clear that what is in Ghayat al-Bayan: that the hearer of the hay'ala does not say the like of what the mu'adhdhin says because it resembles mockery, and what some ignorant ones do is nothing. It is nothing, because how can its doer be ignorant when it occurs in some hadiths and principles testify for it? Because according to us, an early specificator, if not connected, does not specify, rather it is opposed or the general is given precedence. Some of our shaykhs said this, as in al-Zahira. In Fath al-Qadir: We have seen some shaykhs of spiritual wayfaring combine between them, thus calling upon himself and then disavowing power and strength to act upon both hadiths. In the hadith of 'Amr ibn Abi Umama, there is explicit text not to precede the mu'adhdhin but to follow each phrase with a phrase. I have not seen the ruling if the mu'adhdhin finishes and the hearer did not follow: does he respond after his finish? It should be that if the interval is long, he does not respond; otherwise he responds. In al-Mujtaba: In eight situations, when the adhan is heard, one does not respond: in prayer, listening to the Friday sermon, the three sermons of the season and funeral, in learning and teaching knowledge, in intercourse and the restroom, in answering the call of nature and defecation. Abu Hanifa said: He does not repeat with his tongue. Similarly, the menstruating woman and postpartum woman: their adhan is not permissible, nor is their repetition. The intended repetition is the response. Similarly, the response is not obligatory when hearing the sound of the mu'adhdhin from a radio and the like, according to the relied-upon view, because a recorded sound is not really an adhan.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rulings for a person who hears the adhan. It opens with the basic ruling: if someone is reciting the Quran and hears the adhan, he should stop reciting and respond. Then it presents a significant intra-Hanafi disagreement. Al-Halwani holds that the true response (ijabah) is physical — walking to the mosque — not merely verbal repetition. On his view, if one merely says the words but does not go to the mosque, he has not fulfilled the obligation. Conversely, if one is already in the mosque, his presence is the response, so he need not stop reciting. The author notes that the position of al-Halwani may be derived from the practice of the Salaf, where congregational prayer was held only once in each mosque. Missing it meant losing the congregation entirely. The author then argues that the apparent (zahir) view is that verbal response is obligatory, based on the Prophet's command 'say the like of what the mu'adhdhin says.' He reconciles the views by explaining that the ultimate purpose of the adhan is to call people to congregational prayer, which is itself obligatory in the Hanafi madhhab. Thus, the response by foot (going to the mosque) is essential. The passage then discusses the issue of repeating congregation in one mosque, contrasting the Hanafi position (disliked) with the Shafi'i view (allowed). The Hanafi proof is that repeating congregation reduces the number of attendees, whereas the command is to increase the congregation. The author uses the incident where the Prophet prayed at home with his family after having missed the congregational prayer in the mosque to show that it is better to pray individually at home than to form a second congregation in the mosque. This supports al-Halwani's view that one must go to the mosque. The commentary then addresses the wording of the response. The phrase 'say the like of what he says' means similar in words, not necessarily in voice quality. However, for the phrases 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah', the Hanafis prefer to say 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (hawqalah) rather than repeating the same words, based on a hadith. The author notes that some later scholars like Ibn Hajar endorse combining both responses. The passage ends by listing eight situations where one does not respond to the adhan, including prayer, Friday sermon, learning knowledge, etc. Also, the response is not obligatory when hearing a recorded adhan from a radio. Throughout, the passage maintains that the adhan is a call to prayer, and its response is both verbal and physical, with the physical aspect (attending the mosque) being the ultimate objective.

Key Terms
الإجابة (al-ijabah): The response to the adhan; whether verbal repetition or physical attendance at the mosque.
الأذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases announcing the time for salah.
الحوقلة (al-hawqalah): Saying 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' (there is no power nor strength except with Allah) in response to 'hayya 'ala al-salah' and 'hayya 'ala al-falah'.
تكرار الجماعة (tikrar al-jama'ah): Repeating a congregational prayer in the same mosque after it has already been held once.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on repeating a congregational prayer in a mosque that has already held its congregation?
A) Permissible (ja'iz)
B) Disliked (makruh tahrimi)
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Recommended (sunnah)

Key Takeaway
Responding to the adhan requires both verbal repetition and physical attendance at the mosque; the latter is the ultimate purpose of the call.
