بغير أذان ولا إقامة لم يكره كما قدمناه، وصرح به في السراج الوهاج. فتحرر من هذا أن القضاء مخالف للأداء في الأذان لأنه يكره تركهما في القضاء ولا يكره في الأداء وكلاهما في بيته لا في المسجد، وسيأتي فيه زيادة إيضاح آخر الباب. وهل يرفع صوته بأذان الفائتة فينبغي أنه إن كان القضاء بالجماعة يرفع، وإن كان منفرداً، فإن كان كذلك في الصحراء يرفع للترغيب الوارد في الحديث في رفع صوت المؤذن «لا يسمع مدى صوت المؤذن إنس ولا جن ولا مدر إلا شهد له يوم القيامة» وإن كان في البيت لا يرفع ولم أره في كلام أئمتنا . قوله (وكذا لأولى الفوائت وخير فيه للباقي أي في الأذان إن شاء أذن وإن شاء تركه روى أبو يوسف بسنده أنه حين شغلهم الكفار يوم الأحزاب عن أربع صلوات عن الظهر والعصر والمغرب والعشاء قضاهن على الولاء وأمر بلالاً أن يؤذن ويقيم لكل والدنة منهن، ولأن القضاء على حسب الأداء. وله الترك لما عدا الأولى لأن الأذان للاستحضار وهم حضور. وعن محمد في غير رواية الأصول أن الباقي بالإقامة لا غير. قال الرازي: إنه قول الكل والمذكور في الظاهر محمول على صلاة واحدة، وهذا الحمل لا يصح لأن المذكور في ظاهر الرواية إنما هو حكم الفوائت صريحاً، فكيف يحمل على الواحدة؟ وكيف يصح مع الحمل أن يقال يؤذن لأولى الفوائت ويخير فيه للباقي؟ قيد بالفائتة احترازاً عن الفاسدة إذا أعيدت في الوقت فإنه لا يعاد الأذان ولا الإقامة ولهذا قال في المجتبى : قوم ذكروا فساد صلاة صلوها في المسجد في الوقت قضوها بجماعة فيه ولا يعيدون الأذان ولا الإقامة، وإن قضوها بعد الوقت قضوها في غير ذلك المسجد بأذان وإقامة وفي المستصفى : التخيير في الأذان للباقي، إنما هو إذا قضاها في مجلس واحد، أما إذا قضاها في مجالس فإنه يشترط كلاهما اهـ. قوله ولا يؤذن قبل وقت ويعاد فيه أي في الوقت إذا أذن قبله لأن يراد للإعلام
For the missed prayer, he performs adhan and iqamah, and likewise for the first of the missed prayers, and he has a choice regarding the remaining ones. And he does not perform adhan before the time, and it is repeated in the time. And it is disliked to differ regarding the superior. From what has been established, it is known that it is recommended to move to a different spot for iqamah than the place of adhan, and that is agreed upon. And it is known that delaying Maghrib to the extent of performing two rakats is disliked, and we have previously presented in al-Qunyah that a slight delay is not disliked, so it must be interpreted as less than that amount if he delays between them so that the statements of the scholars agree. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And the author did not mention the amount of sitting between them because it is not established in the apparent narration. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifah regarding Fajr: the amount of reciting twenty verses then he performs tathwib. And if he prays the two rakats of Fajr between the adhan and tathwib, that is good. In Zuhr, he prays four rakats between them, reciting in each rakat about ten verses, and Isha is like Zuhr. And if he does not pray, let him sit for that amount. And they did not mention here that he sits between them for the amount of gathering of the congregation, although they said: The mu'adhdhin should consider the congregation; if he sees them gathered he should give iqamah, otherwise he should wait for them. And perhaps, and Allah knows best, that the amount for this is not mentioned in the apparent narration because it is not fixed. His statement: (And he performs adhan for the missed prayer and iqamah) because adhan is sunnah for the prayer, not for the time. So if a prayer is missed, he performs its qada with adhan and iqamah, due to the hadith of Abu Dawood and others that he commanded Bilal to perform adhan and iqamah when they overslept for Fajr and prayed it after sunrise. And that is the correct view in the Shafi'i school as mentioned by al-Nawawi in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab. And because qada resembles the original performance; for this reason the imam recites loudly if it is a loud prayer, otherwise softly. And the commentator mentioned that the rule with us is: every prayer, whether performed on time or qada, adhan and iqamah are given for it, whether performed individually or in congregation, except Zuhr on Friday in a large city, for its performance with adhan and iqamah is disliked; that is narrated from Ali. And it is excepted also, as in al-Fath, what women perform or their congregation performs as qada, because Aisha used to lead them without adhan or iqamah when their congregation was legitimate. This implies that the individual woman is also the same, because leaving them when the congregation is legitimate is sunnah, so when alone it is more appropriate. He gave it absolutely, so it includes whether he performs qada in his house or in the mosque. And in al-Mujtaba, attributed to al-Halwani: It is sunnah to perform qada in houses, not in mosques, because it causes confusion and error. And if they have stated that the missed prayer is not performed as qada in the mosque because of showing laziness in taking the prayer out of its time, and concealment is obligatory, then adhan for the missed prayer in the mosque is more deserving of prohibition. And the ruling of adhan for time-based prayers is known from his statement at the beginning of the chapter: sunnah for obligatory prayers, and it will come at the end of the chapter that it is not disliked to leave them for one who prays in his house. So it is established that the sunnah in performance is only when he prays in a mosque, whether in congregation or individually, or not. And upon this is based the commentator's earlier statement. Thus his statement 'and he performs adhan for the missed prayer' excludes the time-based prayer, because if he prays it in his house without adhan and iqamah, it is not disliked, as we previously mentioned, and it is explicitly stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. It becomes clear from this that qada is different from performance regarding adhan, because it is disliked to leave them in qada but not disliked in performance, and both are in his house, not in the mosque. And further clarification will come at the end of the chapter. And should he raise his voice in the adhan for the missed prayer? It should be that if the qada is in congregation, he raises it; if alone, then if in the desert he raises it due to the encouragement in the hadith about raising the voice of the mu'adhdhin: 'No human, jinn, or anything hears the voice of the mu'adhdhin except that it will bear witness for him on the Day of Judgment'; and if in the house, he does not raise it, and I have not seen this in the words of our imams. His statement: (And likewise for the first of the missed prayers, and he has a choice regarding the remaining) i.e. regarding adhan, if he wishes he performs adhan, if he wishes he leaves it. Abu Yusuf narrated with his chain that when the disbelievers on the Day of Ahzab occupied them from four prayers—Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha—he performed them in order and commanded Bilal to perform adhan and iqamah for each of them. And because qada is according to performance. And he has the option to leave for others besides the first, because adhan is for summoning, and they are present. And from Muhammad, in non-principle narrations, that for the remaining, only iqamah, nothing else. Al-Razi said: That is the saying of everyone, and what is mentioned in the apparent (narration) is applied to a single prayer. But this application is not valid because what is mentioned in the apparent narration is explicitly the ruling of multiple missed prayers. So how can it be applied to one? And how can it be correct with the application to say: he performs adhan for the first of the missed prayers and is given a choice for the rest? He restricted it to the missed prayer to exclude the invalid prayer when repeated within its time, for adhan and iqamah are not repeated. For this reason it is said in al-Mujtaba: A group mentioned that they performed a prayer in the mosque within its time and then discovered it was invalid; they performed qada in congregation in it, and they do not repeat the adhan and iqamah. And if they perform qada after the time, they perform qada in a different mosque with adhan and iqamah. And in al-Mustasfa: The choice regarding adhan for the remaining applies only if he performs qada in one sitting; if he performs it in multiple sittings, then both (adhan and iqamah) are required. His statement: (And he does not perform adhan before the time, and it is repeated in the time) i.e. within the time if he performed adhan before it, because it is meant for notification.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings of adhan for missed prayers (fawa'it). The author begins by stating the core ruling: for a missed prayer, one should give both adhan and iqamah. This is because adhan is sunnah for the prayer itself, not for its time, as established by the hadith of the Prophet commanding Bilal to give adhan and iqamah when they missed Fajr. The passage then addresses the case of multiple missed prayers: the first must be given adhan and iqamah, but for the subsequent ones, there is a choice—one may give adhan or not. This is based on the practice of the Prophet during the Battle of the Trench, as narrated by Abu Yusuf, where he ordered Bilal to give adhan and iqamah for each of the four missed prayers. However, Imam Muhammad, in non-principle narrations, holds that only iqamah is needed for the remaining prayers. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that choice exists, as stated in the text. Next, the passage rules that adhan cannot be given before the time of a prayer; if it is, it must be repeated within the proper time. The commentary also discusses related issues: the recommended pause between adhan and iqamah, the dislike of delaying Maghrib, and exceptions for women and for prayers performed in the house. A key point is that for a missed prayer performed in the mosque, adhan is given, but this is not the case for a time-based prayer performed at home, where leaving both adhan and iqamah is not disliked. The passage ends with a discussion on raising the voice for adhan of missed prayers.

Key Terms
الأذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases, used to announce the time of prayer and summon the congregation.
الإقامة (al-iqamah): The second call to prayer, shorter than adhan, given just before the prayer begins.
الفائتة (al-faytah): A missed obligatory prayer that must be made up (qada).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for adhan for the second of three missed prayers made up in order?
A) Adhan is wajib.
B) Adhan is sunnah muakkadah with no choice.
C) There is a choice: one may give adhan or not.
D) Adhan is makruh.

Key Takeaway
Adhan for missed prayers is sunnah; the first prayer requires it, but for subsequent ones in one sitting, you may choose to give adhan or not, based on the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Adhan for the First Missed Prayer: Wajib, Optional for Subsequent Ones
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on adhan when making up multiple missed prayers and explain the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Adhan for the first of multiple qada prayers is wajib; for the rest, it is optional.

When you have missed several prayers and need to make them up, do you need to call adhan for each one? The Hanafi school teaches that adhan is required for the first missed prayer, but you have a choice for the rest. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence from the Prophet's practice, and an intra-Hanafi difference of opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the adhan for the first of multiple missed prayers. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory), based on the matn.
The matn explicitly says 'for the first' and uses the term 'likewise' connecting to a previous ruling.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a narration from Abu Yusuf about the day of al-Ahzab when the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered Bilal to give adhan and iqamah for each of the four missed prayers.
This is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit command to Bilal indicates obligation (wujub) for adhan in qada in general. However, the matn restricts this to the first prayer only, based on the reason that adhan is for summoning and the congregation is already present for subsequent prayers.
The restriction is derived from the underlying rationale (ta'lil).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad (in a non-usul narration) holds that for the rest, only iqamah is sufficient. Al-Razi attempted to reinterpret the ruling as referring to a single prayer, but the author refutes this.
The mufta bihi position is the matn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وكذا لأولى الفوائت وخير فيه للباقي أي في الأذان إن شاء أذن وإن شاء تركه روى أبو يوسف بسنده أنه حين شغلهم الكفار يوم الأحزاب عن أربع صلوات عن الظهر والعصر والمغرب والعشاء قضاهن على الولاء وأمر بلالاً أن يؤذن ويقيم لكل والدنة منهن، ولأن القضاء على حسب الأداء. وله الترك لما عدا الأولى لأن الأذان للاستحضار وهم حضور. وعن محمد في غير رواية الأصول أن الباقي بالإقامة لا غير. قال الرازي: إنه قول الكل والمذكور في الظاهر محمول على صلاة واحدة، وهذا الحمل لا يصح لأن المذكور في ظاهر الرواية إنما هو حكم الفوائت صريحاً، فكيف يحمل على الواحدة؟ وكيف يصح مع الحمل أن يقال يؤذن لأولى الفوائت ويخير فيه للباقي؟ قيد بالفائتة احترازاً عن الفاسدة إذا أعيدت في الوقت فإنه لا يعاد الأذان ولا الإقامة ولهذا قال في المجتبى : قوم ذكروا فساد صلاة صلوها في المسجد في الوقت قضوها بجماعة فيه ولا يعيدون الأذان ولا الإقامة، وإن قضوها بعد الوقت قضوها في غير ذلك المسجد بأذان وإقامة وفي المستصفى : التخيير في الأذان للباقي، إنما هو إذا قضاها في مجلس واحد، أما إذا قضاها في مجالس فإنه يشترط كلاهما اهـ.
His statement: 'And likewise for the first of the missed prayers, and there is a choice for the rest' means regarding the adhan: if he wishes he may give adhan, and if he wishes he may omit it. Abu Yusuf narrated with his chain that when the disbelievers occupied them on the day of al-Ahzab from four prayers—Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha—he (the Prophet) made them up in order and commanded Bilal to give adhan and iqamah for each of them. And because making up is according to the manner of performing on time. And he may omit for other than the first because adhan is for summoning, and they are already present. And from Muhammad in non-usul narrations: for the rest, only iqamah is sufficient. Al-Razi said: It is the saying of all, and what is mentioned in the apparent (narration) is interpreted as one prayer, but this interpretation is invalid because what is mentioned in the apparent narration is explicitly the ruling of missed prayers, so how can it be interpreted as one? And how can it be correct with this interpretation to say: he gives adhan for the first missed prayer and has a choice for the rest? It is restricted to missed prayer as a precaution against the invalid (prayer) when repeated within the time, for then adhan and iqamah are not repeated. For this reason it is said in al-Mujtaba: People who mentioned the invalidity of a prayer they performed in the mosque within the time, they make it up in congregation there and do not repeat the adhan or iqamah. And if they make it up after the time, they make it up in a different mosque with adhan and iqamah. And in al-Mustasfa: The choice for adhan for the rest is only when he makes them up in one sitting; if he makes them up in separate sittings, then both (adhan and iqamah) are required. End.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase regarding adhan for missed prayers. The author explains that for the first missed prayer when making up multiple missed prayers, adhan is required (according to the narration of Abu Yusuf from the Prophet's practice on the day of al-Ahzab), but for the subsequent ones, there is a choice: one may either give adhan or omit it. This choice is based on the fact that adhan is for summoning people, and if they are already present, it's not needed. There is also a narration from Imam Muhammad (in non-usul sources) that only iqamah is needed for the rest. The author refutes a misinterpretation that the ruling applies only to one prayer. He then distinguishes between making up a prayer that became invalid during its time (no need to repeat adhan) and making up a missed prayer after its time (adhan and iqamah are required). Finally, he notes that the choice for adhan for subsequent prayers applies only if all missed prayers are performed in one session; if performed separately, each requires both adhan and iqamah.

Key Terms
فائتة (fā'itah): A missed obligatory prayer that is to be made up after its time.
قضاء (qaḍā'): Making up an obligatory act of worship (here, prayer) after its prescribed time has passed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When making up multiple missed prayers in one sitting, what is the ruling on adhan for the first prayer?
A) Adhan is not required for any of them
B) Adhan is required for the first prayer and optional for the rest
C) Adhan is required for all four prayers
D) Only iqamah is required, no adhan

Key Takeaway
Adhan is wajib for the first missed prayer when making up multiple, but optional for the rest—a ruling derived from the Prophet's practice and rationalized by the purpose of adhan.

Exceptions: Making Up Invalid Prayers and Separate Sittings
Exceptions and nuances of the ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between making up a missed prayer and repeating an invalid prayer, and explain the effect of separate sittings on the adhan obligation.

Core Idea
Making up an invalid prayer within its time requires no adhan; making up a missed prayer in separate sittings requires adhan for each.

The general ruling on adhan for missed prayers has two important exceptions. First, if a prayer becomes invalid and is repeated within the same time, no adhan or iqamah is repeated. Second, if missed prayers are made up in multiple sessions, each session's first prayer requires adhan. This lesson clarifies these nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first exception: fasad within time
If a prayer becomes invalid (fasad) and is repeated within the same prescribed time, the adhan and iqamah are not repeated. The source quotes al-Mujtaba.
This is because the original adhan still serves the time.
2
Identify the second exception: after time
If the invalid prayer is made up after its time, it is treated as a missed prayer: adhan and iqamah are required, and it should be done in a different mosque.
This is to avoid confusion with the original congregation.
3
Identify the third nuance: separate sittings
The choice for adhan for subsequent prayers in a single sitting only applies if all missed prayers are made up in one sitting. If they are in separate sittings (majalis), each sitting's first prayer requires both adhan and iqamah.
Source: al-Mustasfa.

Source Text

Adhan for Fajr Before Dawn: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on adhan for Fajr before dawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on adhan for Fajr before dawn, identify the proofs for each, and apply the ruling to determine when adhan must be repeated.

Core Idea
Adhan for Fajr before dawn is prohibited by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf allows it after midnight.

The timing of adhan for Fajr is a matter of intra-Hanafi disagreement. While the general rule is that adhan must be given within the prayer time, Fajr is an exception where there is a well-known ikhtilaf. This lesson examines the positions of the three leading Hanafi imams, their respective proofs, and how this dispute affects practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the two views: (1) Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that adhan before dawn for Fajr is not permissible (haram). (2) Abu Yusuf holds it is permissible after midnight and sunnah to have two adhans.
The matn (zahir al-riwayah) follows Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
2
Identify the evidence for Abu Yusuf's view
Examine the hadith of Bilal from the Sahihayn: "Indeed Bilal gives adhan at night, so eat and drink until Ibn Umm Maktum gives adhan." This seems to allow an early adhan.
Also, Abu Yusuf's view aligns with Malik and al-Shafi'i.
3
Analyze the evidence for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
Look at the hadith from al-Bayhaqi: "O Bilal, do not give adhan until dawn breaks." Also the hadith in Muslim about the Prophet praying Fajr sunnah after hearing adhan, implying adhan is at dawn.
They interpret Bilal's practice as an error or a special Ramadan reminder.
4
Examine the Hanafi response and interpretation
Understand how Abu Hanifa and Muhammad reinterpret the Bilal hadith: it was a special case for suhur in Ramadan, or a warning not to rely on Bilal's timing. The command in the Bayhaqi hadith is taken as prohibitive.
The author also explains the practice of 'tasbih' (reminder) before Fajr.
5
Determine the practical implications
The thamarah al-khilaf: If adhan is given before dawn, it must be repeated in the time. Also, iqamah before time is void. If iqamah is given and there is a delay, a long gap invalidates it; a short gap does not.
The mufta bihi position is that adhan should not be given before dawn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولا يؤذن قبل وقت ويعاد فيه أي في الوقت إذا أذن قبله لأن يراد للإعلام فلا يجوز قبله بلا خلاف في غير الفجر. وعبر بالكراهة في فتح القدير والظاهر أنها تحريمية. وأما فيه فجوزه أبو يوسف ومالك والشافعي لحديث الصحيحين «إن بلالاً يؤذن بليل فكلوا واشربوا حتى يؤذن ابن أم مكتوم». ووقته عند أبي يوسف بعد ذهاب نصف الليل وهو الصحيح في مذهب الشافعي كما ذكره النووي في شرح المهذب. والسنة عنده أن يؤذن للصبح مرتين : إحداهما قبل الفجر والأخرى عقب طلوعه. ولم أره لأبي يوسف. وعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لا يؤذن في الفجر قبله لما رواه البيهقي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال : يا بلال لا تؤذن حتى يطلع الفجر . قال في الإمام رجال إسناده ثقات. ولرواية مسلم : كان النبي يصلي ركعتي الفجر إذا سمع الأذان ويخففهما. ويحمل ما رووه على أن معناه لا تعتمدوا على أذانه فإنه يخطىء فيؤذن بليل تحريضاً له على الاحتراس عن مثله. وأما أن المراد بالاذان التسعير بناء على أن هذا إنما كان في رمضان كما قاله في الإمام فلذا قال «فكلوا واشربوا»، والتذكير المسمى في هذا الزمان بالتسبيح ليوقظ النائم ويرجع القائم كما قيل إن الصحابة كانوا خربين خربا مجتهدون في النصف الأول وخربا في الأخير، وكان الفاصل عندهم أذان بلال يدل عليه ما روي عنه عليه السلام لا يمنعكم من سحوركم أذان بلال فإنه يؤذن ليوقظ نائمكم ويرقد قائمكم فلو أوقع بعض كلمات الأذان قبل الوقت وبعضها في الوقت فينبغي أن لا وعليه استئناف الأذان كله وفهم من كلامه أن الإقامة قبل الوقت لا تصح بالأولى كما صرح به ابن الملك في شرح المجمع، وأنه متفق عليه لكن بقي الكلام فيما إذا قام في الوقت ولم يصل على فوره هل تبطل إقامته؟ لم أره في كلام أئمتنا، وينبغي أنه إن طال الفصل تبطل وإلا فلا. ثم رأيت بعد ذلك في القنية : حضر الإمام بعد إقامة المؤذن بساعة أو صلى سنة الفجر بعدها لا يجب عليه أعادتها اهـ.
His statement: 'And he should not give adhan before the time, and it is repeated within it' i.e., within the time if he gave adhan before it, because it is intended for notification. So it is not permissible before the time without disagreement except for Fajr. And it is expressed with dislike in Fath al-Qadir, and apparently it is prohibitive dislike. As for Fajr, Abu Yusuf, Malik, and al-Shafi'i allowed it due to the hadith in the two Sahihs: 'Indeed Bilal gives adhan at night, so eat and drink until Ibn Umm Maktum gives adhan.' And its time according to Abu Yusuf is after half the night has passed, and this is the correct view in the Shafi'i school as mentioned by al-Nawawi in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab. And according to him, the sunnah is to give adhan for Fajr twice: one before dawn and the other after its rising. But I have not seen this from Abu Yusuf. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, one should not give adhan for Fajr before its time, due to what al-Bayhaqi narrated: that the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'O Bilal, do not give adhan until dawn breaks.' He said in al-Imam: its chain is trustworthy. And due to the narration of Muslim: 'The Prophet used to pray the two rak'ahs of Fajr when he heard the adhan and would make them light.' And they interpret what they narrated to mean: do not rely on his adhan, for he errs and gives adhan at night, as a warning to be careful of the like. And that what is meant by adhan is the call to eat, based on the fact that this was only in Ramadan as he said in al-Imam, so he said 'so eat and drink'. And the reminder called in this time 'tasbih' is to wake the sleeper and return the one standing, as it is said the companions were two groups: a group striving in the first half and a group in the latter half, and the dividing line among them was Bilal's adhan. This is indicated by what is narrated from him (peace be upon him): 'Do not let Bilal's adhan prevent you from your suhur, for he gives adhan to wake your sleeper and to return your one standing.' So if some words of the adhan occur before the time and some within the time, it should be that the entire adhan must be restarted. And it is understood from his statement that iqamah before the time is not valid a fortiori, as Ibn al-Malik stated in Sharh al-Majma', and this is agreed upon. But there remains a discussion: if one gives iqamah at the time and does not pray immediately, does his iqamah become invalid? I have not seen this in the statements of our imams. It seems that if the gap is long, it becomes invalid; otherwise not. Then I saw after that in al-Qunya: If the imam arrives an hour after the mu'adhdhin's iqamah, or prays the sunnah of Fajr after it, it is not obligatory for him to repeat it. End.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of giving adhan before the time for Fajr prayer. The matn states that adhan should not be given before the time, but if given, it must be repeated in the time. This is general except for Fajr, where there is ikhtilaf. For other salahs, it is unanimously impermissible. Abu Yusuf allowed adhan for Fajr before dawn, citing the hadith that Bilal used to give adhan at night. According to Abu Yusuf, the time for this adhan is after midnight, and the sunnah is to have two adhans for Fajr: one before dawn and one after. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad prohibit adhan before dawn, relying on other hadiths (from al-Bayhaqi and Muslim) that indicate the adhan should only be given at dawn. They explain away Bilal's practice as an error or a special reminder during Ramadan. The author also discusses a scenario where some words of adhan occur before time and some in time: the entire adhan must be repeated. Similarly, iqamah before time is void. Finally, he addresses a practical question: if iqamah is given and then there is a delay, does the iqamah need to be repeated? He suggests that a long delay invalidates it, but a short one does not, and cites a ruling from al-Qunya that if the imam arrives an hour later, the iqamah need not be repeated.

Key Terms
أذان (adhān): The call to prayer, which is sunnah mu'akkadah for the five daily prayers and wajib for the first of multiple qada prayers.
إقامة (iqāmah): The second call immediately before the prayer, which is sunnah mu'akkadah.
تسبيح (tasbīḥ): A reminder call (similar to adhan) used to wake people for suhur or to indicate the approach of Fajr; not a formal adhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on giving adhan for Fajr before dawn?
A) Permissible after midnight
B) Sunnah to give it twice
C) Not permissible until dawn
D) Only iqamah is required

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that adhan for Fajr should not be given before dawn; the hadith of Bilal is interpreted as a special case for Ramadan.

Timing of the Fajr Adhan and the Ikhtilaf
Dispute on adhan before Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on giving the adhan for Fajr before dawn, identify the opposing proofs, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Giving adhan before Fajr is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf allows it after midnight.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi (and inter-madhhab) dispute: may the adhan for Fajr be given before dawn? The matn states that adhan before the time is prohibited except for Fajr, where there is a difference. We will dissect the proofs from both sides and see how the Hanafi school reconciles the conflicting hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The matn says adhan is not permissible before the time without dispute except for Fajr. This gives the general rule and the exception.
The exception signals the dispute.
2
Contrast the two positions
Abu Yusuf (with Malik and al-Shafi'i) permit adhan before Fajr, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad prohibit it. Each side has a proof.
Remember Abu Yusuf's position is within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad use the hadith 'La tu'adhdhin hatta yatla'a al-fajr' (Do not give adhan until dawn). This is a direct command.
Also the hadith that the Prophet prayed sunnah after hearing the adhan, indicating adhan was after dawn.
4
Analyze the opposing dalil
The other side cites the sahih hadith that Bilal would give adhan at night. Abu Yusuf interprets it as a valid adhan for suhur and allows it after midnight.
The Hanafi response reinterprets this as a reminder for suhur, not a prayer adhan.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, the Hanafi relied-upon position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) leads to one adhan after dawn. Abu Yusuf's view leads to two adhans.
This affects the practice of mosques in some regions.

كتاب الصلاة - باب الأذان بالوقت فلا يجوز قبله بلا خلاف في غير الفجر. وعبر بالكراهة في فتح القدير والظاهر أنها تحريمية، وأما فيه فجوزه أبو يوسف ومالك والشافعي لحديث الصحيحين «إن بلالاً يؤذن بليل فكلوا واشربوا حتى يؤذن ابن أم مكتوم» . (۱) ووقته عند أبي يوسف بعد ذهاب نصف الليل وهو الصحيح في مذهب الشافعي كما ذكره النووي في شرح المهذب. والسنة عنده أن يؤذن للصبح مرتين : إحداهما قبل الفجر والأخرى عقب طلوعه. ولم أره لأبي يوسف. وعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لا يؤذن في الفجر قبله لما رواه البيهقي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال : يا بلال لا تؤذن حتى يطلع الفجر . قال في الإمام رجال إسناده ثقات. ولرواية مسلم : كان النبي يصلي ركعتي الفجر إذا سمع الأذان ويخففهما. ويحمل ما رووه على أن معناه لا تعتمدوا على أذانه فإنه يخطىء فيؤذن بليل تحريضاً له على الاحتراس عن مثله. وأما أن المراد بالاذان التسعير بناء على أن هذا إنما كان في رمضان كما قاله في الإمام فلذا قال «فكلوا واشربوا»، والتذكير المسمى في هذا الزمان بالتسبيح ليوقظ النائم ويرجع القائم كما قيل إن الصحابة كانوا خربين خربا مجتهدون في النصف الأول وخربا في الأخير، وكان الفاصل عندهم أذان بلال يدل عليه ما روي عنه عليه السلام لا يمنعكم من سحوركم أذان بلال فإنه يؤذن ليوقظ نائمكم ويرقد قائمكم فلو أوقع بعض كلمات الأذان قبل الوقت وبعضها في الوقت فينبغي أن لا وعليه استئناف الأذان كله وفهم من كلامه أن الإقامة قبل يصح الوقت لا تصح بالأولى كما صرح به ابن الملك في شرح المجمع، وأنه متفق عليه لكن بقي الكلام فيما إذا قام في الوقت ولم يصل على فوره هل تبطل إقامته؟ لم أره في كلام أئمتنا، وينبغي أنه إن طال الفصل تبطل وإلا فلا. ثم رأيت بعد ذلك في القنية : حضر الإمام بعد إقامة المؤذن بساعة أو صلى سنة الفجر بعدها لا يجب عليه أعادتها اهـ. وفي المجتبى معزياً إلى بغير مسجد فتأمل. قوله : (وأما فيه الخ) أي في الفجر . قوله : ( ويحمل ما رووه الخ) قال في العناية : فإن قيل جاء في الحديث لا يغرنكم أذان بلال ويعلم به أنه كان يؤذن قبل الوقت، أجيب بأنه حجة لنا حيث لم يعتبر النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم أذانه ونهاهم عن الاغترار به واعتباره . وقد ذكر في المبسوط أن أذان بلال أنكره عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأمره أن ينادي على نفسه «ألا أن العبد قد نام يعني نفسه أي أنه أذن في حال النوم والغفلة وكان يبكي ويطوف حول المدينة ويقول : ليت بلالاً لم تلده أمه . وابتل من نضح دم جبينه. وإنما قال ذلك لكثرة معاتبة رسول الله إياه .اهـ. قوله : (وينبغي أنه إن طال الفصل تبطل وإلا فلا) تابعه في النهر فقال : Book of Prayer - Chapter of the Adhan: By time, it is not permissible before it without dispute except for Fajr. And he expressed it as dislike in Fath al-Qadir, and the apparent meaning is that it is prohibitory. As for it (Fajr), Abu Yusuf, Malik, and al-Shafi'i permitted it due to the hadith in the two Sahihs: 'Bilal gives the adhan at night, so eat and drink until Ibn Umm Maktum gives the adhan.' Its time according to Abu Yusuf is after half the night has passed, and this is the correct view in the Shafi'i school as mentioned by al-Nawawi in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab. According to him, the Sunnah is to give the adhan for Fajr twice: one before dawn and another after its rising. I have not seen this for Abu Yusuf. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, he should not give the adhan for Fajr before its time because al-Bayhaqi narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'O Bilal, do not give the adhan until dawn appears.' He said in al-Imam: its narrators are trustworthy. And according to Muslim's narration: 'The Prophet used to pray the two rak'ahs of Fajr when he heard the adhan and would make them light.' And they interpret what they narrated as meaning: 'Do not rely on his adhan because he errs and gives the adhan at night,' as an exhortation for him to be cautious. As for the meaning of 'adhan' here being for the pre-dawn meal (suhur), based on the fact that this was only in Ramadan as he said in al-Imam, therefore he said: 'Eat and drink.' And the reminder called in this time 'tasbih' is to wake the sleeper and cause the one standing in prayer to return, as it is said that the Companions used to be ... The dividing point for them was Bilal's adhan, as indicated by the narration from him (peace be upon him): 'Do not let Bilal's adhan prevent you from your suhur, for he gives the adhan to wake your sleeper and cause your one standing in prayer to return.' So if he pronounces some words of the adhan before the time and some within the time, then it is not... and he must repeat the entire adhan. And it is understood from his words that the iqamah before the time is not valid, as stated by Ibn al-Malak in Sharh al-Majma', and it is agreed upon. But the discussion remains: if he performs the iqamah within the time and does not pray immediately, does his iqamah become invalid? I have not seen this in the words of our imams. It would be appropriate that if the interval is long, it becomes invalid; otherwise not. Then after that I saw in al-Qunyah: 'If the imam arrives an hour after the mu'adhdhin's iqamah or prays the Sunnah of Fajr after it, it is not obligatory for him to repeat it.' And in al-Mujtaba, attributed to 'without a mosque', so ponder. His statement: (As for it, etc.) meaning in Fajr. His statement: (And they interpret what they narrated, etc.) He said in al-'Inayah: If it is said: The hadith 'Do not be deceived by Bilal's adhan' indicates that he used to give the adhan before time, the answer is that it is an argument for us because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not consider his adhan valid and forbade them from being deceived by it and considering it. And it is mentioned in al-Mabsut that Bilal's adhan was rejected by the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and he commanded him to announce over himself: 'Indeed the servant has slept,' meaning himself, that he gave the adhan in a state of sleep and heedlessness, and he used to weep and circle the city saying: 'Would that Bilal's mother had not given birth to him.' And he was tested by the dripping of blood from his forehead. He only said that due to the frequent reproach of the Messenger of Allah to him. His statement: (It would be appropriate that if the interval is long, it becomes invalid; otherwise not) He followed him in al-Nahr and said: The apparent meaning of what is in al-Qunyah is that it is not repeated, but it would be appropriate that if the interval is long or there occurs something that is considered a break, like eating and the like. I say: And likewise the apparent meaning of what preceded from al-Mujtaba in...
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the ruling of giving the adhan before the time of prayer, specifically for Fajr. The matn states that it is not permissible before the time without any dispute except for the Fajr prayer. For Fajr, there is a difference of opinion. The author notes that in Fath al-Qadir, it is expressed as 'karahah' (dislike), and the apparent meaning is that it is prohibitory (tahrimi). Then he presents the dispute: Abu Yusuf, Malik, and al-Shafi'i permit the adhan before Fajr, citing the hadith in the two Sahihs that Bilal used to give the adhan at night. According to Abu Yusuf, the time for this adhan is after half the night, and it is Sunnah to give two adhans for Fajr. However, the author says he has not seen this attributed to Abu Yusuf. On the other hand, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad do not permit the adhan before Fajr, relying on the hadith of al-Bayhaqi where the Prophet told Bilal not to give the adhan until dawn. They interpret the hadith of Bilal's adhan as not being an actual adhan for prayer but a reminder for suhur during Ramadan, and the Prophet's warning not to be deceived by it. The passage also discusses the case where some words of the adhan are said before the time and some within the time: the entire adhan must be repeated. It then digresses to the iqamah, mentioning that if the iqamah is given during the time but the prayer is delayed, the iqamah may become invalid if the delay is long. The commentary provides various scholarly opinions on this point. Overall, the relied upon position in the Hanafi school is that the adhan for Fajr should not be given before its time, following Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Key Terms
الاذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer announcing the entry of the prayer time.
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): A level of prohibition that is close to haram; the act is forbidden and must be avoided.
التسعير (al-tas'ir): A reminder for the pre-dawn meal (suhur) during Ramadan, calling people to eat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on giving the adhan for Fajr before dawn according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) It is Sunnah to give two adhans.
B) It is permissible but disliked.
C) It is not permissible (makruh tahrimi).
D) It is obligatory to give adhan before dawn.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the adhan for Fajr must be given after dawn; pre-dawn adhan is not valid for prayer and was only a reminder for suhur.

Salah — Prayer

Rulings on the Adhan of a Junub, Woman, Fasiq, and Others
Lists individuals whose adhan is disliked and explains the reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the adhan of a junub, woman, fasiq, sitting person, and drunk, and explain the reasoning based on istihsan and dalil.

Core Idea
The adhan of a junub is valid but disliked; the adhan of a muhdith is not disliked in the apparent narration.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the ruling on adhan given by individuals in various states: junub, woman, fasiq, sitting, drunk. The Hanafi school considers these adhans valid but disliked (makruh), with some exceptions. Understanding the underlying principles—such as the role of purity and the purpose of notification—clarifies why certain adhans are disliked and what the practical consequences are for the congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the individuals whose adhan is disliked
List the seven categories mentioned: junub (for his adhan and iqamah), person with hadath (for iqamah), woman, fasiq, sitting person (for others), drunk. Note that the adhan of a naked person is invalid.
The text says 'لا أذان المجرد' meaning the adhan of a naked person is not valid.
2
Analyze the ruling for the junub
The adhan of a junub is disliked in one narration because he calls people to something he cannot respond to (prayer). His iqamah is even more disliked. The adhan remains valid, but repetition is recommended (mustahab).
The source states 'رواية واحدة' indicating it is a weak narration but relied upon.
3
Contrast with the ruling for the muhdith
The adhan of a person with minor impurity (hadath) is not disliked in the apparent narration because adhan resembles prayer but is not prayer; only major impurity is considered. However, a hadith from al-Tirmidhi suggests otherwise, but Hanafi school uses istihsan to prefer the first view.
The hadith 'لا يؤذن إلا متوضىء' is ahad and zanni, so it can be overridden by istihsan.
4
Evaluate the ikhtilaf on iqamah of the muhdith
Some narrations say the iqamah of a muhdith is not disliked (like adhan), but the relied-upon madhhab is that it is disliked because iqamah is more connected to prayer. This is a thamarah al-khilaf affecting whether the iqamah must be repeated.
The mufta bihi is that iqamah of muhdith is makruh; repetition is not required.
5
Determine the practical consequences
If the adhan of a junub is given, the adhan and prayer are valid. Repetition of the adhan is recommended, but not obligatory. For a fasiq, woman, etc., the adhan is valid but disliked; the prayer is not affected.
The source emphasizes that the adhan of these individuals is not invalid, so no need to repeat unless recommended.

كتاب الصلاة - باب الأذان أذان الجنب وإقامته وإقامة المحدث وأذان المرأة والفاسق والقاعد والسكران لا أذان المجرد قال أبو حنيفة : يؤذن للفجر بعد طلوعه، وفي الظهر في الشتاء حين تزول الشمس، وفي الصيف يبرد، وفي العصر يؤخره ما لم يخف تغيير الشمس والعشاء يؤخر قليلاً بعد ذهاب البياض اهـ. قوله (وكره أذان الجنب وإقامته وإقامة المحدث وأذان المرأة والفاسق والقاعد والسكران) أما أذان الجنب فمكروه رواية واحدة لأنه يصير داعياً إلى ما لا يجيب إليه، وإقامته أولى بالكراهة. قيد بالجنب لأن أذان المحدث لا يكره في ظاهر الرواية وهو الصحيح لأن للأذان شبهاً بالصلاة حتى يشترط له دخول الوقت وترتيب كلماته كما ترتبت أركان الصلاة وليس هو بصلاة حقيقة فاشترط له الطهارة عن أغلظ الحدثين دون أخفهما عملاً بالشبهين (٢) وقيل : يكره لحديث الترمذي عن أبي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يؤذن إلا متوضىء» وأما إقامة المحدث فلأنها لم تشرع إلا متصلة بصلاة من يقيم ويروي عدم كراهتها كالأذان، والمذهب الأول. وأما أذان المرأة فلأنها منهية عن رفع صوتها لأنه يؤدّي إلى الفتنة، وينبغي أن يكون الخنثى كالمرأة، وأما الفاسق فلأن قوله لا يوثق به ولا يقبل في الأمور الدينية ولا يلزم أحداً . فلم يوجد الإعلام، وأما القاعد فلترك سنة الأذان من القيام أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يؤذن لنفسه فإن أذن لنفسه قاعداً فإنه لا يكره لعدم الحاجة إلى الإعلام. ويفهم منه كراهته مضطجعاً بالأولى، وأما السكران فلعدم الوثوق بقوله وهو داخل في الفاسق لكن قد يكون سكره من مباح فلا يكون فاسقاً فلذا أفرده بالذكر وأشار به إلى كراهة أذان المجنون والصبي الذي لا يعقل بالأولى لما ذكرنا ولم يتعرض المصنف لإعادة أذان من كره أذانه وفيه تفصيل؛ قالوا : يعاد أذان الجنب لا إقامته على الأشبه. كذا في الهداية وهو الأصح كما في المجتبى، لأن تكراره مشروع كما في أذان الجمعة لأنه لإعلام الغائبين فتكريره مفيد لاحتمال عدم سماع البعض بخلاف تكرار الإقامة إذ هو غير مشروع ويفهم منه عدم إعادة إقامة المحدث بالأولى، وظاهر كلام الشارح أن الإعادة لأذان الجنب مستحبة لا واجبة لأنه قال : وإن لم يعد أجزأه الأذان والصلاة وصرح في الظهيرية باستحباب إعادته وصرح قاضيخان بأنه تجب القولة السابقة أنها لا تعاد ما دام الوقت باقياً، وهذا أدل على المقصود من عبارة القنية وكأن معنى قوله «لم أره» أي صريحاً تأمل قوله : فلأنها منهية عن رفع صوتها قال في النهر : ولو خفضته أخلت بسنة الأذان. قوله : (فلان) قوله لا يوثق به الخ قال في النهر وهذا يقتضي ثبوتها ولو كان عالماً بالأوقات ولم أر لهم ما إذا لم يوجد إلا جاهل بالأوقات تقي وعالم بها فاسق أيهما أولى، وقد قالوا في الإمامة إن الفاسق أولى من الجاهل وعكسوا ذلك في القضاء والفرق لا يخفى إلا أنه ينبغي (۲) رواه الترمذي في كتاب الصلاة باب Book of Prayer - Chapter of the Adhan: The adhan of the junub and his iqamah, the iqamah of the one with hadath, the adhan of the woman, the fasiq, the sitting one, and the drunk; no adhan of the naked person. Abu Hanifa said: He gives the adhan for Fajr after its rising, for Zuhr in winter when the sun declines, in summer he delays, for Asr he delays unless he fears the sun changing, for Isha he delays a little after the whiteness disappears. End. His statement: (And he disliked the adhan of the junub, his iqamah, the iqamah of the one with hadath, the adhan of the woman, the fasiq, the sitting one, and the drunk). As for the adhan of the junub, it is disliked in one narration because he becomes a caller to that which he cannot respond to, and his iqamah is more entitled to dislike. He restricted it to the junub because the adhan of the one with hadath is not disliked in the apparent narration, and that is correct because the adhan resembles the prayer, even requiring the entry of time and order of its words like the pillars of prayer, but it is not actually prayer, so purity from the greater hadath is required but not the lesser, acting on both similarities. And it is said: it is disliked due to the hadith of al-Tirmidhi from Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah said: 'None gives the adhan except one who has wudu.' As for the iqamah of the one with hadath, it was only prescribed connected to the prayer of him who performs it, and it is narrated that it is not disliked like the adhan, but the first opinion is the madhhab. As for the adhan of the woman, she is prohibited from raising her voice because it leads to fitna, and the hermaphrodite should be like the woman. As for the fasiq, his statement is not trusted and is not accepted in religious matters and is not binding on anyone; thus notification is not achieved. As for the sitting one, he leaves the Sunnah of the adhan of standing; this is unrestricted, but restricted to when he does not give the adhan for himself; if he gives the adhan for himself while sitting, it is not disliked because there is no need for notification. From this, lying down is understood as more disliked. As for the drunk, due to lack of trust in his statement, and he is included in the fasiq, but his intoxication may be from something permissible so he is not a fasiq, so he was mentioned separately. This indicates the dislike of the adhan of the insane and the boy who does not understand, by priority due to what we mentioned. The author did not address repeating the adhan of one whose adhan is disliked, and there is detail: they said: The adhan of the junub is repeated, not his iqamah, as is more appropriate. Thus in al-Hidayah, and it is the most correct as in al-Mujtaba, because its repetition is legislated as in the Friday adhan because it is for informing the absent, so its repetition benefits the possibility that some did not hear, unlike the repetition of the iqamah for it is not legislated, and it is understood that the iqamah of the one with hadath is not repeated by priority. The apparent meaning of the commentator's words is that repetition of the adhan of the junub is recommended, not obligatory, because he said: If he does not repeat, his adhan and prayer are valid. And he stated explicitly in al-Zahiriyyah that its repetition is recommended, and Qadikhan stated that it is obligatory... the previous statement that it is not repeated as long as the time remains, and this is more indicative of the intended meaning than the expression of al-Qunyah, and it is as if the meaning of his statement 'I have not seen it' is explicitly, so ponder. His statement: because she is prohibited from raising her voice. He said in al-Nahr: If she lowers it, she violates the Sunnah of the adhan. His statement: (so-and-so) his statement: his statement is not trusted, etc. He said in al-Nahr: This necessitates its establishment even if he is knowledgeable of the times, and I have not seen for them the case where there is only a pious ignorant of the times and a knowledgeable fasiq: which is more worthy? And they said in imamate that the fasiq is more worthy than the ignorant, and they reversed that in qada', and the difference is not hidden, except that it is appropriate. (2) Narrated by al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Prayer, Chapter 33.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on the adhan of various individuals. The matn states that the adhan and iqamah of a junub (person in major impurity), the iqamah of a person with hadath (minor impurity), and the adhan of a woman, fasiq (sinner), sitting person, and drunk are disliked. Additionally, the adhan of a naked person is not valid. The commentary explains each: For the junub, it is disliked in one narration, and his iqamah is even more disliked. The adhan of a person with minor impurity (hadath) is not disliked in the apparent narration because the adhan shares similarities with prayer but is not actual prayer, so only the greater impurity is considered. However, there is also a narration that it is disliked based on the hadith 'None gives the adhan except one who has wudu.' The iqamah of a person with hadath is a matter of ikhtilaf: some say it is disliked, others say it is not; the first opinion is the madhhab. The adhan of a woman is disliked because she is commanded not to raise her voice due to fitna; the same applies to a hermaphrodite. The adhan of a fasiq is disliked because his word is not reliable and does not achieve the purpose of informing people. The adhan of a sitting person is disliked if he does so for others, but if for himself, it is not disliked. The adhan of a drunk is disliked due to lack of reliability; the same applies to the insane and child who do not understand. The passage also discusses whether to repeat the adhan if given by such persons: for the junub, repetition of the adhan is recommended (mustahab) but not obligatory; his iqamah is not repeated. For the person with hadath, his iqamah is not repeated by priority.

Key Terms
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
المحدث (al-muhdith): A person in a state of minor ritual impurity requiring wudu.
الفاسق (al-fasiq): A person who openly commits sins and is unreliable in religious matters.
إقامة (iqamah): The second call to prayer, given immediately before the congregational prayer begins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the adhan of a woman according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is valid and mustahab.
B) It is invalid.
C) It is makruh because she is prohibited from raising her voice.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The adhan of a junub, woman, fasiq, sitting person (for others), and drunk is disliked (makruh tahrimi) in the Hanafi school, but it remains valid; repetition is recommended but not obligatory.

intermediate
8 min
Adhan by the Junub, Woman, Sinner and Others
Rulings on adhan by individuals in impure or disqualifying states

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan by a junub, a muhdath, a woman, a fasiq, a sitting person, and a drunk, and explain the reasoning for each ruling.

Core Idea
Adhan is valid even from an impure person, but disliked when the caller cannot respond or is untrustworthy.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the rulings on the adhan when performed by individuals in various states of impurity or disqualification. While the adhan itself is valid (sahih), the call may be disliked (makruh) depending on the caller's condition. We will examine each case and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
List each category and its ruling
Identify each type of caller (junub, muhdath, woman, fasiq, sitting, drunk) and the ruling stated in the matn: which are disliked and which are not.
The matn lists seven categories, but the naked person is excluded.
2
Analyze the junub and muhdath case
Understand the key distinction: the adhan of a junub is disliked, while the adhan of a muhdath (minor impurity) is not disliked in the relied-upon view. This is based on a qiyas: adhan resembles prayer but is not prayer, so only the greater impurity matters.
The hadith 'لا يؤذن إلا متوضىء' is interpreted as discouragement not prohibition.
3
Examine the remaining categories
For each other caller (woman, fasiq, sitting, drunk), identify the reason for dislike: fitna (woman), lack of trustworthiness (fasiq), abandoning sunnah (sitting), and unreliability (drunk). Note exceptions: sitting for oneself is not disliked.
The drunk is separated from the fasiq because his intoxication may be from a permissible source.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that there is a minority view within the Hanafi school that the adhan of a muhdath is disliked due to the hadith. However, the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that it is not disliked.
This dispute is resolved by preferring the qiyas argument over the isolated hadith.
5
Determine the mufta bihi for each case
Summarize the operative rulings: junub's adhan is makruh tanzih; muhdath's adhan is not disliked; woman's adhan is makruh; fasiq's adhan is makruh; sitting person's adhan is makruh unless for himself; drunk's adhan is makruh. All are valid (sahih).
The common misunderstanding is that disliked adhan must be repeated, but validity is not affected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أذان الجنب وإقامته وإقامة المحدث وأذان المرأة والفاسق والقاعد والسكران لا أذان المجرد قال أبو حنيفة : يؤذن للفجر بعد طلوعه، وفي الظهر في الشتاء حين تزول الشمس، وفي الصيف يبرد، وفي العصر يؤخره ما لم يخف تغيير الشمس والعشاء يؤخر قليلاً بعد ذهاب البياض اهـ. قوله (وكره أذان الجنب وإقامته وإقامة المحدث وأذان المرأة والفاسق والقاعد والسكران) أما أذان الجنب فمكروه رواية واحدة لأنه يصير داعياً إلى ما لا يجيب إليه، وإقامته أولى بالكراهة. قيد بالجنب لأن أذان المحدث لا يكره في ظاهر الرواية وهو الصحيح لأن للأذان شبهاً بالصلاة حتى يشترط له دخول الوقت وترتيب كلماته كما ترتبت أركان الصلاة وليس هو بصلاة حقيقة فاشترط له الطهارة عن أغلظ الحدثين دون أخفهما عملاً بالشبهين (٢) وقيل : يكره لحديث الترمذي عن أبي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يؤذن إلا متوضىء» وأما إقامة المحدث فلأنها لم تشرع إلا متصلة بصلاة من يقيم ويروي عدم كراهتها كالأذان، والمذهب الأول. وأما أذان المرأة فلأنها منهية عن رفع صوتها لأنه يؤدّي إلى الفتنة، وينبغي أن يكون الخنثى كالمرأة، وأما الفاسق فلأن قوله لا يوثق به ولا يقبل في الأمور الدينية ولا يلزم أحداً . فلم يوجد الإعلام، وأما القاعد فلترك سنة الأذان من القيام أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يؤذن لنفسه فإن أذن لنفسه قاعداً فإنه لا يكره لعدم الحاجة إلى الإعلام. ويفهم منه كراهته مضطجعاً بالأولى، وأما السكران فلعدم الوثوق بقوله وهو داخل في الفاسق لكن قد يكون سكره من مباح فلا يكون فاسقاً فلذا أفرده بالذكر وأشار به إلى كراهة أذان المجنون والصبي الذي لا يعقل بالأولى لما ذكرنا
The adhan of the junub and his iqama, and the iqama of one with minor impurity, and the adhan of a woman, a sinner, a sitting person, and a drunk: there is no adhan of a naked person. Abu Hanifa said: One gives adhan for Fajr after its dawn, for Zuhr in winter when the sun passes the meridian, and in summer one delays, for 'Asr one delays as long as one does not fear change of the sun, for 'Isha one delays slightly after the whiteness disappears. His statement: (And disliked is the adhan of the junub and his iqama, and the iqama of one with minor impurity, and the adhan of a woman, a sinner, a sitting person, and a drunk). As for the adhan of the junub, it is disliked in one narration because he becomes a caller to what he does not respond to, and his iqama is more deserving of dislike. He restricted to junub because the adhan of one with minor impurity is not disliked in Zahir al-Riwayah, and that is the correct view because adhan resembles prayer such that entry of time and ordering of phrases are required for it just as the pillars of prayer are ordered, but it is not actually prayer, so purity from the graver of the two hadaths is conditioned for it, not the lighter, acting on the two similarities. It is said it is disliked due to the hadith of Tirmidhi from Abu Huraira: 'None should give adhan except one with wudu.' As for the iqama of one with minor impurity, it is legislated only in connection with the prayer of the one who performs it, and it is narrated that it is not disliked like the adhan, and the first opinion is the madhhab. As for the adhan of a woman, she is prohibited from raising her voice because it leads to fitna, and the hermaphrodite should be like a woman. As for the sinner, his statement is not trusted and not accepted in religious matters and does not obligate anyone, so notification is not achieved. As for the sitting person, he has abandoned the sunnah of adhan by standing; this is unrestricted but restricted to when he does not give adhan for himself; if he gives adhan for himself while sitting, it is not disliked because there is no need for notification. From this it is understood that lying down is more worthy of dislike. As for the drunk, there is no trust in his statement, and he is included in the sinner, but his intoxication may be from permissible means so he may not be a sinner, so he was mentioned separately, and he pointed to the dislike of the adhan of the insane and the child who does not understand by priority due to what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rulings on the adhan by individuals in states of impurity or disqualification. The matn declares the adhan of a junub (majorly impure), a woman, a sinner (fasiq), a sitting person, and a drunk as disliked (makruh). The commentary clarifies: For the junub, his adhan is disliked because he calls others to something he cannot do himself; his iqama is even more disliked. For a person with minor impurity (muhdath), the adhan is not disliked in Zahir al-Riwayah, the soundest position, because adhan resembles prayer but is not actually prayer, so only the greater impurity matters. However, a hadith from Tirmidhi says only one with wudu should give adhan, which some use to argue dislike, but the madhhab follows the first view. A woman's adhan is disliked because she must not raise her voice due to fitna. The fasiq's adhan is not trusted, so the purpose of notification fails. A sitting person misses the sunnah of standing, but if he gives adhan only for himself it is not disliked. A drunk person's adhan is unreliable, and he may not be a fasiq if his intoxication is from permissible sources. The ruling extends to the insane and child who does not understand, by priority. The key takeaway: the adhan is valid (sahih) but disliked; it does not need to be repeated.

Key Terms
الجنب (al-junub): Person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
المحدث (al-muhdath): Person in a state of minor ritual impurity requiring wudu.
الفاسق (al-fasiq): A Muslim who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, whose testimony is rejected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the adhan of a person in minor impurity (muhdath)?
A) Invalid and must be repeated.
B) Disliked but valid.
C) Not disliked and valid.
D) Haram.

Key Takeaway
The adhan is valid (sahih) from all callers, but disliked (makruh tanzih) when the caller is junub, woman, fasiq, sitting for others, or drunk; the muhdath's adhan is not disliked in the mufta bihi view.

Adhan Repetition and Sifat Kamal
Exploring repetition rules and the status of conditions for adhan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repetition of the adhan for various cases and distinguish between conditions of validity (shurut) and attributes of perfection (sifat kamal).

Core Idea
Adhan is valid even from a woman, fasiq, or junub; repetition is recommended, not obligatory.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that the adhan is not invalidated by the absence of certain qualities. It distinguishes between what is necessary for validity and what is desirable for perfection. This distinction has practical implications for appointments and salaries in waqf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main issue
The passage addresses whether the adhan should be repeated when given by someone in a disliked state (e.g., junub, woman, fasiq).
2
Distinguish cases
Categorize the cases: junub, woman, drunk, insane, child, fasiq. For each, note whether repetition is recommended and why.
The key distinction is between cases where confusion is likely (woman, drunk) and where it is not (junub).
3
Understand the ikhtilaf
Qadi Khan holds that repetition for the junub is wajib; the majority (including Al-Hidayah) say it is mustahab. Analyze the proofs and the Hanafi response.
The relied-upon view is mustahab.
4
Locate the concluding principle
The text explicitly states that justice, masculinity, and purity are attributes of perfection (sifat kamal) for the mu'adhdhin, not conditions of validity (shurut sihha).
This is the core legal takeaway.
5
Apply to appointment in waqf
Since the adhan is valid, a fasiq can be appointed as mu'adhdhin and is entitled to the salary. For a woman, there is hesitation but the adhan itself is valid.

أخفهما، فظاهره كغيره أن كراهة أذان الجنب تحريمية الطهارة فيه عن لترك الواجب وإن كانت إعادته مستحبة ويعاد أذان المرأة والسكران والجنون والمعتوه والصبي الذي لا يعقل لعدم الاعتماد على أذان هؤلاء فلا أذان الفاسق ولا يعاد فالإعادة فيه ليقع على وجه السنة. وفي الخلاصة : خمس خصال إذا وجدت في الأذان والإقامة وجب الاستقبال : إذا غشي على المؤذن في أحدهما أو مات أو سبقه حدث فذهب وتوضأ أو حصر فيه ولا ملقن أو خرس يجب الاستقبال وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : معناه فإن حمل الوجوب على ظاهره احتيج إلى الفرق بين نفس الأذان فإنه سنة واستقباله بعد الشروع فيه وتحقق العجز عن إتمامه. وقد يقال فيه إذا شرع فيه ثم قطع تبادر إلى ظن السامعين أن قطعه للخطأ فينتظرون الأذان الحق وقد تفوت بذلك الصلاة فوجب إزالة ما يفضي إلى ذلك بخلاف ما إذا لم يكن أذان أصلاً حيث لا ينتظرون بل يراقب كل منهم وقت الصلاة بنفسه أو ينصبون لهم مراقباً إلا أن هذا يقتضي وجوب الإعادة فيمن ذكرناهم آنفاً إلا الجنب كذا في فتح القدير. والظاهر أن الوجوب ليس على حقيقته بل بمعنى الثبوت لما في المجتبى : وإذا غشي عليه في أذانه أو أحدث فتوضأ أو مات أو ارتد فالأحب استقبال الأذان وكذا صرح بالاستحباب في الظهيرية. وفي السراح الوهاج وفي القنية : وقف في الأذان لتنحنح أو سعال لا يعيد وإن كانت الوقفة كثيرة يعيد اهـ. وذكر الشارح أن إعادة أذان المرأة والسكران مستحبة فصار الحاصل على هذا أن العدالة والذكورة والطهارة صفات كمال للؤذن لا شرائط صحة، فأذان الفاسق والمرأة والجنب صحيح حتى يستحق المؤذن معلوم وظيفة الأذان المقررة في الوقف، ويصح تقرير الفاسق فيها، وفي صحة تقرير المرأة في الوظيفة تردد لكن ذكر في السراج الوهاج إذا لم يكن الأذان كالإمامة. قوله : (وإن كانت إعادته (مستحبة يشير إلى أنه لا منافاة بينه وبين ما في الظهيرية لأن الإعادة مقام آخر. قوله : وفي فتاوى قاضيخان (معناه أي فيها معنى ما في الخلاصة وقوله «فإن حمل الوجوب كلام مستأنف قوله : (إلا) الجنب قال في فتح القدير بعد هذا: ولو قال قائل فيهم إن علم الناس حالهم وجبت وإلا استحب لينقع فعل الأذان معتبر أو على وجه السنة لم يبعد وعكسه في الخمس المذكورة .اهـ. قوله : (وهو يقتضي عدم صحته أقول قال في البدائع : يكره أذان المرأة باتفاق الروايات ولو أذنت للقوم أجزأهم حتى لا يعاد لحصول المقصود وهو الإعلام. وروي عن أبي حنيفة أنه يستحب الإعادة وكذا يكره أذان الصبي الذي يعقل وإن كان جائزاً حتى لا يعاد في لا ظاهر الرواية الحصول المقصود. وأما الصبي الذي لا يعقل فلا يجزىء ويعاد لأن ما يصدر لا يعتد به كصوت الطيور. ويكره أذان المجنون والسكران وهل يعاد ؟ في ظاهر الرواية أحب إلي أن عن عقل
The author did not address the repetition of the adhan of those whose adhan is disliked, and there is detail. They said: The adhan of the junub is repeated, but not his iqama, according to what is more apparent. This is in Al-Hidayah and it is the most sound, as in Al-Mujtaba, because repeating it is legislated as in the adhan of Jumu'ah because it is for informing the absent, so its repetition is beneficial due to the possibility of some not hearing, unlike the repetition of iqama which is not legislated, and it is understood that the iqama of the one with minor impurity is not repeated by priority. The apparent meaning of the commentator's words is that repetition of the junub's adhan is recommended (mustahabb) not obligatory (wajib), because he said: If he does not repeat, the adhan and prayer are valid. In Al-Dhahiriyya it is explicitly stated that its repetition is recommended. Qadi Khan explicitly stated that it is obligatory. The previous statement that it is not repeated as long as time remains is more indicative of the intended meaning than the expression of Al-Quniyyah. It is as if the meaning of his saying 'I did not see it' is explicitly to be considered. His saying: Because she is prohibited from raising her voice... Al-Nahr said: If she lowers it, she has violated the sunnah of adhan. His saying: (So-and-so) His statement that his word is not trusted etc. Al-Nahr said: This requires its establishment even if he is knowledgeable of the times. I have not seen for them what if only a pious person ignorant of times and an immoral person knowledgeable of times exist, which one is better? They said regarding imamate that the immoral is better than the ignorant, and they reversed that in judiciary, and the difference is not hidden except that it should be... (2) Narrated by al-Tirmidhi in the book of Salah, chapter 33. The greater of the two hadaths without the lighter, so its apparent meaning like others is that the dislike of the junub's adhan is prohibitive (tahrimi) due to leaving the obligatory purity, although its repetition is recommended. The adhan of the woman, the drunk, the insane, the mentally deficient, and the child who does not understand is repeated because their adhan is not relied upon, so attention is not paid to them. Perhaps people wait for the proper adhan while it is valid, leading to missing the prayer or doubt in the validity of what was performed or performing it in a disliked time. This does not apply to the junub; the utmost that can be said is his fisq. It is explicitly stated that the adhan of the fasiq is disliked and not repeated, so repetition there would be for the sake of sunnah. In Al-Khulasa: five characteristics if present in adhan and iqama make istiqbal (starting over) obligatory: if the mu'adhdhin faints during one of them, or dies, or is overtaken by hadath and leaves and makes wudu, or is stuck and has no prompter, or becomes mute; istiqbal is obligatory. In the Fatawa of Qadi Khan: its meaning... then if the obligatory is taken literally, there is need to distinguish between the adhan itself, which is sunnah, and istiqbal after starting it and the inability to complete it. It may be said: if he starts and then cuts off, the listeners immediately assume he is wrong and wait for the correct adhan, and thus prayer time may be missed, so it is obligatory to remove what leads to that, unlike if there was no adhan at all, where they do not wait but each watches the prayer time himself or they appoint a watchman. However, this requires obligation of repetition in those we mentioned earlier except the junub, as in Fath al-Qadir. The apparent meaning is that obligation is not literal but rather in the sense of confirmation, as in Al-Mujtaba: If he faints during his adhan, or has hadath and makes wudu, or dies, or apostatizes, then the most beloved is to start over the adhan. Similarly, istihbab is explicitly stated in Al-Dhahiriyya. In Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and Al-Quniyyah: if he stops in adhan due to clearing throat or coughing, he does not repeat; if the stop is long, he repeats. The commentator stated that repeating the adhan of the woman and the drunk is recommended. So the conclusion is that justice ('adala), masculinity (dhukura), and purity (tahara) are attributes of perfection (sifat kamal) for the mu'adhdhin, not conditions of validity (shurut sihha). Therefore, the adhan of the fasiq, woman, and junub is valid, so the mu'adhdhin is entitled to the salary of the adhan function stipulated in the waqf, and it is valid to appoint the fasiq in it. In the validity of appointing a woman to the position, there is hesitation, but it is mentioned in Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that if the adhan is not like the imamate. His saying: (And if its repetition is recommended) indicates that there is no contradiction between it and what is in Al-Dhahiriyyah because repetition is another matter. His saying: (And in the Fatawa of Qadi Khan) its meaning, i.e., in it is the meaning of what is in Al-Khulasa. And his saying: 'If the obligation is interpreted...' is a renewed statement. His saying: (Except) the junub. In Fath al-Qadir after this: If someone says regarding them: if people know their situation, repetition is obligatory; otherwise it is recommended, so that the adhan occurs on a proper or sunnah basis, it is not far-fetched, and the opposite in the five mentioned. His saying: (And it requires its invalidity) I say: In Al-Bada'i: The adhan of a woman is disliked by consensus of narrations, and if she gives adhan for a congregation, it suffices them so that it is not repeated, because the purpose (informing) is achieved. It is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he recommends repeating it. Similarly, the adhan of a discerning child is disliked although permissible, so it is not repeated in the apparent narration because the purpose is achieved. As for the child who does not understand, it is not valid and is repeated because what emanates from him is not considered like the sound of birds. The adhan of the insane and the drunk is disliked; is it repeated? In the apparent narration, I prefer that... (text becomes unclear).
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage discusses whether the adhan should be repeated when given by someone in a disliked state. The text makes clear that the adhan of a junub, woman, or fasiq is valid (sahih); the disliked nature does not render it void. Repetition for the junub is recommended (mustahabb) but not obligatory, as the adhan is still valid without repetition. For the woman and the drunk, repetition is recommended because their adhan may be unreliable and cause confusion about prayer times. For the fasiq, his adhan is disliked but not repeated. The text then lists five cases (fainting, death, hadath, being stuck, muteness) where starting over (istiqbal) is said to be obligatory (wajib) in some sources, but the relied-upon view interprets this as strong recommendation (istihbab). The concluding point is that justice, masculinity, and purity are attributes of perfection for the mu'adhdhin, not conditions of validity. Therefore, an appointment of a fasiq or woman to the position is valid, though appointing a woman is somewhat disputed. The key takeaway: the adhan is valid despite these impurities or imperfections, but it is recommended to have a mu'adhdhin who possesses these qualities to avoid confusion.

Key Terms
الإعادة (al-i'ada): Performing the adhan again from the beginning after it was already given.
الاستقبال (al-istiqbal): Starting the adhan over from the beginning after a disruption (e.g., fainting).
صفات كمال (sifat kamal): Attributes that are recommended for the mu'adhdhin but not necessary for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of 'adalah (justice) for the mu'adhdhin?
A) It is a condition of validity (shart sihha).
B) It is an attribute of perfection (sifat kamal).
C) It is wajib.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Justice, masculinity, and purity are attributes of perfection for the mu'adhdhin, not conditions of validity; the adhan remains valid and repetition is only recommended.

Adhan Validity: The Principle of 'Attributes of Perfection' Are Not Conditions
Ruling with proof: establishing the principle of validity for adhan despite missing perfections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that justice, masculinity, and purity are attributes of perfection (sifat kamal) not conditions of validity (shurut sihha) for adhan, and apply this principle to determine the validity of adhan from a woman, fasiq, or junub.

Core Idea
Adhan is valid even from imperfect persons – perfection is not required for validity, only for merit.

In the Hanafi school, the adhan serves the purpose of informing the community of prayer times. This lesson introduces a key distinction: while certain qualities like justice, masculinity, and ritual purity are highly recommended for the mu'adhdhin, they are not conditions for the adhan's validity. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly evaluating the adhan of various individuals and for avoiding unnecessary repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories and attributes
The passage mentions woman, fasiq, and junub, and states that justice (`adala), masculinity (dhukura), and purity (tahara) are attributes of perfection (sifat kamal) not conditions of validity (shurut sihha).
These three attributes are not exhaustive; the principle is general.
2
Recognize the legal principle
The author explicitly declares that these attributes are perfections, not prerequisites. This means the adhan of someone lacking them is still valid (sahih) but may be disliked (makruh).
Validity (sihha) is distinct from merit (kamal).
3
Understand the proof (dalil)
The proof is based on the purpose of adhan: informing (i'lam). Since the function is to announce the time, any clear vocalization suffices, regardless of the personal qualities of the mu'adhdhin.
This is a qiyas (analogy) rooted in the maqasid (objectives) of the act.
4
Apply the principle
Given the principle, the adhan of a woman, fasiq, or junub is valid. Consequently, if such an adhan is given, the mu'adhdhin is entitled to his stipend (if applicable) and the community need not repeat it, though repetition is recommended.
The passage also notes that appointing a fasiq to the adhan function is valid.
