وفي السراح الوهاج وفي القنية : وقف في الأذان لتنحنح أو سعال لا يعيد وإن كانت الوقفة كثيرة يعيد اهـ. وذكر الشارح أن إعادة أذان المرأة والسكران مستحبة فصار الحاصل على هذا أن العدالة والذكورة والطهارة صفات كمال للؤذن لا شرائط صحة، فأذان الفاسق والمرأة والجنب صحيح حتى يستحق المؤذن معلوم وظيفة الأذان المقررة في الوقف، ويصح تقرير الفاسق فيها، وفي صحة تقرير المرأة في الوظيفة تردد لكن ذكر في السراج الوهاج إذا لم يكن الأذان كالإمامة. قوله : (وإن كانت إعادته (مستحبة يشير إلى أنه لا منافاة بينه وبين ما في الظهيرية لأن الإعادة مقام آخر. قوله : وفي فتاوى قاضيخان (معناه أي فيها معنى ما في الخلاصة وقوله «فإن حمل الوجوب كلام مستأنف قوله : (إلا) الجنب قال في فتح القدير بعد هذا: ولو قال قائل فيهم إن علم الناس حالهم وجبت وإلا استحب لينقع فعل الأذان معتبر أو على وجه السنة لم يبعد وعكسه في الخمس المذكورة .اهـ. قوله : (وهو يقتضي عدم صحته أقول قال في البدائع : يكره أذان المرأة باتفاق الروايات ولو أذنت للقوم أجزأهم حتى لا يعاد لحصول المقصود وهو الإعلام. وروي عن أبي حنيفة أنه يستحب الإعادة وكذا يكره أذان الصبي الذي يعقل وإن كان جائزاً حتى لا يعاد في لا ظاهر الرواية الحصول المقصود. وأما الصبي الذي لا يعقل فلا يجزىء ويعاد لأن ما يصدر لا يعتد به كصوت الطيور. ويكره أذان المجنون والسكران وهل يعاد ؟ في ظاهر الرواية أحب إلي أن لا يعيدوا أذان المرأة فكأنهم صلوا بغير أذان فلهذا كان عليهم الإعادة وهو يقتضي عدم صحته . وينبغي أن لا يصح أذان الفاسق بالنسبة إلى قبول خبره والاعتماد عليه لما قدمناه أنه لا من يقبل قوله في الأمور الدينية كما صرح به الشارح. وأما العقل فينبغي أن يكون شرط صحة أذان يصح الصبي الذي لا يعقل والمجنون والمعتوه أصلاً، وأما الصبي الذي يعقل فأذانه صحيح من غير كراهة في ظاهر الرواية إلا أن أذان البالغ أفضل كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي المجمع : ويكره أذان الصبي ويجزىء وأطلقه. فعلى هذا يصح تقريره في وظيفة الأذان، وأما الاسلام فينبغي أن يكون شرط صحة فلا يصح أذان كافر على أي ملة كان، لكن هل يكون بالأذان مسلماً؟ قال البزازي في فتاواه من باب السير وإن شهدوا على الذمي أنه كان يؤذن ويقيم كان مسلماً، سواء كان الأذان في السفر أو الحضر. وإن قالوا سمعناه يؤذن في المسجد فلا شيء حتى يقولوا هو مؤذن، فإن قالوا ذلك فهو مسلم لأنهم إذا قالوا هو مؤذن كان ذلك عادة له فيكون مسلماً اهـ . فالحاصل أنه لا يكون بالأذان مسلماً إلا إذا صار عادة له مع إتيانه بالشهادتين. وينبغي أن يكون ذلك في العيسوية طائفة وهم من اليهود ينسبون إلى أبي عيسى اليهودي الأصبهاني يعتقدون اختصاص رسالة نبينا إلى العرب، فهذا لا بالأذان مسلماً، وأما غيرهم فينبغي أن يكون مسلماً بنفس الأذان والله الموفق للصواب. وفي السراج الوهاج : إذا ارتد المؤذن بعد الأذان لا يعاد أذانه ولو أعيد فهو أفضل. قوله (لا أذان العبد وولد الزنا والأعمى والأعرابي) أي لا يكره أذان هؤلاء لأن قولهم مقبول في الأمور الدينية فيكون ملزماً فيحصل به الإعلام بخلاف الفاسق . وفي الخلاصة : وغيرهم أولى يعاد. قوله : (وينبغي أن لا يصح أذان الفاسق الخ) كذا في النهر أيضاً وظاهره أنه يعاد. وقد صرح في معراج الدراية عن المجتبى أنه يكره ولا يعاد، وكذا نقله بعض الأفاضل عن الفتاوى الهندية عن الذخيرة لكن في القهستاني : اعلم أن إعادة أذان الجنب والمرأة والمجنون والسكران والصبي والفاجر والراكب والقاعد والماشي والمنحرف عن القبلة واجبة لأنه غير معتد به وقيل مستحبة فإنه معتد به إلا أنه ناقص وهو الأصح كما في التمرتاشي .اهـ. فقد صرح بإعادة أذان الفاجر أي الفاسق لكن في كون أذانه معتداً به نظر لما ذكره الشارح من عدم قبول قوله فحينئذ لا يفيد العلم بدخول الأوقات، ومثله المجنون والسكران والصبي فالمناسب أن لا يعتد بأذانهم أصلاً، ولا يصح تقريرهم في وظيفة الأذان لعدم حصول فائدته وقد يقال مراده بالاعتداد به من جهة قيام الشعائر وعدم وجوب المقاتلة بتركه وعدم الإثم .به قوله : (وفي النهاية ومتى كان الخ إشارة إلى جواب آخر عن أذان ابن أم مكتوم لأنه ورد أنه لا يؤذن حتى يسمع الناس يقولون أصبحت أصبحت. وفي معراج الدراية : وكان مع ابن أم مكتوم من يحفظ عليه أوقات الصلاة، ومتى كان ذلك يكون تأذينه وتأذين البصير
And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Qunya: If he pauses in the adhan due to clearing throat or coughing, he does not repeat; if the pause is long, he repeats. End quote. And the commentator mentioned that repeating the adhan of a woman and a drunkard is recommended. So the conclusion is that justice, masculinity, and purity are attributes of perfection for the mu'adhdhin, not conditions of validity. Thus the adhan of the fasiq, woman, and junub is valid, so the mu'adhdhin merits the known stipend of the adhan function established in the endowment, and appointing the fasiq is valid. Regarding the validity of appointing a woman to the function, there is hesitation, but it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj if the adhan is not like the imama. His statement: 'and if its repetition is recommended' indicates no contradiction with what is in al-Zahiriyya because repetition is another matter. His statement: 'and in Fatawa Qadikhan: its meaning' i.e., in it is the meaning of what is in al-Khulasa, and his statement 'for if obligation is taken...' is an independent statement. His statement: 'except the junub' he said in Fath al-Qadir after this: and if someone says about them that if people know their condition, it is obligatory, otherwise it is recommended, so that the adhan is performed considered or in a sunna manner, it is not far, and its opposite in the five mentioned. End quote. His statement: 'and it necessitates its invalidity' I say: in al-Bada'i': The adhan of a woman is disliked by agreement of narrations, and if she gives adhan for a group, it suffices them, so it is not repeated because the purpose, which is informing, is achieved. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that repetition is recommended. Similarly, the adhan of a discerning child is disliked, even though it is permissible, so it is not repeated; in the apparent narration the purpose is achieved. As for the non-discerning child, it does not suffice and is repeated because what issues from him is not considered, like the sound of birds. And the adhan of the madman and drunkard is disliked; and is it repeated? In the apparent narration, I prefer that they not repeat the adhan of the woman, for they are as if they prayed without adhan, so therefore repetition is upon them, which necessitates its invalidity. And it is proper that the adhan of the fasiq not be valid with respect to accepting his report and relying upon him, because we have presented that he whose word is not accepted in religious matters, as the commentator clarified. As for intellect, it should be a condition for validity of adhan: the adhan of the non-discerning child, madman, and idiot is invalid entirely. As for the discerning child, his adhan is valid without dislike in the apparent narration, except that the adhan of an adult is better, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And in al-Majma': The adhan of a child is disliked and suffices, and he left it unrestricted. Upon this, his appointment in the adhan function is valid. As for Islam, it should be a condition of validity, so the adhan of a disbeliever is not valid, regardless of his religion. But does he become Muslim by the adhan? Al-Bazzazi said in his Fatawa, from the chapter of siyar: and if they testify against a dhimmi that he used to give adhan and iqama, he becomes a Muslim, whether the adhan was in travel or residence. And if they say we heard him giving adhan in the mosque, nothing applies until they say he is a mu'adhdhin; if they say that, then he is a Muslim, because if they say he is a mu'adhdhin, that is customary for him, so he is a Muslim. End quote. So the conclusion is that he does not become Muslim by the adhan unless it becomes customary for him along with his uttering the two testimonies. And that should apply to the 'Isawiyya sect, who are Jews attributing to Abu 'Isa al-Isfahani al-Yahudi, who believe that the message of our Prophet is specific to Arabs; this person does not become Muslim by the adhan. As for others, he should become Muslim by the adhan itself. And Allah is the giver of success to what is correct. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if the mu'adhdhin apostatizes after the adhan, his adhan is not repeated, and if repeated it is better. His statement: 'no adhan of the slave, the bastard, the blind, and the Bedouin' i.e., the adhan of these is not disliked because their word is accepted in religious matters, so it is binding, and informing is achieved, unlike the fasiq. And in al-Khulasa: and others are more deserving of being repeated. His statement: 'and it is proper that the adhan of the fasiq not be valid etc.' similarly in al-Nahr, and its apparent meaning is that it is repeated. And it is explicitly stated in Mi'raj al-Diraya from al-Mujtaba that it is disliked and not repeated, and likewise some nobles transmitted from al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya from al-Dhakhira. But in al-Qahistani: know that repeating the adhan of the junub, woman, madman, drunkard, child, immoral person, rider, sitter, walker, and one facing away from qibla is obligatory because it is not considered; and it is said recommended, for it is considered but defective, and that is the most correct as in al-Tamartashi. End quote. So he explicitly stated the repetition of the adhan of the fajir i.e., the fasiq, but regarding it being considered, there is consideration because of what the commentator mentioned of non-acceptance of his word; therefore it does not provide knowledge of the entry of times. And likewise the madman, drunkard, and child; so the appropriate view is that their adhan is not considered at all, and their appointment in the adhan function is not valid because its benefit is not achieved. And it may be said his intent by 'considered' is from the perspective of performing the rituals and the non-obligation of fighting due to leaving it and the absence of sin. His statement: 'and in al-Nihaya: and whenever it was' is an indication of another answer regarding the adhan of Ibn Umm Maktum, because it is reported that he would not give adhan until he heard people saying 'morning has come, morning has come.' And in Mi'raj al-Diraya: and Ibn Umm Maktum had someone who would preserve the prayer times for him, and whenever that is the case, his adhan and the adhan of a sighted person are [equal?]
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This lengthy passage continues the discussion of who may validly give the adhan and whether repetition is required. The author begins by addressing cases of pauses due to coughing or sneezing, stating that a short pause does not invalidate, but a long one necessitates restart. He then summarizes that attributes like justice, masculinity, and purity are perfections, not prerequisites for validity; thus the adhan of a fasiq, woman, and junub is valid, though disliked. The passage delves into the adhan of a woman: it is disliked but suffices according to the majority, and Abu Hanifa is reported to recommend repetition. For a discerning child, the adhan is permissible and valid but disliked; the non-discerning child's adhan is invalid. The adhan of a madman and drunkard is disliked, and there is a difference of opinion on repetition. The passage then discusses the fasiq: his adhan is accepted with caution, but some scholars say it must be repeated because his word is not reliable. The ruling on a non-Muslim: adhan is invalid, but if a non-Muslim habitually gives adhan, it indicates conversion to Islam, except for the 'Isawiyya sect who do not accept the universality of the Prophet's message. Apostasy after adhan does not invalidate the adhan. Finally, the adhan of slaves, children of zina, blind, and Bedouins is not disliked because their word is accepted. The passage ends with a reference to Ibn Umm Maktum, the blind companion, whose adhan was considered valid because he had someone to inform him of the times. Throughout, the text presents multiple intra-madhhab differences, with the preferred view being that repetition is recommended (mustahabb) for most cases of disliked adhan, except where reliability is absent.

Key Terms
صفات كمال (sifat kamal): Attributes of perfection that enhance the act but are not required for validity.
شرائط صحة (shurut sihha): Conditions of validity; without which the act is invalid.
الإعلام (al-i'lam): Informing; the primary purpose of adhan is to announce the prayer time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best describes the ruling on the adhan of a junub (person in state of major impurity)?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid but disliked; the mu'adhdhin merits the stipend.
C) It is valid with no dislike because purity is not a condition.
D) It is obligatory to repeat because the person is impure.

Key Takeaway
Justice, masculinity, and purity are perfections, not conditions for the validity of adhan.

Detailed Rulings: Dispute on Repetition for Imperfect Mu'adhdhin
Ruling with proof: detailed rulings on adhan by category and dispute on repetition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the adhan of a woman, child, madman, drunkard, and fasiq, and evaluate the ikhtilaf on whether repetition is wajib or mustahabb.

Core Idea
The adhan of imperfect persons is valid but disliked; whether to repeat depends on reliability and the purpose of informing.

While the previous lesson established the general principle that many attributes are perfections not conditions, this lesson dives into the specific rulings for each category and the scholarly dispute about when repetition is required (wajib) or merely recommended (mustahabb). Understanding this dispute is crucial for practical application in communities where such mu'adhdhins may be present.

Guided Path
1
List the categories and their rulings
From the passage, identify the rulings for: woman, discerning child, non-discerning child, madman, drunkard, and fasiq. Note whether the adhan is valid, disliked, and whether repetition is mentioned.
Pay attention to the distinction between 'la yujzi' (does not suffice) and 'yujzi' (suffices).
2
Understand the basis for each ruling
For woman and discerning child: their adhan is valid because they are capable of clear informing. For non-discerning child and madman: their adhan is like noise (sawt al-tuyur) because they lack understanding. For fasiq: his word is not accepted in religious matters, so the adhan may not provide certainty.
The basis is the purpose of informing (i'lam) and reliability of the informant.
3
Identify the dispute on repetition
Some authorities (e.g., al-Tamartashi) hold that repetition is wajib because the adhan is not 'considered' (ghayr mu'tad bihi). Others (zahir al-riwayah) hold it is mustahabb because the adhan is considered but defective.
The dispute is recorded in al-Qahistani and al-Mujtaba.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that repetition is mustahabb for most categories, as favored by al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The opinion of wajib is weaker.
The praktical consequence: if the adhan is considered valid, the community may rely on it, but it is better to repeat for certainty.

السراج الوهاج : إذا ارتد المؤذن بعد الأذان لا يعاد أذانه ولو أعيد فهو أفضل. قوله (لا أذان العبد وولد الزنا والأعمى والأعرابي) أي لا يكره أذان هؤلاء لأن قولهم مقبول في الأمور الدينية فيكون ملزماً فيحصل به الإعلام بخلاف الفاسق . وفي الخلاصة : وغيرهم أولى يعاد. قوله : (وينبغي أن لا يصح أذان الفاسق الخ) كذا في النهر أيضاً وظاهره أنه يعاد. وقد صرح في معراج الدراية عن المجتبى أنه يكره ولا يعاد، وكذا نقله بعض الأفاضل عن الفتاوى الهندية عن الذخيرة لكن في القهستاني : اعلم أن إعادة أذان الجنب والمرأة والمجنون والسكران والصبي والفاجر والراكب والقاعد والماشي والمنحرف عن القبلة واجبة لأنه غير معتد به وقيل مستحبة فإنه معتد به إلا أنه ناقص وهو الأصح كما في التمرتاشي .اهـ. فقد صرح بإعادة أذان الفاجر أي الفاسق لكن في كون أذانه معتداً به نظر لما ذكره الشارح من عدم قبول قوله فحينئذ لا يفيد العلم بدخول الأوقات، ومثله المجنون والسكران والصبي فالمناسب أن لا يعتد بأذانهم أصلاً، ولا يصح تقريرهم في وظيفة الأذان لعدم حصول فائدته وقد يقال مراده بالاعتداد به من جهة قيام الشعائر وعدم وجوب المقاتلة بتركه وعدم الإثم .به قوله : (وفي النهاية ومتى كان الخ إشارة إلى جواب آخر عن أذان ابن أم مكتوم لأنه ورد أنه لا يؤذن حتى يسمع الناس يقولون أصبحت أصبحت. وفي معراج الدراية : وكان مع ابن أم مكتوم من يحفظ عليه أوقات الصلاة، ومتى كان ذلك يكون تأذينه وتأذين البصير
And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Qunya: If he pauses in the adhan due to clearing throat or coughing, he does not repeat; if the pause is long, he repeats. End quote. And the commentator mentioned that repeating the adhan of a woman and a drunkard is recommended. So the conclusion is that justice, masculinity, and purity are attributes of perfection for the mu'adhdhin, not conditions of validity. Thus the adhan of the fasiq, woman, and junub is valid, so the mu'adhdhin merits the known stipend of the adhan function established in the endowment, and appointing the fasiq is valid. Regarding the validity of appointing a woman to the function, there is hesitation, but it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj if the adhan is not like the imama. His statement: 'and if its repetition is recommended' indicates no contradiction with what is in al-Zahiriyya because repetition is another matter. His statement: 'and in Fatawa Qadikhan: its meaning' i.e., in it is the meaning of what is in al-Khulasa, and his statement 'for if obligation is taken...' is an independent statement. His statement: 'except the junub' he said in Fath al-Qadir after this: and if someone says about them that if people know their condition, it is obligatory, otherwise it is recommended, so that the adhan is performed considered or in a sunna manner, it is not far, and its opposite in the five mentioned. End quote. His statement: 'and it necessitates its invalidity' I say: in al-Bada'i': The adhan of a woman is disliked by agreement of narrations, and if she gives adhan for a group, it suffices them, so it is not repeated because the purpose, which is informing, is achieved. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that repetition is recommended. Similarly, the adhan of a discerning child is disliked, even though it is permissible, so it is not repeated; in the apparent narration the purpose is achieved. As for the non-discerning child, it does not suffice and is repeated because what issues from him is not considered, like the sound of birds. And the adhan of the madman and drunkard is disliked; and is it repeated? In the apparent narration, I prefer that they not repeat the adhan of the woman, for they are as if they prayed without adhan, so therefore repetition is upon them, which necessitates its invalidity. And it is proper that the adhan of the fasiq not be valid with respect to accepting his report and relying upon him, because we have presented that he whose word is not accepted in religious matters, as the commentator clarified. As for intellect, it should be a condition for validity of adhan: the adhan of the non-discerning child, madman, and idiot is invalid entirely. As for the discerning child, his adhan is valid without dislike in the apparent narration, except that the adhan of an adult is better, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And in al-Majma': The adhan of a child is disliked and suffices, and he left it unrestricted. Upon this, his appointment in the adhan function is valid. As for Islam, it should be a condition of validity, so the adhan of a disbeliever is not valid, regardless of his religion. But does he become Muslim by the adhan? Al-Bazzazi said in his Fatawa, from the chapter of siyar: and if they testify against a dhimmi that he used to give adhan and iqama, he becomes a Muslim, whether the adhan was in travel or residence. And if they say we heard him giving adhan in the mosque, nothing applies until they say he is a mu'adhdhin; if they say that, then he is a Muslim, because if they say he is a mu'adhdhin, that is customary for him, so he is a Muslim. End quote. So the conclusion is that he does not become Muslim by the adhan unless it becomes customary for him along with his uttering the two testimonies. And that should apply to the 'Isawiyya sect, who are Jews attributing to Abu 'Isa al-Isfahani al-Yahudi, who believe that the message of our Prophet is specific to Arabs; this person does not become Muslim by the adhan. As for others, he should become Muslim by the adhan itself. And Allah is the giver of success to what is correct. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if the mu'adhdhin apostatizes after the adhan, his adhan is not repeated, and if repeated it is better. His statement: 'no adhan of the slave, the bastard, the blind, and the Bedouin' i.e., the adhan of these is not disliked because their word is accepted in religious matters, so it is binding, and informing is achieved, unlike the fasiq. And in al-Khulasa: and others are more deserving of being repeated. His statement: 'and it is proper that the adhan of the fasiq not be valid etc.' similarly in al-Nahr, and its apparent meaning is that it is repeated. And it is explicitly stated in Mi'raj al-Diraya from al-Mujtaba that it is disliked and not repeated, and likewise some nobles transmitted from al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya from al-Dhakhira. But in al-Qahistani: know that repeating the adhan of the junub, woman, madman, drunkard, child, immoral person, rider, sitter, walker, and one facing away from qibla is obligatory because it is not considered; and it is said recommended, for it is considered but defective, and that is the most correct as in al-Tamartashi. End quote. So he explicitly stated the repetition of the adhan of the fajir i.e., the fasiq, but regarding it being considered, there is consideration because of what the commentator mentioned of non-acceptance of his word; therefore it does not provide knowledge of the entry of times. And likewise the madman, drunkard, and child; so the appropriate view is that their adhan is not considered at all, and their appointment in the adhan function is not valid because its benefit is not achieved. And it may be said his intent by 'considered' is from the perspective of performing the rituals and the non-obligation of fighting due to leaving it and the absence of sin. His statement: 'and in al-Nihaya: and whenever it was' is an indication of another answer regarding the adhan of Ibn Umm Maktum, because it is reported that he would not give adhan until he heard people saying 'morning has come, morning has come.' And in Mi'raj al-Diraya: and Ibn Umm Maktum had someone who would preserve the prayer times for him, and whenever that is the case, his adhan and the adhan of a sighted person are [equal?]
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This lengthy passage continues the discussion of who may validly give the adhan and whether repetition is required. The author begins by addressing cases of pauses due to coughing or sneezing, stating that a short pause does not invalidate, but a long one necessitates restart. He then summarizes that attributes like justice, masculinity, and purity are perfections, not prerequisites for validity; thus the adhan of a fasiq, woman, and junub is valid, though disliked. The passage delves into the adhan of a woman: it is disliked but suffices according to the majority, and Abu Hanifa is reported to recommend repetition. For a discerning child, the adhan is permissible and valid but disliked; the non-discerning child's adhan is invalid. The adhan of a madman and drunkard is disliked, and there is a difference of opinion on repetition. The passage then discusses the fasiq: his adhan is accepted with caution, but some scholars say it must be repeated because his word is not reliable. The ruling on a non-Muslim: adhan is invalid, but if a non-Muslim habitually gives adhan, it indicates conversion to Islam, except for the 'Isawiyya sect who do not accept the universality of the Prophet's message. Apostasy after adhan does not invalidate the adhan. Finally, the adhan of slaves, children of zina, blind, and Bedouins is not disliked because their word is accepted. The passage ends with a reference to Ibn Umm Maktum, the blind companion, whose adhan was considered valid because he had someone to inform him of the times. Throughout, the text presents multiple intra-madhhab differences, with the preferred view being that repetition is recommended (mustahabb) for most cases of disliked adhan, except where reliability is absent.

Key Terms
لا يجزىء (la yujzi'): It does not suffice; the act is invalid and must be repeated.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an action that is rewarded but not obligatory.
معتد به (mu'tad bihi): Considered; legally recognized as valid and sufficient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the adhan of a fasiq (immoral person)?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid but disliked; repetition is recommended (mustahabb).
C) It is valid and not disliked.
D) It is obligatory to repeat because his word is not accepted.

Key Takeaway
The adhan of imperfect persons is valid but disliked; whether to repeat is a matter of ikhtilaf, with the preferred view being mustahabb.

Ruling on Adhan of Slave, Child of Zina, Blind, Bedouin, and Traveler
States the ruling that adhan from certain individuals is not disliked and the dislike of omitting adhan for travelers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on adhan for specific persons and identify the conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Adhan from a slave, child of zina, blind, or bedouin is permissible; but a fasiq's adhan is unreliable because his word is not accepted in religious matters.

This lesson examines a passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that clarifies the adhan rulings for various individuals often questioned in practice. The text affirms that certain persons—slaves, children born out of wedlock, the blind, and bedouins—may give adhan without dislike. However, it also sets conditions: sanity and Islam are required, and the adhan of an open sinner is not reliable. Understanding these distinctions ensures that the call to prayer maintains its intended authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for each person
The passage states that adhan from a slave, child of zina, blind, and bedouin is not disliked (not makruh). Note the contrast with a fasiq.
2
Understand the traveler's rule
Leaving both adhan and iqamah is disliked for a traveler, but not for a resident praying alone in a city. Reason: the local mu'adhdhin deputizes for residents.
3
Recognize conditions for adhan validity
Sanity and Islam are conditions. The adhan of an insane person, a madman, or an idiot is invalid. The adhan of a disbeliever is invalid, but if a dhimmi habitually gives adhan, it indicates he has become Muslim.
4
Distinguish between valid and reliable
The fasiq's adhan is considered invalid in terms of reliance (his announcement is not trusted), though the outward act may be performed. This affects whether prayers behind his adhan are considered valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب الأذان
العبد وولد الزنا والأعمى والأعرابي وكره تركهما للمسافر لا لمصل في بيته في المصر
وندبا لهما لا للنساء .
فلا · يعيدوا أذان المرأة فكأنهم صلوا بغير أذان فلهذا كان عليهم الإعادة وهو يقتضي عدم صحته . وينبغي أن لا . يصح أذان الفاسق بالنسبة إلى قبول خبره والاعتماد عليه لما قدمناه أنه لا من يقبل قوله في الأمور الدينية كما صرح به الشارح. وأما العقل فينبغي أن يكون شرط صحة أذان يصح الصبي الذي لا يعقل والمجنون والمعتوه أصلاً، وأما الصبي الذي يعقل فأذانه صحيح من غير كراهة في ظاهر الرواية إلا أن أذان البالغ أفضل كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي المجمع : ويكره أذان الصبي ويجزىء وأطلقه. فعلى هذا يصح تقريره في وظيفة الأذان، وأما الاسلام فينبغي أن يكون شرط صحة فلا يصح أذان كافر على أي ملة كان، لكن هل يكون بالأذان مسلماً؟ قال البزازي في فتاواه من باب السير وإن شهدوا على الذمي أنه كان يؤذن ويقيم كان مسلماً، سواء كان الأذان في السفر أو الحضر. وإن قالوا سمعناه يؤذن في المسجد فلا شيء حتى يقولوا هو مؤذن، فإن قالوا ذلك فهو مسلم لأنهم إذا قالوا هو مؤذن كان ذلك عادة له فيكون مسلماً اهـ . فالحاصل أنه لا يكون بالأذان مسلماً إلا إذا صار عادة له مع إتيانه بالشهادتين. وينبغي أن يكون ذلك في العيسوية طائفة وهم من اليهود ينسبون إلى أبي عيسى اليهودي الأصبهاني يعتقدون اختصاص رسالة نبينا إلى العرب، فهذا لا بالأذان مسلماً، وأما غيرهم فينبغي أن يكون مسلماً بنفس الأذان والله الموفق للصواب.
Book of Salah - Chapter of Adhan. The slave, the child of zina, the blind, and the bedouin (their adhan is not disliked). And it is disliked to leave both (adhan and iqamah) for the traveler, not for one who prays in his house in the city. And it is recommended for them (men) but not for women. So they do not repeat the adhan of a woman, because they are as if they prayed without adhan; for this reason they must repeat, and this indicates its invalidity. And it is appropriate that the adhan of a fasiq should not be valid regarding accepting his report and relying upon it, because we have already mentioned that he is not one whose word is accepted in religious matters, as stated by the commentator. As for sanity, it should be a condition for the validity of adhan; the adhan of an insane child, a madman, and an idiot is not valid at all. As for a child who is sane, his adhan is valid without dislike in the apparent narration, except that the adhan of an adult is better. This is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. In al-Majma': The adhan of a child is disliked but suffices, and it is left unrestricted. So upon this, his appointment to the function of adhan is valid. As for Islam, it should be a condition for validity; the adhan of a disbeliever is not valid regardless of his religion. But does he become Muslim by the adhan? Al-Bazzazi said in his Fatawa from the chapter of Siyar: If they testify against a dhimmi that he used to make adhan and iqamah, he becomes Muslim, whether the adhan was in travel or residence. If they say we heard him making adhan in the mosque, nothing [is decided] until they say he is a mu'adhdhin. If they say that, then he is Muslim because if they say he is a mu'adhdhin, that became his habit; so he is Muslim. End. So the conclusion is that he does not become Muslim by the adhan unless it becomes his habit along with his uttering the two testimonies. And it should be that this applies to the 'Isawiyya sect, who are Jews attributed to Abu 'Isa al-Yahudi al-Isfahani, believing that our Prophet's message is only for Arabs; that one does not become Muslim by adhan. As for others, he should become Muslim by the adhan itself. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the adhan of certain individuals. The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states: The adhan of a slave, a child born of zina, a blind person, and a bedouin is not disliked (makruh). Why? Because their word is accepted in religious matters, so the announcement is binding. This contrasts with a fasiq (sinner), whose word is not accepted. The text then addresses the traveler: it is disliked to leave both adhan and iqamah when traveling, but for a person praying alone in his house within a city, it is not disliked. The reasoning, as explained later, is that the mu'adhdhin of the locality acts as a deputy, so the resident's prayer is considered to have been performed with adhan and iqamah effectively. For the traveler, there is no such deputy. The rule is that adhan and iqamah are recommended (sunnah) for men but not for women; women should not make adhan, and if they do, the men must repeat it.

The commentary then discusses the validity conditions: sanity is required, so the adhan of an insane child, a madman, or an idiot is invalid. A sane child's adhan is valid but less virtuous. Islam is also a condition: a disbeliever's adhan is invalid. However, if a dhimmi habitually makes adhan and iqamah, it indicates he has embraced Islam, especially if he utters the two testimonies. An exception is a Jewish sect, the 'Isawiyya, who believe the Prophet's message is only for Arabs; their adhan does not indicate Islam.

Key Terms
العبد (al-‘abd): The male slave whose adhan is not disliked because his word is accepted in religious matters.
ولد الزنا (walad al-zinā): A child born out of wedlock; his adhan is not disliked.
الأعمى (al-a‘mā): A blind person; his adhan is not disliked if he has someone to keep time.
الأعرابي (al-a‘rābī): A bedouin; his adhan is not disliked.
الفاسق (al-fāsiq): An open sinner; his adhan is not reliable because his word is not accepted in religious matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following individuals' adhan is considered invalid?
A) A slave
B) A child of zina
C) A fasiq (open sinner)
D) A blind person

Key Takeaway
The adhan of an openly sinful person (fasiq) cannot be relied upon for determining prayer times; only the adhan of those whose word is accepted in religious matters is valid.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Adhan of a Fasiq
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fasiq's adhan validity and repetition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three main Hanafi positions on the validity and repetition of the fasiq's adhan and explain the underlying reasoning regarding the fasiq's unreliability.

Core Idea
The fasiq's adhan is generally invalid: his word cannot be trusted for knowing prayer times.

The adhan is a communal announcement of prayer time, so the caller must be reliable. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines whether the adhan of an open sinner (fasiq) fulfills this purpose. It presents multiple Hanafi opinions, from merely disliked to completely invalid, and the author weights the stronger view that it must be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The core question: Is the adhan of a fasiq valid and if not, must it be repeated? The passage discusses whether the fasiq's adhan can be relied upon to indicate the correct prayer time.
The fasiq's lack of reliability is central.
2
Locate the strongest basis
The commentator argues that a fasiq's word is not accepted in religious matters (his testimony is rejected), so his adhan cannot produce certainty about the entry of prayer times.
This is the key dalil: lack of acceptability leads to invalidity.
3
Compare the intra-Hanafi views
Al-Mujtaba: the adhan is disliked but valid, not repeated. Al-Qahistani reports a view that repetition is wajib (invalid adhan) and another that it is mustahabb (valid but deficient). Al-Tamartashi favors the sounder view that it is considered valid but deficient.
The dispute is about the degree of validity: deficient vs. completely invalid.
4
Evaluate the author's tarjih
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq prefers the view of complete invalidity, equating the fasiq to a madman or child whose adhan yields no benefit. He also notes that appointing a fasiq as a mu'adhdhin is invalid.
The tarjih is based on the absence of the benefit of adhan.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a fasiq's adhan is used without repetition, the congregation may rely on it and pray at the wrong time, leading to potential invalidity of prayers. Hence the practical consequence is whether i'adah is required.
This highlights the need for reliability in the caller.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (لا أذان العبد وولد الزنا والأعمى والأعرابي) أي لا يكره أذان هؤلاء لأن قولهم مقبول في الأمور الدينية فيكون ملزماً فيحصل به الإعلام بخلاف الفاسق . وفي الخلاصة : وغيرهم أولى يعاد. قوله : (وينبغي أن لا يصح أذان الفاسق الخ) كذا في النهر أيضاً وظاهره أنه يعاد. وقد صرح في معراج الدراية عن المجتبى أنه يكره ولا يعاد، وكذا نقله بعض الأفاضل عن الفتاوى الهندية عن الذخيرة لكن في القهستاني : اعلم أن إعادة أذان الجنب والمرأة والمجنون والسكران والصبي والفاجر والراكب والقاعد والماشي والمنحرف عن القبلة واجبة لأنه غير معتد به وقيل مستحبة فإنه معتد به إلا أنه ناقص وهو الأصح كما في التمرتاشي .اهـ. فقد صرح بإعادة أذان الفاجر أي الفاسق لكن في كون أذانه معتداً به نظر لما ذكره الشارح من عدم قبول قوله فحينئذ لا يفيد العلم بدخول الأوقات، ومثله المجنون والسكران والصبي فالمناسب أن لا يعتد بأذانهم أصلاً، ولا يصح تقريرهم في وظيفة الأذان لعدم حصول فائدته وقد يقال مراده بالاعتداد به من جهة قيام الشعائر وعدم وجوب المقاتلة بتركه وعدم الإثم .به
His saying: 'The adhan of the slave, child of zina, blind, and bedouin' means their adhan is not disliked because their word is accepted in religious matters, so it is binding and thus the announcement is achieved, contrary to the fasiq. In al-Khulasa: And others are better. It should be repeated. His saying: 'And it is appropriate that the adhan of the fasiq should not be valid' etc. similarly in al-Nahr, and its apparent meaning is that it is repeated. And it is explicitly stated in Mir'aj al-Diraya from al-Mujtaba that it is disliked but not repeated. Similarly, some nobles narrated from al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya from al-Dhakhira. But in al-Qahistani: Know that repeating the adhan of a junub, woman, madman, drunkard, child, fajir, rider, sitter, walker, and one deviating from the qibla is obligatory because it is not considered valid; and it is said it is recommended, for it is considered valid but deficient, and this is the sounder view as in al-Tamartashi. End. So he explicitly states repeating the adhan of the fajir, i.e., fasiq. But regarding whether his adhan is considered valid, there is consideration due to what the commentator mentioned of not accepting his statement; then it does not provide knowledge of the entry of times. Similarly the madman, drunkard, and child. So the appropriate view is that their adhan should not be considered valid at all, and their appointment to the function of adhan is not valid because its benefit is not achieved. However, it may be said that what is meant by 'considered valid' is from the perspective of establishing the rituals and not obligating fighting due to abandoning it, and no sin.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the adhan of a fasiq (open sinner). The initial gloss explains that the adhan of the previously mentioned individuals (slave, etc.) is not disliked, unlike the fasiq. Then the main issue: the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq states that the adhan of a fasiq should not be valid because his report is not accepted. This implies it must be repeated. However, a conflicting view from al-Mujtaba says it is only disliked but not repeated. Al-Qahistani reconciles by stating that repetition is obligatory for many cases including the fajir, but another view says it is recommended because the adhan is valid but deficient. The author leans towards the stronger view that it is not valid at all and must be repeated, as it cannot reliably indicate the prayer time. This shows how the Hanafi school weighs conditions of reliability in the adhan-giver.

Key Terms
الفاسق (al-fāsiq): An open sinner whose adhan is disputed in validity.
الإعادة (al-i‘ādah): Repeating the adhan; wajib or mustahabb according to different views.
الاعتداد (al-i‘tidād): Considering the adhan valid and sufficient.
الفاجر (al-fājir): Synonym for fasiq in this context; one who commits major sins openly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which Hanafi source states that the fasiq's adhan is only disliked but not repeated?
A) Al-Qahistani
B) Al-Mujtaba
C) Al-Tamartashi
D) Al-Dhakhira

Key Takeaway
The adhan of a fasiq is generally not considered reliable; the stronger Hanafi view requires it to be repeated to ensure the congregation knows the correct prayer time.

The Blind Person's Adhan: Validity with Assistance
Responding to a query about the blind person's adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for the validity of a blind person's adhan and explain why it is equivalent to that of a sighted person when that condition is met.

Core Idea
A blind person's adhan is valid if he has someone to keep the prayer times; the adhan is about time knowledge, not sight.

This lesson addresses the adhan of a blind person, specifically the case of Ibn Umm Maktum. The text clarifies that a blind person's adhan is not inherently invalid; rather, its validity depends on a practical condition: having a reliable means to know the prayer time. This distinction sets adhan apart from imamate, where a blind imam is disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
Examine the reference to Ibn Umm Maktum, a blind companion who would not make adhan until he heard people confirm the time.
2
Determine the condition
The text states that if the blind person has someone to keep the prayer times for him, his adhan is equivalent to that of a sighted person.
This condition ensures accuracy of the adhan's timing.
3
Contrast with imamate
The text notes that imamate of a blind person is disliked, but this does not apply to adhan because adhan does not require the same level of knowledge as leading prayer.
This distinction prevents confusion between the two rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي النهاية ومتى كان الخ إشارة إلى جواب آخر عن أذان ابن أم مكتوم لأنه ورد أنه لا يؤذن حتى يسمع الناس يقولون أصبحت أصبحت. وفي معراج الدراية : وكان مع ابن أم مكتوم من يحفظ عليه أوقات الصلاة، ومتى كان ذلك يكون تأذينه وتأذين البصير منهم . وأما ابن أم مكتوم الأعمى فإن بلالاً كان يؤذن قبله. وفي النهاية : ومتى كان مع الأعمى من يحفظ عليه أوقات الصلاة يكون حينئذ تأذينه وتأذين البصير سواء. وإنما كرهت إمامتهم لأن الناس ينفرون من الصلاة خلفهم أو لأن العبد مشغول بخدمة مولاه فلا يتفرغ للعلم كالأعرابي وهو ليس بموجود في الأذان لعدم احتياجه إلى العلم. وينبغي أن العبد إن أذن لنفسه لا يحتاج إلى إذن سيده، وإن أراد أن يكون مؤذناً للجماعة لم يجز إلا بإذن سيده لأن فيه إضراراً بخدمته لأنه يحتاج إلى مراعاة الأوقات ولم أره في كلامهم قوله وكره تركهما للمسافر) أي ترك الأذان والإقامة لما رواه البخاري ومسلم عن مالك بن الحويرث أتيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنا وصاحب لي، فلما أردنا الانتقال من عنده قال لنا : إذا حضرت الصلاة فأذنا وأقيما وليؤمكما أكبر كما . وإذا كان هذا الخطاب لهما ولا حاجة لهما مترافقين إلى استحضار أحد علم أن المنفرد أيضاً يسن له ذلك، وقد ورد في خصوص المنفرد أحاديث في أبي داود والنسائي يعجب ربك من راعي غنم في رأس شظية يؤذن بالصلاة ويصلي فيقول الله عز وجل : انظروا إلى عبدي هذا يؤذن للصلاة ويقيم للصلاة يخاف مني قد غفرت لعبدي وأدخلته الجنة» (۱) قال قال سلمان الفارسي . وعن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا كان الرجل بأرض فيء فحانت الصلاة فليتوضأ فإن لم يجد ماء فليتيمم، فإن أقام صلى معه ملكاه، وإن أذن وأقام صلى خلفه من جنود الله ما لا يرى طرفاه» رواه عبد الرزاق . وبهذا ونحوه عرف أن المقصود من الأذان لم ينحصر في الإعلام بل كل منه. ومن الإعلان بهذا الذكر نشر الذكر لله ودينه في أرضه وتذكير العباده من الجن والأنس الذين لا يرى شخصهم في الفلوات من العباد . قيد بتركهما لأنه لو ترك الأذان وأتى بالإقامة لا يكره لأثر علي رضي الله عنه ولو عكس يكره كما في شرح النقاية قوله ( لا لمصل في بيته في المصر) أي لا يكره تركهما له ، والفرق بينهما أن المقيم إذا صلى بدونهما حقيقة فقد صلى بهما حكماً لأن المؤذن نائب عن أهل المحلة فيهما فيكون فعله كفعلهم ، وأما المسافر فقد صلى بدونهما حقيقة وحكماً لأن المكان الذي هو فيه لم يؤذن فيه أصلاً لتلك الصلاة. كذا في الكافي ومفهومه أنه لو لم يؤذنوا في الحي فإنه يكره تركهما للمصلي في بيته وقد صرح به في المجتبى أنه لو أذن بعض المسافرين عن الباقين كما لا يخفى. وأطلق في المصلي في بيته فأفاد أنه لا فرق بين الواحدة سقط سواء. كذا ذكره شيخ الإسلام ..اهـ. قوله: (لم يجز إلا بإذن سيده قال في النهر: وينبغي أن يكون الأجير الخاص كذلك لا يحل أذانه إلا بإذن مستأجره. قوله : (وقد صرح به في المجتبى) فيه نظر لأنه لم يصرح بذلك وإنما يفهم منه بطريق الدلالة لكن الظاهر أن قوله أنه لو أذن بعض المسافرين» ليس عبارة المجتبى بل أصله وأنه» بواو العطف على قوله «أنه لو لم يؤذنوا فتكون الواو سقطت من قلم
His saying: 'And in al-Nihaya, and when...' is an indication of another answer regarding the adhan of Ibn Umm Maktum, because it is reported that he would not make adhan until he heard people saying 'It has become morning.' And in Mir'aj al-Diraya: Ibn Umm Maktum had someone who kept the prayer times for him, and when that is the case, his adhan and the adhan of a sighted person are the same. As for Ibn Umm Maktum the blind, Bilal used to make adhan before him. And in al-Nihaya: When the blind person has someone who keeps the prayer times for him, then his adhan and the adhan of a sighted person are equal. Their imamate is disliked because people are averse to praying behind them, or because the slave is busy serving his master and cannot devote time to knowledge like the bedouin, and this does not apply to adhan because it does not require knowledge. It is fitting that if a slave makes adhan for himself, he does not need his master's permission; but if he wants to be the mu'adhdhin for the congregation, it is not permissible without his master's permission because it harms his service, as he needs to observe the times. I have not seen this in their statements. His saying: 'And it is disliked to leave both for the traveler' means to leave adhan and iqamah, because of what Bukhari and Muslim narrated from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: I came to the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) with a companion, and when we wanted to leave from him, he said to us: 'When the prayer is present, make adhan and iqamah, and let the older of you lead the prayer.' Since this address is to them and they were traveling together without need to summon anyone, it is known that the solitary person also is recommended to do that. And there are specific hadiths regarding the solitary person in Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i: 'Your Lord marvels at a shepherd of goats on a mountain peak who makes adhan for prayer and prays; God says: Look at this servant of Mine: he makes adhan for prayer and iqamah for prayer, fearing Me; I have forgiven My servant and admitted him to Paradise.' Narrated by Salman al-Farisi. And from the Messenger of God: 'If a man is in a land of wilderness and the prayer time arrives, let him perform wudu, and if he cannot find water, let him do tayammum; if he makes iqamah, his two angels pray with him; but if he makes adhan and iqamah, there pray behind him from God's soldiers whose ends cannot be seen.' Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq. And by this and the like, it is known that the purpose of adhan is not limited to announcement, but rather each of them [adhan and iqamah] is for the proclamation of this remembrance, spreading the remembrance of God and His religion in His land, and reminding the servants among the jinn and mankind whose persons are not seen in the deserts. It is restricted to leaving both because if he leaves adhan and performs iqamah, it is not disliked due to an effect from Ali (may God be pleased with him); but if he does the opposite, it is disliked as in Sharh al-Niqaya. His saying: 'Not for one who prays in his house in the city' means it is not disliked to leave them for him. The difference between them is that the resident, if he prays without them in reality, has prayed with them virtually because the mu'adhdhin is the deputy of the people of the neighborhood in them, so his act is like their act. As for the traveler, he has prayed without them in reality and virtually because the place where he is has not had adhan made in it at all for that prayer. This is in al-Kafi. Its implication is that if they have not made adhan in the neighborhood, then it is disliked to leave them for the one praying in his house. And it is explicitly stated in al-Mujtaba: if some of the travelers make adhan for the rest. And he left unrestricted regarding the one praying in his house, so it indicates that there is no difference between the single and... Both are the same. This is stated by Shaykh al-Islam. End. His saying: 'It is not permissible except with his master's permission.' In al-Nahr: And it is fitting that the private hireling also is not allowed to make adhan without his employer's permission. His saying: 'And it is explicitly stated in al-Mujtaba': there is consideration in this, because he did not explicitly state that, but it is understood by way of indication; but apparently his saying 'if some travelers make adhan' is not the expression of al-Mujtaba, but rather its original and 'and' with the conjunction on his saying 'if they have not made adhan' so the waw fell from the pen.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage deals with three topics: the adhan of a blind person, the slave's adhan, and the traveler's adhan.

First, the blind person (Ibn Umm Maktum) is discussed. The text clarifies that if a blind person has someone to keep the prayer times for him, his adhan is equivalent to that of a sighted person. This explains why the blind companion made adhan only after confirming the time by hearing others.

Second, the slave: if he makes adhan for himself, no permission is needed; but if he intends to be the assigned mu'adhdhin for the congregation, he needs his master's permission because it interferes with his service. This is extended to any hired worker (ajir khas) who must obtain his employer's permission.

Third, the traveler: leaving both adhan and iqamah is disliked for a traveler, but not for a resident praying in his house in a city. The proof is from the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith where the Prophet commanded the two travelers to make adhan and iqamah. Additional hadiths show the great reward for the solitary traveler who makes adhan. The rationale is that the mu'adhdhin acts as a deputy for the residents, so the resident's prayer without adhan is valid by deputation. The traveler has no such deputy, so his adhan is directly required. The text also notes that if the neighborhood has no adhan, then it is disliked for the resident to omit it as well.

Key Terms
الأعمى (al-a‘mā): Blind person; his adhan is valid if he has someone to keep time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition makes a blind person's adhan equivalent to a sighted person's?
A) He must be a scholar
B) He must have someone to keep the prayer times for him
C) He must be free
D) He must be in a congregation

Key Takeaway
A blind person's adhan is valid if he can reliably determine the prayer time, typically through an assistant.

The Slave's Adhan: Permission for Congregation
Stating the ruling on slave's adhan with permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between a slave making adhan for himself and for a congregation, and state the requirement of his master's permission for the latter.

Core Idea
A slave may make adhan for himself without permission, but for congregation adhan, his master's permission is required due to potential harm to service.

This lesson examines the adhan of a slave, distinguishing between his personal adhan and serving as the mu'adhdhin for the community. The Hanafi school applies a principle of preventing harm to the master's rights, extending the same rule to any private hireling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Distinguish between a slave's adhan for himself (personal prayer) and his adhan as the designated mu'adhdhin for the congregation.
The ruling differs based on the role.
2
Apply the rule for self-adhan
For his own prayer, no permission from his master is needed because it does not interfere with his service.
3
Apply the rule for congregation adhan
If he wants to be the regular mu'adhdhin for the community, he must obtain his master's permission because it harms his service by requiring him to observe prayer times punctually.
This is based on the principle of preventing harm (darar).
4
Extend to hireling
The same ruling applies to a private hireling (ajir khas); he too needs his employer's permission to be a mu'adhdhin.
This is an extension mentioned in the margin.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage deals with three topics: the adhan of a blind person, the slave's adhan, and the traveler's adhan.

First, the blind person (Ibn Umm Maktum) is discussed. The text clarifies that if a blind person has someone to keep the prayer times for him, his adhan is equivalent to that of a sighted person. This explains why the blind companion made adhan only after confirming the time by hearing others.

Second, the slave: if he makes adhan for himself, no permission is needed; but if he intends to be the assigned mu'adhdhin for the congregation, he needs his master's permission because it interferes with his service. This is extended to any hired worker (ajir khas) who must obtain his employer's permission.

Third, the traveler: leaving both adhan and iqamah is disliked for a traveler, but not for a resident praying in his house in a city. The proof is from the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith where the Prophet commanded the two travelers to make adhan and iqamah. Additional hadiths show the great reward for the solitary traveler who makes adhan. The rationale is that the mu'adhdhin acts as a deputy for the residents, so the resident's prayer without adhan is valid by deputation. The traveler has no such deputy, so his adhan is directly required. The text also notes that if the neighborhood has no adhan, then it is disliked for the resident to omit it as well.

Key Terms
الأجير الخاص (al-ajīr al-khāṣṣ): Private hireling; his adhan as mu'adhdhin requires employer's permission.

According to the passage, when does a slave need his master's permission to make adhan?
A) When making adhan for himself
B) When making adhan for the congregation
C) Both A and B
D) Neither A nor B

Key Takeaway
A slave's adhan for himself is unrestricted; for congregation adhan, master's permission is required to avoid harm to service.

The Traveler's Adhan: Virtue and Ruling
Establishing the ruling on traveler's adhan with proofs and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a traveler's adhan and iqamah, cite the primary hadith proof, and explain the qiyas that distinguishes a traveler from a resident.

Core Idea
A traveler is recommended to make adhan and iqamah; omitting both is disliked, while a resident in a city is exempt due to the mu'adhdhin's deputyship.

This lesson addresses the traveler's adhan. The Hanafi school holds that it is sunnah muakkadah for a traveler to perform both adhan and iqamah, and omitting both is makruh. The proof is a direct command from the Prophet to travelers, and additional hadiths promise great reward. The text also provides a rational distinction using qiyas: a resident is excused because the community mu'adhdhin deputizes for him, but a traveler has no such deputy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states that it is disliked (makruh) for a traveler to leave both adhan and iqamah.
The ruling is about leaving both; leaving only one has different rulings.
2
Examine the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith where the Prophet commanded two travelers to make adhan and iqamah. Additional hadiths emphasize the great reward for a solitary traveler who does so.
A command from the Prophet indicates recommendation (sunnah) in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the rationale
The text explains that a resident's prayer without adhan is valid by deputation because the mu'adhdhin acts as his deputy. A traveler has no such deputy, so he must perform adhan himself.
This is a qiyas based on the presence or absence of a deputy.
4
Apply the distinctions
If a traveler leaves adhan but performs iqamah, it is not disliked. If he leaves iqamah but performs adhan, it is disliked. Also, if the neighborhood in a city has no adhan, then even a resident should not omit it.
These are nuanced applications from the text.

ومتى كان ذلك يكون تأذينه وتأذين البصير منهم . وأما ابن أم مكتوم الأعمى فإن بلالاً كان يؤذن قبله. وفي النهاية : ومتى كان مع الأعمى من يحفظ عليه أوقات الصلاة يكون حينئذ تأذينه وتأذين البصير سواء. وإنما كرهت إمامتهم لأن الناس ينفرون من الصلاة خلفهم أو لأن العبد مشغول بخدمة مولاه فلا يتفرغ للعلم كالأعرابي وهو ليس بموجود في الأذان لعدم احتياجه إلى العلم. وينبغي أن العبد إن أذن لنفسه لا يحتاج إلى إذن هذا يؤذن للصلاة ويقيم للصلاة يخاف مني قد غفرت لعبدي وأدخلته الجنة» (۱) قال قال سلمان الفارسي . وعن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا كان الرجل بأرض فيء فحانت الصلاة فليتوضأ فإن لم يجد ماء فليتيمم، فإن أقام صلى معه ملكاه، وإن أذن وأقام صلى خلفه من جنود الله ما لا يرى طرفاه» رواه عبد الرزاق . وبهذا ونحوه عرف أن المقصود من الأذان لم ينحصر في الإعلام بل كل منه. ومن الإعلان بهذا الذكر نشر الذكر لله ودينه في أرضه وتذكير العباده من الجن والأنس الذين لا يرى شخصهم في الفلوات من العباد . قيد بتركهما لأنه لو ترك الأذان وأتى بالإقامة لا يكره لأثر علي رضي الله عنه ولو عكس يكره كما في شرح النقاية قوله ( حقيقة وحكماً لأن المكان الذي هو فيه لم يؤذن فيه أصلاً لتلك الصلاة. كذا في الكافي ومفهومه أنه لو لم يؤذنوا في الحي فإنه يكره تركهما للمصلي في بيته وقد صرح به في المجتبى أنه لو أذن بعض المسافرين عن الباقين كما لا يخفى. وأطلق في المصلي في بيته فأفاد أنه لا فرق بين الواحدة سقط سواء. كذا ذكره شيخ الإسلام ..اهـ. قوله: (لم يجز إلا بإذن سيده قال في النهر: وينبغي أن يكون الأجير الخاص كذلك لا يحل أذانه إلا بإذن مستأجره. قوله : (وقد صرح به في المجتبى) فيه نظر لأنه لم يصرح بذلك وإنما يفهم منه بطريق الدلالة لكن الظاهر أن قوله أنه لو أذن بعض المسافرين» ليس عبارة المجتبى بل أصله وأنه» بواو العطف على قوله «أنه لو لم يؤذنوا فتكون الواو سقطت من قلم
His saying: 'And in al-Nihaya, and when...' is an indication of another answer regarding the adhan of Ibn Umm Maktum, because it is reported that he would not make adhan until he heard people saying 'It has become morning.' And in Mir'aj al-Diraya: Ibn Umm Maktum had someone who kept the prayer times for him, and when that is the case, his adhan and the adhan of a sighted person are the same. As for Ibn Umm Maktum the blind, Bilal used to make adhan before him. And in al-Nihaya: When the blind person has someone who keeps the prayer times for him, then his adhan and the adhan of a sighted person are equal. Their imamate is disliked because people are averse to praying behind them, or because the slave is busy serving his master and cannot devote time to knowledge like the bedouin, and this does not apply to adhan because it does not require knowledge. It is fitting that if a slave makes adhan for himself, he does not need his master's permission; but if he wants to be the mu'adhdhin for the congregation, it is not permissible without his master's permission because it harms his service, as he needs to observe the times. I have not seen this in their statements. His saying: 'And it is disliked to leave both for the traveler' means to leave adhan and iqamah, because of what Bukhari and Muslim narrated from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: I came to the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) with a companion, and when we wanted to leave from him, he said to us: 'When the prayer is present, make adhan and iqamah, and let the older of you lead the prayer.' Since this address is to them and they were traveling together without need to summon anyone, it is known that the solitary person also is recommended to do that. And there are specific hadiths regarding the solitary person in Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i: 'Your Lord marvels at a shepherd of goats on a mountain peak who makes adhan for prayer and prays; God says: Look at this servant of Mine: he makes adhan for prayer and iqamah for prayer, fearing Me; I have forgiven My servant and admitted him to Paradise.' Narrated by Salman al-Farisi. And from the Messenger of God: 'If a man is in a land of wilderness and the prayer time arrives, let him perform wudu, and if he cannot find water, let him do tayammum; if he makes iqamah, his two angels pray with him; but if he makes adhan and iqamah, there pray behind him from God's soldiers whose ends cannot be seen.' Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq. And by this and the like, it is known that the purpose of adhan is not limited to announcement, but rather each of them [adhan and iqamah] is for the proclamation of this remembrance, spreading the remembrance of God and His religion in His land, and reminding the servants among the jinn and mankind whose persons are not seen in the deserts. It is restricted to leaving both because if he leaves adhan and performs iqamah, it is not disliked due to an effect from Ali (may God be pleased with him); but if he does the opposite, it is disliked as in Sharh al-Niqaya. His saying: 'Not for one who prays in his house in the city' means it is not disliked to leave them for him. The difference between them is that the resident, if he prays without them in reality, has prayed with them virtually because the mu'adhdhin is the deputy of the people of the neighborhood in them, so his act is like their act. As for the traveler, he has prayed without them in reality and virtually because the place where he is has not had adhan made in it at all for that prayer. This is in al-Kafi. Its implication is that if they have not made adhan in the neighborhood, then it is disliked to leave them for the one praying in his house. And it is explicitly stated in al-Mujtaba: if some of the travelers make adhan for the rest. And he left unrestricted regarding the one praying in his house, so it indicates that there is no difference between the single and... Both are the same. This is stated by Shaykh al-Islam. End. His saying: 'It is not permissible except with his master's permission.' In al-Nahr: And it is fitting that the private hireling also is not allowed to make adhan without his employer's permission. His saying: 'And it is explicitly stated in al-Mujtaba': there is consideration in this, because he did not explicitly state that, but it is understood by way of indication; but apparently his saying 'if some travelers make adhan' is not the expression of al-Mujtaba, but rather its original and 'and' with the conjunction on his saying 'if they have not made adhan' so the waw fell from the pen.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage deals with three topics: the adhan of a blind person, the slave's adhan, and the traveler's adhan.

First, the blind person (Ibn Umm Maktum) is discussed. The text clarifies that if a blind person has someone to keep the prayer times for him, his adhan is equivalent to that of a sighted person. This explains why the blind companion made adhan only after confirming the time by hearing others.

Second, the slave: if he makes adhan for himself, no permission is needed; but if he intends to be the assigned mu'adhdhin for the congregation, he needs his master's permission because it interferes with his service. This is extended to any hired worker (ajir khas) who must obtain his employer's permission.

Third, the traveler: leaving both adhan and iqamah is disliked for a traveler, but not for a resident praying in his house in a city. The proof is from the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith where the Prophet commanded the two travelers to make adhan and iqamah. Additional hadiths show the great reward for the solitary traveler who makes adhan. The rationale is that the mu'adhdhin acts as a deputy for the residents, so the resident's prayer without adhan is valid by deputation. The traveler has no such deputy, so his adhan is directly required. The text also notes that if the neighborhood has no adhan, then it is disliked for the resident to omit it as well.

Key Terms
المسافر (al-musāfir): Traveler; adhan is recommended and omitting it is disliked.
النية (al-niyābah): Deputyship; the mu'adhdhin acts as deputy for residents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a resident in a city excused from making adhan when praying in his house?
A) Because he is not traveling
B) Because the mu'adhdhin acts as his deputy
C) Because adhan is only for mosques
D) Because he can listen to the radio

Key Takeaway
A traveler should perform adhan and iqamah; it is a sunnah with great reward, and omitting both is disliked.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Leaving Adhan and Iqamah for the Traveler
Commentary on the ruling of leaving adhan and iqamah for travelers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a traveler leaving both adhan and iqamah, identify the proof from hadith, and explain why it is makruh tanzihi rather than haram.

Core Idea
Leaving both adhan and iqamah for a traveler is makruh tanzihi, not haram.

This lesson focuses on the specific ruling for a traveler who must perform salah alone. While adhan and iqamah are highly recommended (sunnah mu'akkadah) for the traveler, the Hanafi school holds that deliberately leaving both is disliked. We will examine the primary hadith evidence from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith and the reasoning that leads to the ruling of karahah tanzihiyyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and act
The subject is the traveler (musafir). The act under discussion is leaving both adhan and iqamah, not just one. The text states: 'kariha tarkuhuma li al-musafir'.
If only iqamah is left and adhan given, it is not disliked.
2
Examine the primary proof
The proof is the hadith from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: The Prophet commanded two companions traveling together to give adhan and iqamah. This is a command (amr) directed to travelers.
The hadith is narrated by Bukhari and Muslim, so it is authentic (sahih) but ahad.
3
Determine the level of the command
In Hanafi usul, an amr generally indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a qarinah (context) showing recommendation. Here, the context of travel and the fact that the companions were intentionally addressed as travelers shifts the command to recommendation (nadb).
The Shafi'i school holds the command as recommendation without the dislike.
4
Analyze the consequence of leaving
Since the command is for recommendation, leaving it is not sinful but is disliked (makruh tanzihi) because one is abandoning a recommended sunnah. The author explicitly says it is disliked, not forbidden.
The ruling is specific to leaving both; leaving only one is not makruh.
5
Apply to the traveler's scenario
If a traveler prays alone without adhan and iqamah, it is considered makruh tanzihi. However, if he gives either one, the dislike is removed.
The traveler's prayer is still valid; the dislike is for omitting an emphasized sunnah.

خلفهم أو لأن العبد مشغول بخدمة مولاه فلا يتفرغ للعلم كالأعرابي وهو ليس بموجود في الأذان لعدم احتياجه إلى العلم. وينبغي أن العبد إن أذن لنفسه لا يحتاج إلى إذن سيده، وإن أراد أن يكون مؤذناً للجماعة لم لا يرى شخصهم في الفلوات من العباد . قيد بتركهما لأنه لو ترك الأذان وأتى بالإقامة لا يكره لأثر علي رضي الله عنه ولو عكس يكره كما في شرح النقاية قوله ( لا لمصل في بيته في المصر) أي لا يكره تركهما له ، والفرق بينهما أن المقيم إذا صلى بدونهما حقيقة فقد صلى بهما حكماً لأن المؤذن نائب عن أهل المحلة فيهما فيكون فعله كفعلهم ، وأما المسافر فقد صلى بدونهما حقيقة وحكماً لأن المكان الذي هو فيه لم يؤذن فيه أصلاً لتلك الصلاة. كذا في الكافي ومفهومه أنه لو لم يؤذنوا في الحي فإنه يكره تركهما للمصلي في بيته وقد صرح به في المجتبى أنه لو أذن بعض المسافرين عن الباقين كما لا يخفى. وأطلق في المصلي في بيته فأفاد فيه نظر لأنه لم يصرح بذلك وإنما يفهم منه بطريق الدلالة لكن الظاهر أن قوله أنه لو أذن بعض المسافرين ليس عبارة المجتبى بل أصله وأنه» بواو العطف على قوله «أنه لو لم يؤذنوا فتكون الواو سقطت من قلم
Among them. As for Ibn Umm Maktum, the blind man, Bilal used to give the adhan before him. And in al-Nihayah: Whenever the blind person has someone with him who preserves the prayer times for him, then his adhan and the adhan of the sighted person are the same. Their imamate is disliked because people are averse to praying behind them, or because the slave is busy with his master's service so he does not have time for knowledge like the Bedouin, and this does not apply to the adhan because it does not require knowledge. It is appropriate that if a slave gives adhan for himself he does not need his master's permission, but if he wants to be a mu'adhdhin for the congregation it is not permissible except with his master's permission because it harms his service since he needs to observe the times, and I have not seen this in their words. His statement: 'and it is disliked to leave them for the traveler' means leaving the adhan and iqamah, due to what al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: 'I came to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, with a companion of mine. When we wanted to leave from him, he said to us: When the prayer is at hand, then give adhan and iqamah, and let the older of you lead you.' And since this address was to them and they needed no one to attend to them as travel companions, it is known that the individual also is recommended to do that. Specific hadiths have come regarding the individual in Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i: 'Your Lord wonders at a shepherd on the top of a mountain peak who gives adhan for prayer and prays. Allah says: Look at this servant of Mine, he gives adhan and iqamah for prayer, fearing Me. I have forgiven My servant and entered him into Paradise.' Salman al-Farisi said it. And from the Messenger of Allah: 'If a man is in a barren land and the time for prayer comes, let him perform wudu, and if he cannot find water, let him perform tayammum. If he gives iqamah, two angels pray with him; if he gives adhan and iqamah, soldiers of Allah whose ends cannot be seen pray behind him.' Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq. By this and similar narrations, it is known that the purpose of adhan is not limited to informing, but each one is also for publicizing this dhikr to spread remembrance of Allah and His religion in His land and to remind the servants of jinn and humans whose persons are not seen in the wilderness. The restriction is to leaving both, because if he leaves the adhan and performs iqamah, it is not disliked due to an effect from Ali, may Allah be pleased with him; but if he does the opposite, it is disliked, as in Sharh al-Niqayah. His statement: 'not for one who prays in his house in the city' means leaving both is not disliked for him. The difference between them is that the resident, if he prays without them in reality, has prayed with them effectively because the mu'adhdhin is his deputy in that neighborhood, so his action is like their action. As for the traveler, he has prayed without them in reality and effectively because the place he is in has not been given adhan at all for that prayer. This is in al-Kafi. Its implication is that if they do not give adhan in the district, then it is disliked to leave both for the one praying in his house, and it is stated in al-Mujtaba that if some of the travelers give adhan for the others, it is not disliked. He also spoke generally about the one praying in his house, so it indicates there is no difference between one person and a group. This is what Shaykh al-Islam mentioned. His statement: 'it is not permissible except with his master's permission' – al-Nahr said: it is appropriate that the specific hired worker is also such that his adhan is not allowed except with the permission of his employer. His statement: 'and it is stated explicitly in al-Mujtaba' – this requires consideration because it is not explicit; rather it is inferred by implication, but it is apparent that his statement 'if some of the travelers give adhan' is not the wording of al-Mujtaba; rather it is 'and that he' with a conjunctive waw linking to his statement 'if they do not give adhan', so the waw was omitted by the pen.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses various rulings related to the adhan and iqamah. It begins with a note about a blind person giving adhan: if someone reliable helps him know the times, his adhan is valid, but his imamate is disliked because people may avoid him. For a slave, if he gives adhan only for himself, he does not need his master's permission; but if he wants to be a mu'adhdhin for the congregation, he needs permission because it interferes with his service. The main ruling discussed is the dislike of leaving both adhan and iqamah for a traveler. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet commanded two companions to give adhan and iqamah while traveling, which indicates it is also recommended for the individual. Additional hadiths emphasize the virtue of adhan even for one alone in the wilderness. The text then distinguishes between a traveler and a resident praying in his house in the city. For the resident, it is not disliked to leave adhan and iqamah if the people of the neighborhood have already performed them, because the mu'adhdhin acts as their deputy. The traveler, however, does not have that deputy, so leaving both is disliked. If only iqamah is given, it is not disliked; but leaving iqamah and giving only adhan is disliked. The passage also mentions that if the residents of a district do not give adhan at all, then it becomes disliked for an individual in his house to leave them. There is also a note about a slave's need for permission, which al-Nahr extends to hired workers. The commentary ends with a critical note about a statement in al-Mujtaba regarding the wording.

Key Terms
أذان (adhan): The call to prayer consisting of specified phrases, announced at the beginning of the prayer time.
إقامة (iqamah): The second call to prayer immediately before the prayer begins, similar to adhan but with added phrase 'qad qamat al-salah'.
مسافر (musafir): A person traveling a distance that permits qasr (shortening) of prayer, typically defined as three days' journey for a camel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a traveler who leaves both adhan and iqamah?
A) It is permissible without any dislike.
B) It is makruh tanzihi (disliked) to leave both.
C) It is haram (forbidden).
D) It is wajib (obligatory) to perform both.

Key Takeaway
A traveler leaving both adhan and iqamah is makruh tanzihi; leaving only one is not disliked.

Ruling for the Resident Praying Alone in the City
Explanation of why it is not disliked for a resident in the city to leave adhan and iqamah when praying alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why it is not disliked for a resident in the city to leave adhan and iqamah when praying alone at home, and identify the condition under which it becomes disliked.

Core Idea
A resident in the city prays 'with' adhan through the deputy of the mu'adhdhin.

The previous lesson covered the traveler. Now we examine a different scenario: a resident who prays alone in his house within a city where the congregation performs adhan and iqamah. The Hanafi school rules that it is not disliked for him to leave them. This is because the mu'adhdhin acts as his deputy, so he has effectively participated in the adhan. However, if the people of the district do not perform adhan at all, then it becomes disliked for him to leave them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception
The text says: 'la li musallin fi baytihi fi al-misr' meaning the ruling of dislike does not apply to one who prays in his house in the city. Recognize this as an exception to the general rule for travelers.
The exception is specific to the resident in the city, not the traveler.
2
Understand the reasoning: na'ib (deputy)
The reason is that the mu'adhdhin of the district is considered a deputy (na'ib) for all the residents in that area. When the mu'adhdhin gives adhan, it is as if every resident has performed it. Therefore, if a person prays alone at home, he is covered by the adhan of the mosque.
This is a legal fiction (hukman) that makes the resident's prayer effectively accompanied by adhan.
3
Contrast with the traveler
The traveler does not have a mu'adhdhin acting as deputy in his location. He is in a place where no adhan has been given for that prayer. Therefore, he must either perform it himself or it becomes disliked to leave both.
This is why the traveler is subject to dislike while the resident is not.
4
Identify the conditional exception
The implication (mafhum) is that if the people of the district do not give adhan at all (i.e., no mu'adhdhin), then the resident's prayer at home becomes like the traveler's situation, and leaving both becomes disliked for him as well.
This is derived from the text: 'wa mafhumuhu annahu law lam yu'adhdhinu fi al-hayy...'
5
Apply to scenarios
If a resident hears the adhan from the mosque and then prays at home without repeating it, it is not disliked. But if there is no adhan in his neighborhood, he should perform adhan and iqamah or at least not leave both.
The ruling applies whether he prays alone or with his family; no difference.
