Among them. As for Ibn Umm Maktum, the blind man, Bilal used to give the adhan before him. And in al-Nihayah: Whenever the blind person has someone with him who preserves the prayer times for him, then his adhan and the adhan of the sighted person are the same. Their imamate is disliked because people are averse to praying behind them, or because the slave is busy with his master's service so he does not have time for knowledge like the Bedouin, and this does not apply to the adhan because it does not require knowledge. It is appropriate that if a slave gives adhan for himself he does not need his master's permission, but if he wants to be a mu'adhdhin for the congregation it is not permissible except with his master's permission because it harms his service since he needs to observe the times, and I have not seen this in their words. His statement: 'and it is disliked to leave them for the traveler' means leaving the adhan and iqamah, due to what al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: 'I came to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, with a companion of mine. When we wanted to leave from him, he said to us: When the prayer is at hand, then give adhan and iqamah, and let the older of you lead you.' And since this address was to them and they needed no one to attend to them as travel companions, it is known that the individual also is recommended to do that. Specific hadiths have come regarding the individual in Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i: 'Your Lord wonders at a shepherd on the top of a mountain peak who gives adhan for prayer and prays. Allah says: Look at this servant of Mine, he gives adhan and iqamah for prayer, fearing Me. I have forgiven My servant and entered him into Paradise.' Salman al-Farisi said it. And from the Messenger of Allah: 'If a man is in a barren land and the time for prayer comes, let him perform wudu, and if he cannot find water, let him perform tayammum. If he gives iqamah, two angels pray with him; if he gives adhan and iqamah, soldiers of Allah whose ends cannot be seen pray behind him.' Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq. By this and similar narrations, it is known that the purpose of adhan is not limited to informing, but each one is also for publicizing this dhikr to spread remembrance of Allah and His religion in His land and to remind the servants of jinn and humans whose persons are not seen in the wilderness. The restriction is to leaving both, because if he leaves the adhan and performs iqamah, it is not disliked due to an effect from Ali, may Allah be pleased with him; but if he does the opposite, it is disliked, as in Sharh al-Niqayah. His statement: 'not for one who prays in his house in the city' means leaving both is not disliked for him. The difference between them is that the resident, if he prays without them in reality, has prayed with them effectively because the mu'adhdhin is his deputy in that neighborhood, so his action is like their action. As for the traveler, he has prayed without them in reality and effectively because the place he is in has not been given adhan at all for that prayer. This is in al-Kafi. Its implication is that if they do not give adhan in the district, then it is disliked to leave both for the one praying in his house, and it is stated in al-Mujtaba that if some of the travelers give adhan for the others, it is not disliked. He also spoke generally about the one praying in his house, so it indicates there is no difference between one person and a group. This is what Shaykh al-Islam mentioned. His statement: 'it is not permissible except with his master's permission' – al-Nahr said: it is appropriate that the specific hired worker is also such that his adhan is not allowed except with the permission of his employer. His statement: 'and it is stated explicitly in al-Mujtaba' – this requires consideration because it is not explicit; rather it is inferred by implication, but it is apparent that his statement 'if some of the travelers give adhan' is not the wording of al-Mujtaba; rather it is 'and that he' with a conjunctive waw linking to his statement 'if they do not give adhan', so the waw was omitted by the pen.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses various rulings related to the adhan and iqamah. It begins with a note about a blind person giving adhan: if someone reliable helps him know the times, his adhan is valid, but his imamate is disliked because people may avoid him. For a slave, if he gives adhan only for himself, he does not need his master's permission; but if he wants to be a mu'adhdhin for the congregation, he needs permission because it interferes with his service. The main ruling discussed is the dislike of leaving both adhan and iqamah for a traveler. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet commanded two companions to give adhan and iqamah while traveling, which indicates it is also recommended for the individual. Additional hadiths emphasize the virtue of adhan even for one alone in the wilderness. The text then distinguishes between a traveler and a resident praying in his house in the city. For the resident, it is not disliked to leave adhan and iqamah if the people of the neighborhood have already performed them, because the mu'adhdhin acts as their deputy. The traveler, however, does not have that deputy, so leaving both is disliked. If only iqamah is given, it is not disliked; but leaving iqamah and giving only adhan is disliked. The passage also mentions that if the residents of a district do not give adhan at all, then it becomes disliked for an individual in his house to leave them. There is also a note about a slave's need for permission, which al-Nahr extends to hired workers. The commentary ends with a critical note about a statement in al-Mujtaba regarding the wording.

Key Terms
مقيم (muqim): A resident who is not traveling; one who is settled in a city or town.
نائب (na'ib): Deputy; the mu'adhdhin acts as a representative for the residents of the district in performing adhan and iqamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does it become disliked for a resident in the city to leave adhan and iqamah when praying alone at home?
A) Never, because he is a resident.
B) Only if he prays in congregation.
C) If the people of his district do not give adhan at all.
D) Only if he is a traveler.

Key Takeaway
A resident in the city is excused from adhan at home due to the deputy role of the mu'adhdhin, unless the district itself neglects adhan, in which case the traveler's ruling applies.

The Lexical and Technical Definition of Shart
Lexical and technical definition of shurut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the lexical definition of shart and distinguish it from rukn in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A shart is an external prerequisite; a rukn is an internal pillar. Knowing the difference prevents invalid worship.

This lesson opens the chapter on the conditions (shurut) of salah. The author first clarifies the Arabic word 'shart'—its lexical origin and plural forms—before applying it as a technical term. Understanding this linguistic foundation helps you avoid conflating conditions with pillars, a common source of confusion in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the lexical definition
The text states that 'shart' (pl. shurut) is originally a verbal noun from the verb sharata. Note the pattern: fi'l (فعل). This is the standard Arabic plural.
Another plural, shara'it, exists with singular sharitah, but it is rare in fiqh.
2
Contrast with rukn
In Hanafi usul, a shart is external to the act (e.g., wudu before prayer), while a rukn is internal (e.g., ruku'). The text does not elaborate this contrast, but it is essential to apply the definition correctly.
Shurut must be present before the act begins; arkan are performed during the act.
3
Connect to the chapter's subject
Recognize that the entire chapter on shurut will now enumerate the specific prerequisites for salah. This definition prepares you to receive and categorize them accurately.
Common shurut include purity, covering the awrah, facing qiblah, and correct time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Chapter on the Conditions of Prayer. They (shurut) are the plural of shart, on the pattern of fi'l, and its origin is a verbal noun. As for shara'it, its singular is sharitah. Thus in al-Nasikh: consider his statement: 'In summary, the adhan and iqamah etc. if he delayed it to the following statement it would be more appropriate.' His statement: 'Because the solitary woman gives iqamah and does not give adhan as we mentioned earlier' – al-Ramli said: 'What he stated earlier in explaining his statement: 'And he gives adhan for the missed prayer if he leaves them is the sunnah in the case of being alone, rather he made it primary, so refer to it.' Chapter on the Conditions of Prayer. His statement: 'and its origin is a verbal noun i.e., the verbal noun of sharata yashritu with fatha on the 'ayn in the past and damma and kasra in the 'ayn...' incomplete.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the conditions (shurut) of salah. The author defines the term: 'shurut' is the plural of 'shart', which originally is a verbal noun. Another plural form is 'shara'it', with singular 'sharitah'. This lexical clarification is typical in fiqh works to distinguish between linguistic and technical meanings. The text then includes a critical note from al-Nasikh about the arrangement of a previous section (likely a cross-reference to the discussion on adhan and iqamah). It also includes a brief discussion on whether a solitary woman gives iqamah but not adhan, with a reference to al-Ramli. The final part repeats the chapter heading and begins explaining the verbal noun derivation of 'shart', but the text cuts off. In the Hanafi school, the conditions of prayer include taharah from hadath and najasah, covering the private parts, facing the qiblah, and the entry of time. These are prerequisites, not integral parts (arkan).

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition; a prerequisite for the validity of an act of worship or contract, not part of its essence.
شريطة (sharitah): A rare singular form of shara'it (conditions), used lexically but not commonly in fiqh terminology.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A shart is an external prerequisite for an act of worship, distinct from a rukn; the lexical definition helps anchor this technical concept.

General Ruling on Adhan and Iqamah for Mosque People and Others
Rulings on adhan/iqamah for mosque people vs. others

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for adhan and iqamah for the people of a mosque versus others, and apply the distinction to scenarios such as entering a mosque after congregation.

Core Idea
Adhan and iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah for mosque people; for others they are merely sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the ruling of adhan and iqamah for various groups. A common mistake is to assume that these calls are always emphasized sunnah regardless of context. The Hanafi school distinguishes between those responsible for a mosque's congregation and others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary distinction
Determine the two main categories: 'people of the mosque' (those who are part of a fixed congregation) and 'others' (those who are not).
The text defines this distinction clearly.
2
Determine the hukm for mosque people
For mosque people, leaving either adhan or iqamah is makruh tanzihi, indicating it is sunnah mu'akkadah.
Makruh tanzihi means disliked but not sinful.
3
Determine the hukm for others
For others (e.g., individuals in their homes, travelers), adhan and iqamah are not sunnah mu'akkadah; they are simply recommended (sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah).
Omission is not disliked.
4
Analyze the exception: entering a mosque after congregation
If someone enters a mosque after the congregation has prayed, he should not give adhan or iqamah; he may pray individually without them.
This is because the mosque's call has already been made.
5
Consider the case of a group in a house relying on the mosque's adhan
A group praying at home may rely on the mosque's adhan; their prayer is valid but they have done wrong (by not giving adhan themselves as a group).
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between a single person (no wrong) and a group (wrong).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب شروط الصلاة هي طهارة بدنه من حدث وخبث وثوبه ومكانه وستر عورته وهي من تحت والجماعة. وعن أبي حنيفة في قوم صلوا في المصر في منزل واكتفوا بأذان الناس أجزأهم وقد أساءوا ففرق بين الواحد والجماعة في هذه الرواية والتقييد بالبيت ليس احترازياً بل المصلي في المسجد إذا صلى بعد صلاة الجماعة لا يكره له تركهما بل ليس له أن يؤذن. وفي السراج الوهاج : وإن دخل مسجداً ليصلي فإنه لا يؤذن ولا يقيم وإن أذن في مسجد جماعة وصلوا يكره لغيرهم أن يؤذنوا ويعيدوا الجماعة ولكن يصلوا وحداناً، وإن كان المسجد على الطريق فلا بأس أن يؤذنوا فيه ويقيموا .اهـ. وفي الخلاصة : جماعة من أهل المسجد أذنوا في المسجد على وجه المخافتة بحيث لم يسمع غيرهم، ثم حضر من أهل المسجد قوم وعلموا فلهم أن يصلوا بالجماعة على وجهها ولا عبرة للجماعة الأولى والتقييد بالمصر ليس احترازياً أيضاً بل القرية كالمصران كان في القرية مسجد فيه أذان وإقامة وإن لم يكن فيها مسجد، فحكمه حكم المسافر . كذا في شرح النقاية للشمني والحاصل أن الأذان والإقامة كل منهما في حق أهل المسجد يكره ترك واحد منهما أذاناً أو إقامة وأما غيرهم فلا يكونان سنة مؤكدة. قوله وندبا لهما أي الأذان والإقامة للمسافر والمصلي في بيته في المصر ليكون الأداء على هيئة الجماعة. وفي السراج الوهاج ولو أذن المسافر راكباً فلا بأس به من غير كراهة وينزل للإقامة. وفي الظهيرية بين له مسجد يكره أن يصلي فيه ويترك الإقامة. قوله (لا للنساء) أي لا يندب للنساء أذان ولا إقامة لأنهما من سنن الجماعة المستحبة. قيد بالنساء أي جماعة النساء لأن المرأة المنفردة تقيم ولا تؤذن كما قدمناه وظاهر ما في السراج الوهاج أنها لا تقيم أيضاً وأشار إلى أن العبيد لا أذان ولا إقامة عليهم لأنها من سنن الجماعة وجماعتهم غير مشروعة، ولهذا لم يشرع التكبير عقبها أيام التشريق. ذكره الشارح والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
Chapter of Conditions of Prayer: They are purification of his body from ritual impurity and filth, and his garment and his place, and covering his nakedness, and it is from under, and congregation. And from Abu Hanifa regarding a group who prayed in the city in a house and were satisfied with the people's adhan: it suffices them but they have done wrong. So he distinguished between the single person and the group in this narration. And the restriction to 'house' is not exclusive; rather, the one praying in the mosque if he prays after the congregational prayer, it is not disliked for him to leave them, rather he should not give adhan. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he enters a mosque to pray, he should not give adhan or iqamah. If some gave adhan in a mosque and they prayed, it is disliked for others to give adhan and repeat the congregation, but they should pray individually. If the mosque is on the road, there is no harm in them giving adhan and iqamah. End quote. And in al-Khulasa: A congregation from the mosque people gave adhan in the mosque in a subdued manner such that others did not hear them, then some mosque people came and knew, so they may pray in congregation properly, and the first congregation is disregarded. And the restriction to 'city' is not exclusive; rather, a village is like a city if there is a mosque in the village with adhan and iqamah, but if there is no mosque in it, its ruling is that of a traveler. Likewise in Sharh al-Nuqaya by al-Shumnuni. And the conclusion is that adhan and iqamah, for the mosque people, it is disliked to leave either one, whether adhan or iqamah. As for others, they are not emphasized sunnah. His statement: 'and recommended for them both' meaning adhan and iqamah for the traveler and the one praying in his house in the city so that the performance is in the manner of congregation. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If a traveler gives adhan while riding, there is no harm in it without dislike, and he descends for iqamah. And in al-Zahiriyya: If there is a mosque for him, it is disliked for him to pray in it and leave the iqamah. His statement: 'Not for women' meaning adhan and iqamah are not recommended for women because they are from the sunan of congregation that is mustahabb. Restricted by women meaning congregation of women, because the solitary woman performs iqamah and does not give adhan as we presented, and the apparent meaning of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is that she also does not give iqamah. And he indicated that slaves have no adhan or iqamah upon them because they are from the sunan of congregation, and their congregation is not legislated, and for this reason the takbir following them on the days of Tashriq is not legislated. The commentator mentioned it, and Allah most high knows best.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a legal commentary on the rulings of adhan and iqamah. It begins by stating that the chapter on conditions of prayer includes the sunnah of congregation. The passage then narrates a view from Imam Abu Hanifa: if a group of people in a city pray in a house and rely on the adhan of others (i.e., the mosque's adhan), their prayer is valid but they have done wrong. Abu Hanifa distinguishes between a single person and a group in this regard. The restriction to 'house' is not exclusive; rather, if someone prays in a mosque after the congregational prayer, he should not give adhan himself, and it is not disliked for him to omit adhan and iqamah. The passage then cites al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: one entering a mosque to pray should not give adhan or iqamah; if others already gave adhan and prayed, it is disliked for others to give adhan and repeat the congregation—they should pray individually. However, if the mosque is on a public road (i.e., a mosque that is not for a specific neighborhood), there is no harm in giving adhan and iqamah. From al-Khulasa: if a mosque congregation gives adhan quietly so that only they hear, and then other mosque people arrive, the newcomers may pray in congregation; the first congregation is disregarded. The ruling applies to villages as well: if there is a mosque with adhan, it is like a city; if no mosque, the ruling is that of a traveler. The conclusion: for the people of a mosque, it is disliked to leave either adhan or iqamah. For others (e.g., individuals in their homes), they are not emphasized sunnah. The commentator then explains that adhan and iqamah are recommended (mandub) for travelers and for those praying at home in a city, to follow the manner of congregation. A traveler may give adhan while riding without dislike, but must descend for iqamah. If there is a mosque nearby, it is disliked to pray leaving iqamah. For women, adhan and iqamah are not recommended because they are sunan of congregation that are mustahabb. The restriction to women refers to a congregation of women; a solitary woman may give iqamah (according to some) but not adhan, though al-Siraj al-Wahhaj suggests she does not even give iqamah. Slaves have no adhan or iqamah because their congregation is not legislated; hence the takbir on Tashriq days is not legislated for them.

Key Terms
أذان (adhān): The call to prayer announcing the time and inviting the congregation.
إقامة (iqāmah): The second call to prayer just before the prayer begins.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah whose omission is disliked (makruh tanzihi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid but they have done wrong.
B) Invalid.
C) Valid and they have done no wrong.
D) Requires repetition.

Key Takeaway
Adhan and iqamah are sunnah mu'akkadah for mosque people; for others they are merely recommended.

Rulings on Adhan and Iqamah for Travelers, Women, and Slaves
Specific rulings for traveler, women, slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for adhan and iqamah for travelers, women, and slaves, and explain the reasons based on Hanafi principles.

Core Idea
Travelers may give adhan while riding, but women and slaves are not required because these acts are tied to legitimate congregation.

The passage continues with specific rulings for three groups: the traveler, women, and slaves. These rulings illustrate that adhan and iqamah are primarily for establishing congregational prayer. Where congregation is not legislated or not emphasized, these acts are not prescribed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three groups
The passage discusses: (1) traveler, (2) women (including a congregation of women), (3) slaves.
2
Ruling for the traveler
The traveler may give adhan while riding (no dislike), but must dismount for iqamah. If he is near a mosque, it is disliked to pray there without iqamah.
Adhan while riding is permissible; iqamah requires standing.
3
Ruling for women
Adhan and iqamah are not recommended for women because they are from the sunan of congregation. A solitary woman may give iqamah according to some, but the relied-upon view is that she gives neither.
The text notes an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Ruling for slaves
Slaves have no adhan or iqamah upon them because their congregation is not legislated; hence the takbir of Tashriq is also not required for them.
This is based on the same principle: congregation is not prescribed for slaves.

Chapter of Conditions of Prayer: They are purification of his body from ritual impurity and filth, and his garment and his place, and covering his nakedness, and it is from under, and congregation. Definition and Classification of Shart (Condition) in Hanafi Usul
Definition and classification of 'shart' with commentary expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define shart (condition) in its legal and linguistic senses, distinguish it from rukn, illa, sabab, and alama, and apply the classification to examples from Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A condition is something upon which an act depends but is not part of it, and it does not cause the ruling.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the term 'shart' (condition) from the chapter heading 'Conditions of Prayer'. Understanding this term accurately is essential: confusion between shart and related concepts like rukn or illa leads to errors in deriving and applying rulings. The commentator, following the Hanafi usul tradition, clarifies the linguistic and Shar'i definitions and categorizes external factors affecting rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition of shart
From lexical works: al-shart (with sukun) means the known condition; al-shart (with tashreeq) means a sign. Confirm that the correct plural in the chapter heading is shurūṭ, not sharā'iṭ.
2
State the Shar'i definition
Shart in Shari'ah is 'that upon which the existence of something depends and is not part of it'. Note the key distinctions: dependence (tawaqquf) and externality (khārijī).
3
Distinguish shart from rukn, illa, sabab, and alama
Using the uṣūlī classification: rukn is internal (like ruku'), illa is effective cause (like marriage for halal), sabab is a means (like time), shart is a non-effective dependence (like wudu), alama is an indicator (like adhan). Understand each with examples.
4
Differentiate real vs. conventional conditions
Real conditions depend on reality (e.g., life for knowledge). Conventional conditions are set by Shari'ah (e.g., wudu for prayer) or by a mukallaf with Shari'ah permission (e.g., conditional clauses).
5
Apply to the conditions of prayer
The chapter lists conditions like purification from hadath and khabath. Note that takbir al-tahrimah is a condition but not listed here because it is the starting point, not a prerequisite before commencement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب شروط الصلاة قوله: (وأصله مصدر أي مصدر شرط يشرط بفتح العين في الماضي وضمها وكسرها في ضياء الحلوم مختصر شمس العلوم في اللغة. فمن عبر هنا بالشرائط فمخالف للغة كما عرفت وللقاعدة التصريفية فإن «فعائل» لم يحفظ جمعاً لفعل بفتح الفاء وسكون العين بخلاف التعبير لأن مفرده فريضة كصحائف جمع صحيفة وهو في اللغة العلامة. كذا بالفرائض فإنه صحيح في فتح القدير. وأما في الصحاح : الشرط معروف والشرط بالتحريك العلامة، وقوله تعالى فقد جاء أشراطها [محمد : ۱۸] أي علاماتها. وفي الشريعة ما يتوقف عليه وجود الشيء ولا يكون داخلاً فيه. وقد قسم الأصوليون الخارج المتعلق بالحكم إلى مؤثر فيه ومفض إليه بلا تأثير. فالأول والطهارة للصلاة، وغير شرعي أي بجعل المكلف بتعليق تصرفه عليه مع إجازة الشرع كأن دخلت الدار فكذا. وذكر الشمني أن المراد بالشروط هنا ما لا يكون المكلف بحصولها شارعاً في الصلاة احترازاً عن التحريمة فإنها شرط عندنا ولا تذكر في هذا الباب .اهـ وأطلق الشروط ولم يقيدها بالتقدم كما في مختصر لأنه لا حاجة إليه لأنها صفة كاشفة لا مخصصة إذ الشرط لا يكون إلا متقدماً، وما القدوري ذكره الشارحون بخلاف ذلك فقد رده في فتح القدير. من الحدث شريطة قوله : (هي طهارة بدنه من حدث وخبث وثوبه ومكانه أما طهارة بدنه فبآية الوضوء والغسل، ومن الخبث فبقوله للتنزهوا من البول فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه؟ ولحديث فاطمة بنت أبي حبيش اغسلي عنك الدم وصلي والحدث مانعية شرعية قائمة بالأعضاء إلى غاية استعمال المزيل والخبث عين مستقذرة شرعاً. وقدم الحدث لقوته لأن المضارع اهـ حلية قوله : (وأما في الصحاح الخ) استدراك على ما في كتب الفقه من أن المفسر بالعلامة هو الشرط محركاً فقيدوه بذلك. وفي القاموس : الشرط إلزام الشيء والتزامه في البيع ونحوه، جمعه شروط وبالتحريك العلامة جمعه أشراط .اهـ. ولعل الفقهاء وقفوا على تفسيره بالعلامة أيضاً. والحاصل أن الشروط جمع شرط ساكناً، والأشراط جمعه محركاً، والشرائط جمع المشقوقة الأذن من الإبل والشاة كما في القاموس فقول النهر وهي أي الشروط جمع شرط محركاً العلامة لغة فسهو من قلم الناسخ قوله : ( وقد قسم الأصوليون (الخ) قال الشيخ إسمعيل : بمعنى اعلم أن المتعلق بالمشروع إما أن يكون داخلاً في ماهيته فيسمى ركناً كالركوع في الصلاة، أو خارجاً عنه. وهذا إما أن يؤثر فيه كعقد النكاح للحل فيسمى علة، أو لا يؤثر وهذا إما أن يكون موصلاً إليه في الجملة كالوقت ويسمى سبباً، أو لا يوصل وهذا إما أن يتوقف الشيء عليه كالوضوء للصلاة فيسمى شرطاً أو لا يتوقف كالأذان فيسمى علامة كما بسطه البرجندي. وبه يتضح ما في قوله تبعاً للعناية الشرط ما يتوقف عليه وجود الشيء ولا يكون داخلاً فيه من أنه لا بد أن يكون غير مؤثر
Chapter of Conditions of Prayer: His statement: (and its origin is a verbal noun) meaning a verbal noun from sharaṭa yashriṭu with fatha on the 'ayn in the past and damma and kasra on it in Diya' al-Hulūm, an abridgement of Shams al-'Ulūm in language. So whoever here uses 'shara'iṭ' is violating the language as you know, and the morphological rule, for 'fa'ā'il' is not preserved as a plural of fa'l with fatha on the fa and sukun on the 'ayn, unlike the expression because its singular is farīḍah, like ṣaḥā'if is plural of ṣaḥīfah. And it is in the language: the sign. Likewise in al-Farā'iḍ it is correct in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. As for in al-Ṣiḥāḥ: al-sharṭ is known, and al-sharṭ with tashreeq is the sign, and His statement 'indeed the signs thereof have come' (Muhammad 18) meaning its signs. And in the Sharī'ah: it is that upon which the existence of something depends and is not part of it. And the uṣūliyyūn have divided the external related to the ruling into that which has an effect on it and that which leads to it without effect. The first is the 'illa, and the second is the sabab. Otherwise, if the existence depends on it then it is shart; otherwise if it indicates it then it is 'alāmah. And shart is of two types: real and conventional. The first is that upon which the thing depends in reality; the second is Shar'i, i.e., by the making of the Sharī'ah, so it depends Shar'iyan, like witnesses for marriage and purity for prayer; and non-Shar'i, i.e., by the making of the accountable person by suspending his action upon it with the permission of the Sharī'ah, like 'if you enter the house, then so and so'. And al-Shumnunī mentioned that what is meant by the conditions here is that by attaining which the accountable person does not commence the prayer, as a precaution against the takbīr al-taḥrīmah, for it is a condition according to us and is not mentioned in this chapter. End quote. And he mentioned the conditions without restricting them to precedence as in al-Mukhtaṣar, because there is no need for it, since they are a descriptive attribute not a specifying one, for a condition is only prior. And what al-Qudūrī mentioned, the commentators said otherwise, and he rejected it in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. 'From the event' is a condition. His statement: (they are purification of his body from ritual impurity and filth, and his garment and his place) as for purification of his body, it is by the verse of wuḍū' and ghusl; and from filth, by his statement: 'Shield yourselves from urine, for most of the punishment of the grave is from it?' and by the hadith of Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh: 'Wash the blood from you and pray.' And ritual impurity is a Shar'i preventative quality residing in the limbs until the use of the remover; and filth is something considered impure in the Sharī'ah. And he placed ritual impurity first because of its strength. End quote from Ḥilyah. His statement: (And as for in al-Ṣiḥāḥ) is a detraction from what is in the fiqh books that the one interpreted as the sign is al-sharṭ with tashreeq, so they restricted it to that. And in al-Qāmūs: al-sharṭ is the binding of something and its obligation in sale and the like, its plural is shurūṭ, and with tashreeq it is the sign, its plural is ashrāṭ. End quote. And perhaps the fuqahā' relied on its interpretation as sign as well. The conclusion is that al-shurūṭ is the plural of sharṭ (sakin), and al-ashrāṭ is its plural with tashreeq, and al-sharā'iṭ is the plural of the animal with split ear among camels and sheep as in al-Qāmūs. So the statement of al-Nahr 'and they, i.e., al-shurūṭ, is the plural of sharṭ with tashreeq meaning sign in language' is an oversight from the copyist's pen. His statement: (and the uṣūliyyūn have divided) said al-Shaykh Ismā'īl: meaning, know that that which is related to the legislated matter either is internal to its essence, then it is called a rukn, like bowing in prayer; or external to it. And this either has an effect on it, like the marriage contract for permissibility, then it is called 'illa; or has no effect, and this either leads to it in general, like the time, and is called sabab; or does not lead, and this either the thing depends on it, like wuḍū' for prayer, then it is called shart; or does not depend, like adhan, then it is called 'alāmah, as expounded by al-Birjandī. And by this is clarified what is in his statement following al-'Ināyah: 'shart is that upon which the existence of something depends and is not part of it' that it must be ineffective.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a detailed linguistic and legal analysis of the term 'shart' (condition) as used in the chapter heading 'Conditions of Prayer'. The commentator begins by noting that the plural of shart is shurūṭ, not sharā'iṭ, which is a plural for a different word. He cites lexical works: al-Ṣiḥāḥ defines shart as known, and with tashreeq (shart) as a sign, citing the Quranic verse 'indeed the signs thereof have come' (Surah Muhammad, 18). He then provides a Sharī'ah definition: 'something upon which the existence of something else depends and is not part of it.' The commentator then presents the uṣūlī classification of external factors related to a ruling: effective cause ('illa), means to it without effect (sabab), condition (shart), and indicator (alāmah). A condition is further divided into real (e.g., life for knowledge) and conventional—the latter being either Sharʿī (e.g., wuḍū for prayer) or non-Sharʿī (e.g., conditional clauses in contracts). He quotes al-Shumnunī that the conditions intended in this chapter are those that, if not present, prevent one from even beginning the prayer, thus excluding the opening takbir (takbīr al-taḥrīmah), which is a condition according to the Hanafis but is not discussed here. The commentator also addresses the disagreement over whether conditions must precede the act; the correct view is that they must be prior by nature. The passage then returns to the specific conditions of prayer: purification from hadath and khabath, covering the 'awrah, etc., and cites the relevant Quranic and hadith evidence. Finally, he reiterates the classification of related concepts: rukn (internal, part of act), 'illa (effective cause), sabab (means), shart (condition), and 'alāmah (indicator), clarifying that a condition is 'ineffective' (ghayr mu'aththir) in the sense that it does not cause the ruling but is required for its validity.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): In Sharī'ah: something upon which the existence of another thing depends but is not part of it.
ركن (rukn): Something internal to the essence of an act, like bowing (ruku') in prayer.
علة (ʿilla): The effective cause that produces the ruling, e.g., marriage contract for permissibility (halal).
سبب (sabab): Something that leads to the ruling without being its cause, like time for prayer.
علامة (ʿalāmah): An indicator that does not depend on the act for its existence, e.g., adhan for prayer time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is the plural of 'shart' (meaning condition) used in the chapter heading?
A) شروط
B) شرائط
C) أشراط
D) شرطة

Key Takeaway
A condition (shart) in Hanafi usul is an external prerequisite for an act's validity, distinct from pillars, causes, means, and indicators; it is non-effective (ghayr mu'aththir).

The Obligation of Covering the 'Awrah: Proofs and Consensus
Full Hanafi proof and exception for minors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on covering the 'awrah in prayer, identify the three proofs (ijma', Quran, hadith), and explain the exception for minors using istihsan.

Core Idea
Covering the 'awrah is fard by ijma', Quran, and Sunnah; only pre-pubescent girls are excused by istihsan.

This lesson opens the discussion on the obligation of covering the private parts during prayer. The Hanafi school holds this as a fard (obligatory) condition, supported by a firm consensus (ijma') and primary texts. We will examine the proofs and note an important exception for minors based on juristic preference (istihsan).

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and its basis
The text states covering is fard due to ijma' (consensus). Note how the author asserts that later opposition (e.g., Qadi Isma'il al-Maliki) is invalid after the consensus was settled.
Ijma' is a binding proof in Hanafi usul.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof (7:31)
The verse 'Take your adornment at every mosque' is interpreted as covering the 'awrah at every prayer. Explain the metonymy: 'mosque' stands for 'prayer' because covering is for prayer, not for the building (tawaf naked is allowed).
The operative phrase is 'zinatakum' (your adornment) understood as covering.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith 'Allah does not accept the prayer of a menstruating woman except with a khimar' is used. Identify that it applies to mature women only, as the term 'ha'id' means one who has reached menstruation age.
The hadith is cited to show the obligation for adult females; the text later uses it to derive the minor's exception.
4
Derive the exception for minors by istihsan
The text argues that the hadith's restriction to 'ha'id' excludes pre-pubescent girls. Further, obligations (khitab) fall away due to childhood, so a girl near puberty (murahiqah) who prays without headcover is not required to repeat, by istihsan. Compare to the stricter qiyas that would require repetition.
Istihsan overrides qiyas in this case because the address of obligations is weak for minors.

بأن له ثوباً إذ العادم له يستوي في حقه الصافي وغيره، وحينئذ فلا يجوز له الإيماء للفرض اهـ. قال العلامة الشيخ اسمعيل : ولي في الكلامين نظر لإمكان تصوير ركوعه وسجوده في الماء الكدر بحيث لا يظهر من بدنه شيء إذا سدّ منافذه بل ما يفعله الغطاس في استخراج الغريق أبلغ من ذلك. قوله : (لكن في السراج الخ) وجه الاستدراك أن قوله فعليه أن يزره يفيد الوجوب وهو ظاهر الحديث المذكور. قال البرهان الحلبي في شرح المنية والدليل يساعده وهو أن الستر وجب شرطاً للصلاة ذاتها لا لخوف رؤية العورة فيها، وإذا كان بحال لو نظر لرأى بلا تكلف لم يوجد الشرط وهو الستر، ولذا
His saying: (And covering his private parts) due to consensus that it is fard in prayer, as transmitted by more than one transmitter, until some Malikis happened and differed in it, like Qadi Isma'il, and that is not permissible after the establishment of consensus. Supporting it is His saying: 'O children of Adam, take your adornment at every mosque' (7:31), meaning its place. What is intended is that which covers his private parts at every prayer, using the name of the state for the place in the first and the opposite in the second. And his saying (peace be upon him): 'Allah does not accept the prayer of a menstruating woman except with a khimar' meaning the mature woman, called ha'id because she has reached the age of menstruation, and the restriction to the menstruating woman excludes the one below puberty. As it is said in al-Muhit: A young girl on the verge of puberty who prays without wudu or naked is ordered to repeat, but if she prays without a headcover, her prayer is complete by istihsan, because his saying (peace be upon him): 'A menstruating woman does not pray without a headcover' does not apply to non-menstruating women, and because covering the head's private part fell due to the excuse of slavery, then the excuse of childhood is more appropriate, because the address of obligations falls due to the excuse of childhood, unlike other conditions which do not fall due to the excuse of childhood. End quote. The linguists said: The private part (awrah) is so called because of the ugliness of its appearance and the lowering of glances from it, derived from al-awr which is deficiency, defect, and ugliness, from which is 'awr of the eye and the ugly word 'awra'. The term is applied to what is used to cover, thus including what is permissible to wear and what is not. So if he covers it with a silk garment and prays, the prayer is valid but he sins, like praying in usurped land. If he finds no other, he prays in it, not naked. The limit of covering is that what is underneath is not seen; so if he covers it with a thin garment that describes what is underneath, it is not permissible. It includes whether someone is present or not; even if he prays naked in a dark room, even with a pure garment, it is not permissible by consensus, because covering contains the right of Allah and the right of servants, although it is observed in a general sense due to being hidden from them, so the right of Allah Almighty is not like that. If it is said: Covering does not conceal from Allah because He sees the covered as He sees the uncovered, it is answered that He sees the uncovered as abandoning etiquette and the covered as being polite, and this etiquette must be observed when capable. If he prays naked in water, if it is turbid, his prayer is valid; if it is clear such that his private parts can be seen, it is not valid. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and the image of prayer in water is prayer over a funeral, otherwise the depiction is not valid. The intention is that covering from others suffices, not from oneself, so if he sees his penis through his fly or it is such that he would see it if he looked, then it is valid according to the general scholars and this is correct, as in al-Muhit and others. However, in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: in the case, it is the adornment, and the place is intended, which is the covering; and in the second, it is the opposite, meaning the name of the place, which is the mosque, was used and the state, which is prayer, was intended. This is because covering is not obligatory for the very mosque, as evidenced by the permissibility of circumambulating naked. From this it is known that covering is for prayer, not for people, as in Mi'raj al-Diraya, because people in markets are more than in mosques; if it were for people, He would have said 'at every market'. And it is transmitted from his teacher, the scholar, that the first is of the type of using the name of the effect for the cause. He said: The garment is the cause of adornment and the place of adornment is the person. His saying: (Otherwise, the depiction is not valid). He said in al-Nahr: It is not valid in other than it because the distinction between clear and other indicates that he has a garment, because the one who lacks it is the same for clear and other, and in that case, he is not permitted to gesture for the fard. End quote. The scholar Shaykh Isma'il said: I have a reservation about both statements because it is possible to depict his bowing and prostrating in turbid water such that nothing of his body appears if he blocks his openings; indeed, what the diver does in rescuing a drowning person is more than that. His saying: (But in al-Siraj...). The reason for the exception is that his saying: 'He must button it' indicates obligation, and it is apparent from the mentioned hadith. Al-Burhan al-Halabi said in Sharh al-Munyah: Evidence supports it, and that is that covering became a condition for prayer itself, not for fear of seeing the private parts in it. And if it is such that if he looked he would see without effort, the condition of covering is not met, and therefore...
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a thorough exposition on the obligation of covering the 'awrah (private parts) in prayer. It opens by asserting that covering the 'awrah is fard (obligatory) based on consensus (ijma'), which is so firmly established that any later opposition (like that of some Malikis, e.g. Qadi Isma'il) is invalid. The proof is then supported by the Quranic verse (7:31) 'Take your adornment at every mosque' — interpreted as covering the private parts at every prayer — and by the hadith 'Allah does not accept the prayer of a menstruating woman except with a khimar (headcover).' The text explains that the headcover requirement applies only to mature women, and by istihsan a girl nearing puberty who prays without a headcover is not required to repeat, as the hadith specifically mentions 'menstruating' (which excludes pre-pubescent girls). A linguistic note explains the term 'awrah' from deficiency and ugliness. The text then covers several conditions and exceptional cases: (1) Covering with a silk garment renders the prayer valid but sinful, analogous to praying on usurped land; (2) The covering must be opaque such that what is underneath is not visible — a thin or transparent garment invalidates the prayer; (3) Privacy does not suffice: even if one prays naked in a dark room where no one sees, the prayer is invalid by consensus, because covering is a right of both Allah and people; the response to the objection that Allah sees anyway is a matter of etiquette (adab). (4) Praying naked in water: if the water is turbid, it is valid; if clear, it is not, because the 'awrah is visible. (5) Covering from others suffices; if one sees his own private parts from a hole or the like, the prayer is still valid according to the majority (al-ammah) and this is the correct view. A subtle point from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is then discussed: the phrase 'at every mosque' in the verse is a metonymy (majaz); the intended meaning is 'at every prayer', since covering is not required for the mosque itself (as shown by permissibility of naked tawaf). Further discussions include a critique by Shaykh Isma'il about the possibility of performing prayer in turbid water by gestures (ishara) that conceal the body, and the need to button the garment to ensure coverage. The passage concludes with the principle that covering is a condition for prayer itself, not merely to prevent observation by others.

Key Terms
عورة (awrah): Private parts that must be covered in prayer; for males generally the navel to knee; for females the entire body except face and hands. The text emphasizes covering from others and oneself.
خمار (khimār): A headcover worn by women; the hadith requires it for a menstruating woman (mature) to have her prayer accepted.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; used here to consider the prayer of a minor girl without headcover as valid, despite the general obligation, due to the weakness of the address for minors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a 10-year-old girl who has not yet menstruated and prays without a headcover?
A) Her prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) Her prayer is valid by istihsan and does not need repetition.
C) Her prayer is valid only if no one sees her.
D) She must cover her head because all females must cover in prayer.

Key Takeaway
Covering the 'awrah is fard in prayer by consensus and texts, but pre-pubescent girls are excused from headcovering by juristic preference (istihsan).
